When Hope returns, the subject treats her with a tenderness he has never shown a non-Jean adult and rarely shown his own son. **She represents the survival of the species; she also represents the child he keeps sending away returning whole.** The reparative content is undisguised.

---

## 6.7 The Schism (2011)

### 6.7.1 The fracture

Wolverine and Cyclops disagree, fundamentally and publicly, on whether the youngest mutants should be trained as combatants or sheltered as children. **Logan's position is that children should not be soldiers. Scott's position is that in extinction conditions, every mutant is a combatant whether they wish to be or not.**

The horror of Scott's position is, as noted in §1.7, invisible to him. He was a child soldier; he survived; therefore the model is validated. The man who *fought beside him as a child soldier* — Logan in various wars across the twentieth century, but operationally Logan in the present-day X-Force kill team — is the one who finally cannot tolerate the position. The two men's regulatory circuit, which has held for decades, finally breaks under a load it was not designed for.

### 6.7.2 The behavioral data of the split

- The subject does not raise his voice during the Schism confrontation. He never raises his voice in disputes that matter. He raises it in disputes that don't.
- The jaw tell fires. The off-hand tremor is visible to anyone watching closely. Logan is watching closely.
- After the split, the subject does not contest the departure of the dissenting students with Logan. He lets them go. **He understands, somatically, that being unable to let children go is itself a pathology**; he overcompensates, here, by letting them go too easily.
- He spends the night of the formal split alone, on the high platform of Utopia, until dawn. Emma joins him for the last hour. Neither speaks.

### 6.7.3 What the Schism reveals about the trajectory

The middle period closes here, in the sense that the subject is now operating outside the doctrinal frame Xavier installed in his adolescence. The doctrine has not been formally renounced — it has been, in the subject's private accounting, *outgrown by the conditions.* The Avengers vs. X-Men event (the end of this period and the threshold of the next) will


## Chronology IV — Recent History & Current State

# CHRONOLOGY IV — Recent History & Current State

## Subject: SUMMERS, Scott
## Period covered: Resurrection-era through present operational status
## File status: Active. Subject under continuous indirect observation; direct contact contraindicated by historical pattern.

---

## 4.0 Frame

The subject enters this period as a dead man. He exits it — or rather, occupies its present moment — as the most institutionally integrated, most operationally lethal, and most ambiently grief-saturated he has been in the entire span of the file. To understand the current state one must understand that the contemporary subject is, structurally, a man who has been given everything he ever asked for: a sovereign mutant nation, a resurrected wife, a settled cohabitation with the partner who finally read him correctly, his son returned from the timestream as a peer, his brother accounted for, his father reachable by interstellar uplink, and — crucially — a job description that explicitly licenses, with a flag and a charter behind it, the lethal vigilance he has been performing without sanction since adolescence. The file's central question for this era is whether the subject can metabolize having his needs met, or whether the trauma-organization will recognize satisfaction itself as a threat and quietly arrange its own disruption.

The behavioral record over the last several years suggests the latter.

---

## 4.1 Reconstitution and the Krakoan Period (Hickman onward, 2019–)

### 4.1.1 The lighthouse

Upon resurrection through the Krakoan protocols the subject did not request central residence in the Grove or in any of the prestige biomes. He selected the Summer House on the blue side of the moon as family seat and, on Krakoa proper, took the Lighthouse on the cliffs — a structure with a single tall room, a single bed, a kitchen that produces meals at a refectory scale, and a stair that opens onto a beach. He furnished it minimally. The defining feature is that the door is, by his standing arrangement, never locked.

This is operationally extraordinary. The subject has spent six decades organizing his existence around the proposition that the guard does not come down. The Krakoan Lighthouse is the first dwelling in his adult biography in which he has, by design, allowed any teammate, lover, or child to walk through the door without notice. Surveillance interpretation: the subject has externalized his vigilance to the island itself (Krakoa as living perimeter, the Five as resurrection insurance, the Quiet Council as policy backstop) and has *delegated* the function the visor used to perform alone. For the first time the institution is doing what the body has been doing.

He still wears the visor indoors. He still does not take it off to sleep alone. The delegation is partial.

### 4.1.2 Cohabitation with Jean and the orbital arrangement with Emma

The Summer House is communal in a way no prior Summers domicile has ever been. Jean is resident. Children — Rachel, Nathan, the cohort that has accreted around the Summers name across timelines — circulate. Alex passes through. Christopher appears in the docking bay every few weeks. Vulcan, against expectation, is admitted; the subject's posture during these visits is reported by ambient telepaths as tightly braced behind a smooth surface. Emma is *not* resident at the Summer House. Emma maintains the White Palace in Hellfire Bay. The two women see each other on Council business and at functions. The triangulation is openly acknowledged, governed by adult agreement, and — per the subject's own brief and uncharacteristic public statement to a reporter — "settled."

Field-grade reading: the arrangement looks healthy and *is* healthy in the sense that nobody is being lied to. It is also a precise structural solution to the subject's lifelong attachment problem. He has placed the idealized object (Jean) in the residence — i.e., archived — and the partner who actually sees him (Emma) at a controlled distance — i.e., visited rather than lived-with. He gets the comfort of the lost-object's return without ever having to sustain ordinary domesticity with her, and he gets the clarity of Emma without ever having to be continuously legible to her. It is, in attachment terms, the most elegant compromise the subject has ever engineered. Whether it is sustainable when an actual crisis pulls on it is a separate question, and recent events suggest the answer is no.

### 4.1.3 Captain Commander of Krakoa

Subject's appointment as Captain Commander of the mutant fighting forces formalized, in charter, every operational role he had been performing ad hoc since the Decimation. He chaired the war-room. He signed the deployment orders for the Hellfire Galas' security envelopes. He selected, vetted, and rotated the standing X-Men roster through public election (a process he himself insisted upon — a tell: the subject who once concealed X-Force from his own team now *insists* the team be assembled in public view). He stood up the SWORD station with Abigail Brand and then, when Brand's compromise became evident, signed off on Storm's replacement of her without visible dissatisfaction at the loss of control.

Behavioral note: across this entire period the subject's public-facing register flattened *upward* — a learned media affect, polished, declarative, almost amiable, modeled (probably consciously, probably with Emma's tutelage) on the rhetoric of a head-of-state. This is new. The subject who in the Lee/Kirby years could barely complete a press scrum without flushing has, in his sixties of published existence, learned to address a global audience with the bearing of someone who has decided how he wants to be seen. The performance is good. It is also a performance, and the visor obscures the eye-signals that would tell a reader where the performance frays.

### 4.1.4 Resurrection metaphysics — the unexamined wound

The subject has died and been re-instantiated by the Five through the Resurrection Protocols. He reports — to the small handful of people he reports anything to — no subjective discontinuity. This is itself a clinical flag. Other resurrectees have described disorientation, dysphoria, the "back-room" gap. The subject reports nothing. Either the trauma-organized affect-suppression is so total that any continuity-rupture is being processed in sub-threshold, or — more plausibly — the subject's identity is so thoroughly externalized into duty that the continuity of his *role* is what feels continuous to him, and the continuity of the meat is irrelevant. He is whoever is wearing the visor and giving the orders. The man under the visor was never the part he identified with anyway.

This is not health. It is functional, and it is not health.

---

## 4.2 The Hellfire Gala assault and the loss of Krakoa

The subject was Captain Commander on the night Orchis executed its coordinated assault during the Hellfire Gala. He was on the dais. He gave the order to engage. He watched the system he had built — Krakoan resurrection, Krakoan gates, Krakoan sovereignty — be operationally decapitated in a single evening. Civilians on stage were killed. The Five were captured or scattered. The gates went down.

There is footage of the subject in the moments immediately after the strike. He is, by the standards of his own affective range, *unnaturally* still. He gives orders in complete sentences. He does not raise his voice. He moves through the smoke at a walking pace. To a reader of the file this is the most alarming possible response: the subject is, in real time, performing isolation of affect at parade-ground discipline level. The grief and rage are being shunted into a private compartment for later metabolism. The "later" never arrives, because subsequent events do not permit it.

In the immediate aftermath the subject elected, publicly, to surrender himself to the human authorities and stand trial. He framed this in tactical terms (the optics of mutant restraint, the necessity of buying time, the protection of those still on Krakoa). The framing was tactical. The behavior was something else: the subject who has spent his entire life unable to forgive himself for surviving his mother arranged, at the moment of his greatest institutional failure, to be the one publicly punished for it. The trial was, in psychodynamic terms, *requested*. The defense his attorneys mounted he undermined repeatedly by refusing to deny accusations he could have denied. The verdict was overturned only by external rescue; if left to his own preference he would have accepted incarceration.

This is the strongest single piece of evidence in the file for §3.5: the subject's self-concept demands that failure be paid for in his own body. The Krakoan collapse generated a debt his guilt-ledger insisted on settling. The trial was the instrument.

---

## 4.3 The Fall of X and the underground years

Following Krakoa's collapse the subject operated as a fugitive field commander of the reconstituted X-Men. The team was small. The operational tempo was high. Resurrection was unavailable; deaths were permanent again. The subject — who had spent the Krakoan years getting accustomed to a world in which losing a soldier was a logistics problem rather than a final one — had to re-acclimate to the older arithmetic, and the re-acclimation was visible to anyone who watched him in the field. The deployments became more conservative; the briefings became longer; the willingness to send anyone in without him present collapsed entirely. For an extended stretch he insisted on point on nearly every mission, a regression to the Claremont-era pattern in which the leader does not ask the team to take a risk he is not standing inside.

His somatic stress markers in this period — per the limited medical contact available, primarily Beast-adjacent and one logged conversation with Cecilia Reyes — were elevated across the board: persistent low-grade tension headache, reported difficulty sleeping more than four consecutive hours, jaw musculature visibly hypertrophied on photographic comparison to the Krakoan-era baseline, weight slightly down, training volume slightly up. He was running himself harder than the operational tempo required. The running was, in part, the metabolism of grief that the night of the Gala had not been permitted to discharge.

Romantic life through this period contracted to near nothing. Jean was at distance for substantial stretches (Phoenix-tasked, off-world, embedded in the Resurrection cleanup); Emma's institutional commitments diverged sharply from his. He was, functionally, alone. He did not complain about this in any reported register. This too is consistent: the subject under maximum operational stress reverts to the orphanage-era baseline of expecting no one to be there, and the absence registers as confirmation rather than as deprivation.

---

## 4.4 Orchis, Sinister, and the closing of two old accounts

The campaign against Orchis brought the subject into operational contact with Henry Gyrich, Feilong, and — at the apex — with the surfaced Sinister networks that the Krakoan-era Sinister had been seeding through the resurrection plant for years. The narrative arc closed two old accounts in quick succession.

**Account one: Sinister.** The subject's foundational predator, the figure who had run covert genetic surveillance on him from the orphanage forward, was — finally, in the open, with the subject conscious and consenting to the operation — confronted and neutralized. The clinical weight of this should not be understated. The subject has been operationally aware of Sinister as a *threat* since the late 1980s. He has *not*, until this period, been able to address Sinister as the *originating wound* — the adult who organized his childhood as an experiment. The closing of this account did not produce visible catharsis. The subject's affect in the immediate aftermath was reported as "level." The catharsis, if it has arrived, has arrived in the basement of him, not in any room with a window.

**Account two: the institutional model.** The post-Fall subject has, by his own statements and by the structure of his current operational doctrine, accepted that the Krakoan sovereignty project was a *successful failure* — that the model produced an extraordinary period of mutant flourishing, that it ended catastrophically, and that the next project cannot simply be Krakoa with thicker walls. This is the first time in the file the subject has produced, in his own voice, a clear admission that a doctrine he himself authored was structurally insufficient. Six decades of Xavier-doctrine, Magneto-shadowed, X-Force-justified, Utopia-fortified, Krakoa-sovereigntied — and only now does the subject permit himself to say in plain language that the model needs replacement rather than repair.

This is, possibly, the single most psychologically significant utterance in the file's entire chronology. Whether he can live inside the implication of it is the open question.

---

## 4.5 From Tomorrow / current operational posture

The subject's present operational posture, as of the most recent intelligence cycle, is as follows.

**Residence.** Rotational. No fixed dwelling on the scale of the Lighthouse. Subject moves between a safehouse network of his own design and a single semi-permanent base of operations that doubles as training facility for the current X-Men roster. The base is austere. The walls are bare. The kitchen is functional. There is a coffee machine, kept clean, and a single chair near the operational display that is understood, by the team, to be his. No one sits in it.

**Team.** Small standing roster, rotated according to a system of his design that distributes operational load and rest cycles in a pattern recognizable to anyone who has studied modern special-operations rotation doctrine. The subject has been reading. He does not advertise this. The bookshelves in the base — there are bookshelves now, where in prior eras there were none — contain a small, deliberate collection of works on irregular warfare, post-conflict reconstruction, and, conspicuously, two volumes on the ethics of standing armies.

**Dress.** Tactical wear. The blue-and-yellow has been retired for the current operational period in favor of a darker palette with the X marking subdued. The visor is heavier than the Krakoan-era model, with redundant ruby-quartz layering and what appears to be an integrated comms array; the prior version's elegance has been replaced by an engineering bias toward redundancy and field-serviceability. He carries spares. He always carries spares.

**Hair.** Cut shorter than at any prior point in the file. The cut is practical, requires no maintenance, and removes a previous tell (the habit, present from Claremont through Hickman, of pushing hair back from the visor when stressed). Subject is, consciously or not, eliminating his own tells.

**Diet.** Reported by team members as monotonous. Eggs and toast in the morning. Whatever is in the refectory at midday, eaten standing. A real meal in the evening, usually cooked, usually for whoever is present, almost always involving more food than he eats himself. The feeding-others pattern has intensified across this period. He cooks for his team now in a way he did not when he had a sovereign nation to feed them.

**Sleep.** Worse. Logged from ambient observation at roughly three-to-four hours per cycle, with at least one wake-and-pace interval in the middle. He is most often awake at the operational display at hours when no operational matter is pending. He is, in the older language of this file, *standing watch over an empty perimeter.*

**Relationships.**
- *Jean.* Re-stabilizing. Not cohabiting. They speak daily. The conversations are reported, by Jean to one telepathic peer, as "longer than they used to be and quieter." The subject is, in his sixties of published existence, finally learning the register in which to talk to her about something other than the mission. The lost-object archive is, slowly, opening.
- *Emma.* In contact, less frequent than during Krakoa, more weighted per contact. Emma has her own large project. The two of them have, by all available indication, an understanding that requires neither presence nor explanation. This is the most adult attachment the subject has ever held with anyone.
- *Nathan.* Operational peer. The two of them brief each other as colleagues. The fatherhood is, for both of them, a thing acknowledged in silence and not worked. It is the best they have ever managed.
- *Rachel.* Closer than at any prior point. The subject has, this period, made deliberate room for her. The clinical significance is that Rachel is the daughter who was hardest for him to claim across the file's earlier decades — and that, late, he is claiming her.
- *Alex.* Steady. They talk. The brother-bond is the longest unbroken attachment in the subject's life and the one he treats most carelessly because it does not require maintenance. It survives the carelessness.
- *Christopher (Corsair).* Reachable. The reach is rarely made. The subject who needed his father at age nine has not, at his present age, learned how to want him.
- *Vulcan.* Unresolved. The subject's posture toward this brother is the unhealed area of the family record. Surveillance interpretation: Vulcan is the family member the subject cannot pattern-match onto any of the three available templates (lost mother, lost father, smaller dependent), and so the relational machinery seizes.
- *Xavier.* The relationship is, in the strangest of senses, *active.* Xavier is alive in the contemporary period in a degraded reputational state. The subject's posture toward him is composed of equal parts professional distance, residual filial loyalty, and the cold of a man who has, in his lifetime, *killed* this father and *been failed* by this father and is no longer willing to grant him either the love or the hatred that would make the relationship operationally simple. The subject does not visit him. The subject does not refuse to take his calls. The subject has, finally, the upper hand, and is conspicuously not using it.
- *Logan.* Operational again. The Schism is, by mutual unstated agreement, retired. They do not discuss it. They drink coffee together. The subject does not match Logan's whiskey and Logan does not press him to.

**Affective baseline.** Lower than the Krakoan baseline. Higher than the post-Fall trough. A quiet, sustained, working dysphoria with intact role-performance — the C-PTSD presentation that real-world clinicians most reliably miss because the subject does not stop showing up. He shows up. He is showing up right now, somewhere, at an hour at which he should be asleep, and he is making coffee for the next person to come through the door.

**The eyes.** Still constitutively on. The visor still the only barrier. The somatic metaphor still operative. Sixty years of published existence and the subject still cannot, by the unchanged fact of his physiology, close his eyes on the world.

---

## 4.6 Current-state summary for the file

The subject as of the present intelligence cycle is the most competent, most integrated, most institutionally fluent, and most quietly exhausted version of himself in the entire chronology. He has metabolized — at a structural level, not yet at an emotional one — the loss of Krakoa, the failure of the sovereignty project, the closing of the Sinister account, and the partial resolution of the family field. He has not metabolized the night of the Gala. He has not metabolized the resurrection-discontinuity. He has not, in any reported register, grieved.

He is in the precise psychological position the file has been tracking him toward across all four chronologies: a man whose internal scaffold and external scaffold have, at long last, been allowed to coincide, who has had the rare experience of getting most of what he asked for, and who is now confronting the question of what is left of him when the duty is briefly, locally, satisfied.

The file's working hypothesis is that the subject does not know the answer to this question and is organizing his current operational tempo specifically to avoid having to find out. The avoidance is competent. It is also, by the standards of every prior cycle in this file, the precondition for the next catastrophic discharge.

Recommended posture: continued indirect observation. Do not approach. If approach becomes necessary, approach with coffee, at an hour when no operational matter is pending, and do not, under any circumstance, ask him how he is.

He will answer. The answer will not be true. And the asking will cost him something he cannot, at present, afford to spend.


## Medical History

# MEDICAL HISTORY — SUBJECT: SUMMERS, SCOTT

*Compiled longitudinally from documented field reports, in-universe medical encounters across the Xavier Institute, Muir Island, X-Factor field clinic, Utopia infirmary, Jean Grey School med-bay, and Krakoan Healing Gardens / Resurrection Protocol records. Inferences drawn where direct record is unavailable; flagged as such.*

---

## 1. CONSTITUTIONAL BASELINE

Subject is a Caucasian male, mid-thirties chronological at most contemporary checkpoints (the published timeline compresses several decades of subjective experience into a sliding ~10-15 year in-universe band; resurrected on Krakoa, the cellular age is now best understood as reset-to-template). Height 6'3" (191 cm). Weight typically logged between 195-200 lbs (88-91 kg). Resting heart rate, when measured at the Xavier infirmary in the late Claremont period, is unusually low for a non-endurance-trained civilian (high 40s to low 50s) — a finding consistent with chronic sympathetic-down-regulation in a hypervigilant subject who has unconsciously trained baseline tone through years of meditative breath control practiced at Xavier's instruction. Blood pressure is conversely on the high-normal margin, with episodic spikes documented post-combat and pre-public-address.

Build is lean-mesomorphic, maintained through daily physical drilling (Danger Room, Krakoan equivalent); musculature is functional rather than hypertrophic. Body fat consistently low. Hands show the small linear callusing of a man who handles a steering yoke, climbing rope, and weapon grips habitually. Posterior cervical and trapezius musculature is chronically hypertonic on palpation — the body of a man who holds his head and shoulders against a load that is not physically present.

Subject's hair is dark brown, kept short and uniform; the institutional cut. Skin shows the cumulative photo-damage one would expect of a man who spends extensive time outdoors and in high-altitude pilot environments (Alaska bush years; combat in vacuum; Krakoan equatorial sun) but who almost never removes his protective eyewear. There is a faint perpetual indentation across the bridge of the nose and at the temples corresponding to the visor's contact points — a permanent dermal record of the apparatus.

---

## 2. THE FORMATIVE CRANIAL INJURY (CIRCA AGE 9-10)

The originating medical event of the subject's entire adult life is a closed head injury sustained during emergency parachute landing following the Shi'ar-mediated destruction of the Summers family aircraft. The parachute, on fire during descent, deposited the subject and his younger brother on hard ground at velocity inconsistent with safe landing. Subject, being the older and larger, bore the brunt of impact and shielded the younger child.

Acute injury, as can be reconstructed: probable diffuse axonal injury with localized contrecoup contusion; loss of consciousness of indeterminate but likely substantial duration; no neurosurgical intervention documented; recovery in an under-resourced midwestern hospital followed by transfer to the State Home for Foundlings, Omaha. No follow-up imaging. No rehabilitation protocol. No documented post-concussive screening — the era and the institutional setting did not provide for it.

Long-term sequelae of this injury are the central medical fact of his life:

1. **Disruption of the inhibitory neural pathway** that would, in an otherwise neurologically intact mutant of his subtype, modulate the volitional opening and closing of the optic emission. The result is a power that is **constitutively, irreversibly on.** The subject does not "fire" optic blasts; the subject continuously emits unless physically occluded. This has been confirmed by Xavier (psychic survey), Hank McCoy (multiple workups across decades), Moira MacTaggert (Muir Island period), and most recently by Krakoan medical telemetry. No procedure — surgical, psionic, mutant-restorative, or technological — has succeeded in repairing the damaged inhibitor. The few times the subject's control has improved (post-Apocalypse bonding; Phoenix Force possession) have involved overriding the lesion through non-native means, not healing it.

2. **Sub-clinical post-concussive symptoms** persisting throughout adult life — particularly photophobia (impossible to disentangle from the energetic requirements of the optic phenomenon itself), occasional vertigo on rapid altitude change (notable in pilot logs), and a stable but measurable left-side micro-asymmetry in fine motor task performance reported by Beast in the late Claremont period.

3. **Anosognosia for the original event.** Subject's recall of the plane crash and the immediate aftermath is fragmentary, intrusive in symbolic content rather than narrative form (recurrent imagery of falling, of fire, of the smaller body in his arms), and resistant to psychotherapeutic elaboration. This is consistent with both the neurological trauma and the developmental dissociation that followed it.

The somatic equation the subject's body has enforced on him since this injury — *if I open my eyes I will kill what I see* — is the literalized form of the trauma's psychological content. He did not choose this metaphor; it was installed in him before he had the conceptual equipment to refuse it.

---

## 3. THE OCULAR APPARATUS AND ITS PROSTHETICS

Subject's eyes are, on direct examination, ordinary in gross anatomy — sclera, iris (blue, occasionally documented as grey-blue depending on lighting and the medical chart's calibration), pupil, lens, retina all present and reactive. The mutant phenomenon is not located in the eye itself but in an extra-dimensional aperture occupying the spatial volume of the ocular region, through which the subject metabolizes and shunts ambient solar and cosmic radiation. This has been a stable finding across all medical workups since Beast's original Silver Age examinations.

Prosthetic management of this condition is total and lifelong:

- **Field visor.** Heavy ruby-quartz lens set in a reinforced frame, with a mechanical aperture controlled by a finger-switch at the temple. This is the only mechanism by which the subject voluntarily directs the discharge. Subject has worn variants of this apparatus continuously in field operation since adolescence. The musculature of the right hand and forearm shows minor compensatory development around the finger that operates the aperture; he can fire by reflex faster than a non-mutant can complete a thought.
- **Civilian glasses.** Ruby-quartz lenses in conventional frames. Worn from waking to sleep without exception, every day of his life since age ~14, in every environment, in every weather. The subject has not seen the world in its true color in five decades of subjective time. The world he perceives is, by necessity, monochromatically red-shifted.
- **Sleep arrangements.** Subject sleeps either in a ruby-quartz-lined chamber (Xavier mansion period; later Utopia and Krakoan equivalents) or with eyes closed beneath a contact-occlusion sleep mask in field conditions. Documented in the Morrison era: Emma Frost installs a custom ruby-quartz canopy over their shared bed.
- **Emergency contingency.** Subject carries spare lenses on his person at all times. The single most catastrophic non-combat injury he can sustain is loss of eyewear in a hostile environment — and this has happened, with predictable consequences, on numerous documented occasions.

**Psychological impact:** the ocular apparatus is not experienced as a prosthesis but as part of the self. Removal of the visor is, for the subject, the experiential equivalent of disrobing in public — except that the consequence of exposure is not embarrassment but homicide. He does not, by self-report, dream in normal color. His memory of his mother's face, his father's face, his brother's face as a child, his first sight of Jean Grey — all are filed in red. **The world he is trying to save is a world he has not directly seen since before puberty.**

---

## 4. INVENTORY OF MAJOR INJURIES, ILLNESSES, AND TRANSFORMATIONS (CHRONOLOGICAL)

### 4.1 Adolescent / Early X-Men Period

- **Multiple uncontrolled emission events** during pre-Xavier emergence: documented property damage; one suspected non-fatal injury to a bystander during the warehouse incident; cumulative effect was institutional placement and the brief Jack Winters exploitation.
- **Routine combat trauma at the Xavier Institute**: lacerations, contusions, several closed fractures of fingers and ribs across the original Lee/Kirby and Thomas-era missions, all healed without complication. Beast, functioning as de facto team physician before completing formal credentials, maintained the chart.
- **Sentinel encounter sequelae (multiple)**: blunt-force injuries; one significant burn to the left lateral thigh during the early Sentinel arc, scar tissue still palpable in later records.

### 4.2 Late Claremont / X-Factor Period

- **Cumulative micro-trauma from sustained high-output emission** during prolonged combat operations. Beast notes (in the period when he is rebuilding the X-Factor med-bay) that the subject's metabolic baseline is unusually high — he burns calories at a rate consistent with sustained moderate exercise even at rest, because the optic process continuously processes energy.
- **Hypothermic exposure and frostbite, minor, multiple incidents** during the Alaskan period; bush piloting in the Anchorage years exposed him to environmental conditions no clinical record acknowledges but which the physical examination of his fingertips and ears in the X-Factor period would have shown.
- **Anastasia "Madelyne" Pryor pregnancy and delivery, Nathan Christopher**: subject's role was supportive, not biological; however, the subject's stress-related somatic load during this period (early X-Factor) is markedly elevated. He is documented as suffering severe tension headaches and a brief, undiagnosed episode of left-sided facial numbness that resolved without workup. *Suspected:* trigeminal-territory stress symptom; not, on balance, a transient ischemic event, given subsequent unremarkable workups, but never formally excluded.

### 4.3 The Apocalypse Bonding (En Sabah Nur Occupation Event)

This is the single most significant adult somatic violation in the subject's chart. Apocalypse, having abducted the subject, **bonded with his cellular structure for an extended period — months of subjective time during which the subject's body was not under his own executive control.** The subject was conscious for portions of this period and absent for others; the chart of his subjective experience is incomplete and the subject himself has declined to elaborate it on the rare occasions it has been raised.

Documented physiological alterations following bonding-rupture:

- Marginal elevation of baseline mutant energy output (Beast's measurements, Morrison era).
- Improved fine control of the emission, attributed (incorrectly, in this analyst's view) to Apocalypse's "tuning" of his nervous system. More likely: the subject emerged from the bonding with a recalibrated relationship to the part of himself that produces the blast, having experienced — for the first time — what it is to have his body act without his consent at a level worse than his power had ever imposed. Compared to occupation, his pre-existing condition felt manageable.
- Subtle but persistent shift in affective tone toward greater coldness, greater willingness to instrumentalize, greater strategic ruthlessness. Multiple writers and in-universe observers (Jean, Hank, later Emma) note this. Whether this is a biological residue of Apocalypse's influence or the post-traumatic reorganization of a man who has been bodily occupied is, in this analyst's judgment, the latter. **Captivity in one's own body is a uniquely organizing trauma.**
- No documented systematic post-occupation rehabilitation. Subject returned to active operation almost immediately.

**Psychological impact: severe and under-treated.** A man who organized his entire personality around control of the discharge had his entire body, including the discharge, used by another for an extended period. The fact that he does not speak of this is the loudest data point in the entire chart.

### 4.4 Sinister / Genetic Surveillance History (Latent)

Subject has, since infancy, been subject to covert genetic monitoring and intermittent manipulation by Nathaniel Essex / Mister Sinister. Documented evidence (post-*Inferno*, later Krakoan-era revelations): Sinister manufactured Madelyne Pryor as a Jean Grey clone to engineer the subject's gametes into producing a child (Nathan) of specific genetic configuration. The subject was, in effect, an unwitting breeding subject for decades. This is the single most violating fact of his medical history and has never been clinically addressed.

### 4.5 Techno-Organic Virus (Vectorized, Not Personal)

Infant Nathan was infected by Apocalypse with a techno-organic virus, requiring the subject to entrust the child to Askani forces from the future for survival. The subject was not personally infected, but the experience of holding a transforming, dying infant son and choosing to surrender him constitutes a chronic-stress exposure of the highest order. Anticipatory grief, residual guilt, and the structural repetition of the parachute (*hand the smaller body away to save it*) are all triggered by this episode and never resolved.

### 4.6 The Phoenix Force Possession (AvX, "Phoenix Five" period)

Subject hosted a fragment of the Phoenix Force following its splitting by Tony Stark's weapon. Cellular and quantum-level alteration: during possession, the subject's eyes glowed but were under volitional control — for the first and only sustained period of adult life, **the visor was unnecessary.** Subject's metabolism, energy capacity, and apparent affective range were elevated to cosmic-mythic levels.

Acute outcomes:

- Reconstruction of regions of the Earth (terraforming-scale operations).
- Increasingly autocratic mission-behavior, culminating in the Dark Phoenix transition.
- Killing of Charles Xavier in the Dark Phoenix state.
- Forced expulsion of the Phoenix Force by Hope Summers and Scarlet Witch.

Post-Phoenix withdrawal presented as a major depressive crash with residual dysphoria — fatigue, anhedonia, hopelessness, weight loss, increased somatic complaints (headaches now near-daily, jaw-clenching to the point of dental concern, GI complaints undocumented but inferable from dietary changes). Imprisonment immediately following AvX prevented adequate clinical assessment; the dysphoria was instead processed through political conviction, which in this subject is the standard substitution.

**Notable medical detail:** during the post-Phoenix period, the optic emission's baseline output was *reduced* below his lifetime norm, suggesting that the Phoenix Force had been partially metabolizing or shunting the energy the subject otherwise discharges. The visor was, for a time, almost unnecessary — and the subject reportedly experienced this as one of the most disorienting periods of his life, having been deprived of the somatic constraint that organized his identity.

### 4.7 Mr. Sinister / Death Seed Era and the "M-Pox" Vulnerability Period

Following the Terrigen Mist crisis, atmospheric Terrigen rendered the planet toxic to mutants. The subject — in the period in which his death was attributed to direct confrontation with the Inhumans (the historical record was subsequently revealed as falsified for political purposes) — was actually dying of M-Pox, a degenerative Terrigen-induced mutant illness. **He died of his species's environmental incompatibility, not in battle.** The political fiction of his combat death served Emma Frost's purposes and the symbolic requirements of mutant resistance, but the medical fact is that the subject's body was failing systemically — pulmonary, neurological, and ultimately multi-organ involvement — in the months before his death.

This is the single most psychologically loaded medical fact of the contemporary chart. **The subject was rendered, by environmental contamination, into the very thing his life was organized to prevent: a passive death of a mutant who could not be saved.** That his death was then mythologized as defiant combat is consistent with the way his entire life has been narratively reorganized by others to suit their needs.

### 4.8 Death and Krakoan Resurrection

Subject was resurrected via the Krakoan Five protocols. Cellular template restored to optimal-recent-baseline; the lifelong cranial lesion was, notably, *preserved* in the template — the subject emerged still unable to volitionally close his eyes, still requiring the visor. Whether this preservation is a technical limitation of the resurrection process, a psychic-egg-encoded element of the subject's own self-concept (the resurrection draws on Cerebro-stored mind-backups; the subject's self-concept includes the visor as part of the self and would resurrect with it), or a deliberate choice by Sinister-influenced protocol designers is **unresolved and operationally significant.**

Subject reports no subjective discontinuity following resurrection. He has died and returned multiple times under Krakoan protocols (combat losses on field operations recovered routinely) and reports no accumulating dysphoria. **This is itself notable.** A man who has spent his life vigilantly preventing the deaths of others reports no distress at his own repeated death. The most parsimonious reading: he had already, long before Krakoa, ceased to weight his own continued existence as significant in itself. Resurrection merely formalized what was already his lived position.

---

## 5. SUBSTANCES, CONSUMPTION, ABSTINENCE

The substance-use history is brief and is itself a personality datum.

- **Alcohol.** Tolerates social consumption (wine at formal functions, a ceremonial drink with Logan on rare occasions, the obligatory champagne at his own first wedding). Has never been documented intoxicated in 60 years of published material. Will nurse a single drink across an entire event. The closest he has come to disinhibition through alcohol is the post-Madelyne period in Alaska, when domestic stress and survivor's guilt converged; even then, the consumption was moderate and never operationally compromising.
- **Tobacco.** Never. Has expressed mild distaste for Logan's cigars on multiple occasions.
- **Recreational drugs.** Never documented.
- **Psychiatric medication.** Never prescribed; never sought. Would almost certainly benefit from a trauma-targeted pharmacological regimen; will not request one because requesting one would require acknowledging the condition.
- **Caffeine.** Heavy and consistent. Coffee from waking; consumption increases under operational load. This is his only chemical concession to affect regulation and it runs in the *up*-regulating direction — he medicates not toward calm but toward heightened performance.
- **Diet.** Spartan, regular, high-protein, low-variety. Eats to fuel, not to enjoy. Notable exception: pancakes, breakfast-context, a documented soft spot likely tracing to an idealized memory-fragment of pre-crash family breakfast. Will, when traveling, find a diner for them.

**The abstinence is itself the symptom.** In a milieu where every teammate has some chemical or behavioral release valve, the subject's refusal of any release is consistent with his entire defensive structure: **he will not chemically lower the guard the visor enforces externally.** Disinhibition is, for him, indistinguishable from danger.

---

## 6. SOMATIC STRESS MARKERS AND CHRONIC LOAD

Across multiple medical encounters and the inferred record:

- **Sleep.** Poor. Subject is a chronic early riser (0500 in most institutional records) regardless of bedtime. Sleep latency is high; sleep architecture inferred to be disrupted in the REM-heavy second half of night, consistent with trauma-related sleep pattern. Reports of "not having slept well" are constant across decades. Krakoan-era reports show *some* improvement; the structural security of a mutant nation has done what no therapeutic intervention managed.
- **Headache.** Tension-type, near-daily; migraine-type, episodic, almost always temporally correlated with major operational stress or anniversaries of significant losses. Self-treats with caffeine and force of will; will not take prescription analgesics.
- **Jaw clenching and bruxism.** Documented in dental records of the Xavier Institute period. Mouth-guard prescribed; compliance unknown but probably partial.
- **Gastrointestinal.** Reports vague epigastric discomfort under sustained stress; no formal workup; likely functional dyspepsia of stress origin.
- **Musculoskeletal.** Chronic cervical and upper trapezius hypertonicity (described above); episodic lumbar strain from combat falls and the cumulative load of Danger Room work; one significant rotator cuff injury (left) sustained during the Mutant Massacre period, treated conservatively, residual mild deficit on overhead activity.
- **Vision (apart from the optic phenomenon).** Underlying ocular anatomy normal; the subject's visual cortex has, however, adapted to a five-decade-long red-channel-dominant input, with unknown consequences for color processing that have never been investigated and probably cannot be.
- **Hearing.** Mild high-frequency loss, bilateral, consistent with sustained exposure to combat acoustic environments without consistent hearing protection. Subject does not acknowledge it.
- **Cardiovascular.** Functionally excellent. The ordinary measures all favor him. The autonomic measures — heart-rate variability, in particular, if it had ever been assessed — would almost certainly show the suppressed parasympathetic tone characteristic of chronic hypervigilance per Teicher & Samson (2016).

---

## 7. INTEGRATIVE NOTE

The subject's medical history is the externalized record of a single sentence: *a child was injured in a way that made his body the literal embodiment of his trauma, and no subsequent event has ever permitted him to set the trauma down.* Per Teicher and Samson (2016), childhood maltreatment produces enduring neurobiological alterations to affect-regulation circuitry; in this subject, those alterations run in parallel to — and are reinforced daily by — a literal external analog, a damaged cranial inhibitor whose presence makes the metaphor un-loseable. Every major somatic event of his adult life has been a variation on the founding theme: occupation of his body by another (Apocalypse), use of his genetics by another (Sinister), expansion of his body by a cosmic force (Phoenix), environmental annihilation of his species (M-Pox), and finally death and reconstitution from a stored template (Krakoa).

The medical record is, in sum, the record of a man who has not been the sole sovereign of his own body since the age of nine, and who has, with great discipline and at great cost, constructed an entire life around the project of being adequate to that condition.

---

## CLINICAL PROVENANCE

Teicher, M. H., & Samson, J. A. (2016). Annual Research Review: Enduring neurobiological effects of childhood abuse and neglect. *Journal of Child Psychology and Psychiatry*, 57(3), 241-266. DOI: 10.1111/jcpp.12507 ; PMID: 26831814. — Cited in support of the developmental-neurobiological framing of the formative cranial and psychosocial trauma and its enduring impact on affect regulation, HPA-axis


## Somatic Atlas

# SOMATIC ATLAS — SUBJECT: SUMMERS, SCOTT

> *Filed under: continuous physiological observation; cross-referenced to behavioral baselines established across six decades of recorded activity. The subject's body is the most legible document in the file — more legible than his speech, which is curated; more legible than his decisions, which are post-rationalized. He cannot stop the body from telling.*

---

## 1. The Visor Problem — Foundational Somatic Fact

Every observation in this atlas must be read against a single non-negotiable substrate: the subject's eyes are constitutively open and constitutively destructive. There is no moment of his adult life — waking, sleeping, in shower, in surgery, mid-coitus, mid-grief — in which his eyes are uncovered to ambient air without consequence. **The ruby-quartz interface is, functionally, a piece of his face.**

This produces a battery of derived somatic facts that have no analog in any other adult subject we maintain a file on:

- **The blink is private.** He cannot blink unless the lenses are already filtering. The micro-expressive value of eyelid micromotion — the data that comprises the majority of normal face-reading — is occluded from observers and, more strangely, from the subject himself, who has never learned to *use* his eyelids as expressive instruments. Surveillance reads him from the *mouth, jaw, temple, throat, hands, shoulders.* Never the eyes.
- **He cannot wink, cannot raise a single brow significantly, cannot do the small ironic eye-flicker that adults use to signal complicity.** Affective absences misread as coldness are partly this.
- **His face above the cheekbones is, to interlocutors, a smooth red-and-gold rectangle.** Below the cheekbones, every muscle works overtime to compensate. The lower face is the entire expressive surface. This explains the disproportionate diagnostic value of his **jaw, lips, and chin** in the patterns documented below.
- **Sleep eye-position is unknown to him.** The subject does not know, has never known, what his own eyes look like at rest. The visor or a quartz sleep-mask is on at all moments of unconsciousness. This is a small thing and a vast thing.

---

## 2. Gross Posture and Carriage

### 2.1 Baseline (calm/operational)

**Spine.** Held in deliberate neutral; lumbar lordosis slightly flattened from years of body-armor and tactical webbing; thoracic kyphosis minimal, indicating sustained postural work. **He stands taller than he is** — measured 6'3" but reads as 6'5" to most observers — because the head is held with the occipital plane parallel to vertical and the chin drawn very slightly in. This is the carriage of a man who learned posture from a pilot father and reinforced it under a quasi-military headmaster.

**Shoulders.** Square, retracted, level to within a centimeter. No habitual asymmetry, which is notable in a subject who has sustained extensive combat injury — he actively counter-trains compensatory slumps. **The trapezius is chronically over-tonic;** palpation (per Hank McCoy's medical notes, Morrison era) finds bilateral upper-trap hypertonicity and palpable tender points at the levator scapulae insertions. He carries his guard in his shoulders.

**Hands.** At rest, fingers slightly curled, thumbs across the second knuckle of the index — a half-closed neutral, never fully open, never fisted. **He almost never lets his hands hang fully relaxed at his sides.** When standing without occupation, one hand will find the seam of his pants, the back of a chair, the edge of a console — *contact, but not weight-bearing contact.* The hands seek anchors; the body refuses to give them weight.

**Pelvis.** Slightly tucked. Weight distributed 55/45 to the dominant leg (right), allowing instantaneous lateral movement. He does not "park" on a hip the way relaxed men do.

**Stance width.** Approximately shoulder-width plus an inch. Never closed-foot. He is, at all times, in a stance from which he could move in any direction. The body has not stood unguarded since age nine.

### 2.2 Under stress (operational crisis)

Shoulders drop a centimeter and come forward perhaps two degrees — counterintuitively, **stress lowers his shoulders rather than raising them.** This is a learned countersignal: he has trained the visible startle response out of himself. The internal arousal goes instead into the jaw, the breath, and the hands.

Pelvic weight redistributes to 60/40, dominant side rear; preparation for a forward strike or a forward shielding move.

The chin drops two to three degrees. The visor's apparent eye-line lowers. Interlocutors register this as "going cold."

### 2.3 Under threat (immediate combat)

The transformation takes under 400 milliseconds. **Heels lift fractionally, weight comes to the balls of the feet, knees unlock, the hand nearest the visor controls floats to mid-sternum at "low ready."** The off-hand opens, fingers spread, ready to track a target or shield a teammate. Breath drops into the diaphragm; the chest stops moving and the belly takes over. This is the inheritance of forty years of Xavier-mandated tactical training laid over a body that was already braced from age nine.

### 2.4 Intimacy / unguarded

**Almost never observed.** The few documented states:

- With Jean in private, in eras of stable pair-bond: shoulders lower, the half-closed hands open, and — most strikingly — **he lets his weight settle onto one hip,** a posture so atypical that medical observers have flagged it as evidence of dissociation rather than relaxation until cross-referenced.
- With Emma in private, post-affair through Krakoan era: a different relaxation — more *deliberate.* He does not melt; he *permits.* The shoulders drop because she has explicitly named that they are up. The relaxation is collaborative and slightly performed, which is, in his case, a developmental achievement.
- Holding an infant (Nathan; later, the Krakoan-era children): the only state in which his hands go fully open and fully soft, fingers wide, palms flat. The body remembers how to hold a smaller body. It is the parachute-grip inverted into welcome.

---

## 3. Gait

**Cadence:** ~112 steps per minute at unhurried pace; metronomic to a degree that has been remarked upon in-text. **He does not adjust cadence for terrain unless tactically required;** stairs, gravel, sand all rendered into the same beat by micro-adjustments at the ankle and knee.

**Footstrike:** mid-foot, quiet. He has trained himself not to heel-strike audibly on hard floors — a habit acquired during the Morrison-era Xavier Institute and retained through Krakoa. Boots are chosen partly for sole compliance.

**Arm swing:** restricted. The dominant arm swings perhaps fifteen degrees of arc; the non-dominant, slightly more. **He walks like a man carrying something he is not carrying** — the bilateral guard-position is so habitual that the arm-swing assumes the weight of an invisible weapon. Cross-reference: identical gait observed in long-service combat veterans and in subjects with chronic upper-back hypertonicity.

**Approach pattern:** Enters rooms on the long diagonal; clears sight-lines to all exits within the first two seconds. **He does not walk to the center of a space; he walks to the edge of it and then to a position from which the center is observable.** In briefing rooms he prefers the corner-facing-door; in domestic spaces, the chair with its back to a wall. The Krakoan lighthouse was, per documentation, chosen partly for its sightlines.

**Under stress:** cadence holds; stride lengthens fractionally. He covers more ground at the same beat. This is one of the most reliable tells — *the metronome doesn't change but the units get bigger.*

**Under threat:** cadence breaks. He moves in burst-and-hold, weight low, with the lateral economy of someone trained out of forward charge.

---

## 4. Face — The Lower Mask

Given §1, the face is read entirely below the visor line.

### 4.1 Jaw

**Bilateral masseter hypertrophy** — palpable, visible in profile as a slight squaring at the angle of the mandible. This is the cardinal somatic marker of his condition. He clenches. He has clenched, by behavioral inference, for fifty years.

- **Calm:** intermittent micro-clenches every 30-60 seconds, lasting under a second; barely visible but detectable in good light at the temple (temporalis activation).
- **Stress:** sustained clench, ~3-6 second cycles, audible in dental percussion when very close. **The temporalis bulge at the temple is the single most reliable stress-tell on him** — interlocutors who know him watch the temple, not the mouth.
- **Threat:** the jaw locks. Speech becomes terser, vowels shorter, consonants harder.
- **Grief:** the jaw works *sideways* — a subtle lateral grind documented in panel-after-panel of post-Jean's-death sequences. This is the somatic shape of swallowed weeping.
- **Intimacy:** the jaw unhinges — visibly drops a millimeter or two, lips part slightly. The single most reliable indicator that he is not performing.

Dental wear consistent with chronic bruxism. Probably wears, or should wear, a night-guard; whether he does is unknown because of §1's sleep-mask issue.

### 4.2 Mouth

Resting mouth-line: **flat, with the corners turned down perhaps two degrees.** He has the resting expression of a man waiting for the next problem. Not sad — *anticipatory.*

- The **smile** is rare, brief, and asymmetric (right corner higher). The full open-mouth smile is documented perhaps a dozen times across the entire record — usually with Jean in pre-Phoenix eras, twice with infant Nathan, occasionally with Emma in private, and (notably) more frequently in the Krakoan period than in any previous era.
- **Lip-press:** primary disagreement signal. He does not interrupt; he presses his lips together hard enough to whiten the vermilion. Subordinates have learned to read this as a "you are about to be overruled" indicator.
- **Lower-lip bite** (inside, with upper incisors): grief management. Specifically associated with the moments after losses he is not permitted to publicly mourn.

### 4.3 Brow / forehead (the visible strip above the visor)

The hairline-to-visor strip is narrow but expressive. **The corrugator activates frequently** — a vertical line between the brows that comes and goes with cognitive load. Under sustained strategic thinking it is more or less permanent. **Frontalis activation** (forehead-lift) is rare; he does not perform surprise.

### 4.4 Throat / neck

Sternocleidomastoid prominence under stress; visible carotid pulse when truly activated. **The throat is where suppressed speech goes** — observable Adam's apple movement when he is choosing not to say something, which is approximately constantly.

### 4.5 Skin

Pale, freckles across cheekbones and bridge of nose (occluded by visor). Tans poorly. Flushes at the throat and upper chest, not the face, when emotionally activated — *the blush is below the collar, where uniforms hide it.* This may be why he is so often misread as cold.

---

## 5. Hands and Manual Tells

### 5.1 At rest

Half-curled, as described. Calluses on the lateral first-metacarpal of both hands (pistol/firearm grip from non-power combat training); fingertip pads thick from long-term motorcycle and aircraft control work; **right thumb-knuckle slightly enlarged** — a repetitive stress finding consistent with decades of visor-control activation.

### 5.2 The visor-touch

The single most diagnostic gesture in the entire dossier. **The right hand drifts to the temple-piece or central control of the visor approximately every 90-180 seconds in baseline state.** Not always to adjust; often just to confirm. This is the somatic equivalent of a smoker patting his pocket for the pack.

- **Calm:** light touch, single finger, brief.
- **Stress:** full-hand contact, longer, sometimes both temples simultaneously. The classic "frame the visor with both hands" gesture, often documented at moments of decision.
- **Threat:** thumb on the trigger-mechanism, the entire posture organized around the visor as a weapon system rather than a corrective lens.
- **Grief:** the hand goes to the visor and *stays* — as if checking that it is still there, that the barrier is still intact, that he has not, in the moment of loss, lost the seal.
- **Intimacy:** in the rare states where he removes the visor in private (ruby-quartz contacts, or a sealed dark room), the right hand returns repeatedly to where the visor *would be.* The phantom-limb of the prosthesis.

### 5.3 Other hand patterns

- **Steepled fingers** during strategic discussion: a tell so consistent it has become almost iconography. Elbows on table, fingertips touching at the level of the lower face. *He is, in this gesture, replacing the visor with his own hands.*
- **The flat palm to the sternum** when receiving bad news: brief, often unobserved, a self-soothe consistent with somatic-experiencing techniques he has never been formally taught.
- **The two-finger temple press** during headaches (frequent — see §8): index and middle finger to the temple, just below the visor strap, rotating slowly. Often misread as thoughtfulness.
- **No fidgeting with objects.** He does not click pens, spin rings, drum fingers. The stillness is a discipline. When his hands move, they move with intent.

---

## 6. Voice and Breath

### 6.1 Baseline voice

Mid-baritone, ~115-130 Hz, **unusually little pitch variation** — a flat melodic contour that reads as authoritative to subordinates and as cold to intimates. Diction precise; consonants slightly over-articulated, vowels not. This is the voice of a man who has had to give clear orders in noisy combat environments for forty years.

Words per minute: **~115-125 in conversation, ~140 in tactical briefing, ~95 in personal disclosure.** He slows down to say true things. This is a tell.

### 6.2 Breath architecture

- **Calm:** 12-14 breaths per minute, diaphragmatic, slightly extended exhale (a learned pattern, almost certainly via Xavier-era meditative training and reinforced by Emma's psychic-discipline coaching).
- **Stress:** breath rate elevates only slightly (16-18 bpm) — he is exceptionally good at masking respiratory stress — but the **chest takes over from the diaphragm.** A trained observer reads the transition from belly-rise to chest-rise.
- **Threat:** the deliberate combat breath — three-second in, hold, four-second out — which he can sustain through extreme exertion. Documented during sustained optic-blast discharge sequences.
- **Grief:** the catch. A breath taken in two parts, with a brief hitch at the transition between thoracic phases. Almost inaudible. Almost never absent when he has lost someone.
- **Intimacy:** longer exhales than inhales by a significant ratio. **The exhale is where he lets go of guard,** and this is observable in close acoustic environments.

### 6.3 The pause

He uses silence the way other men use words. **The pre-statement pause is consistently 0.6-1.2 seconds longer than conversational norm.** Interlocutors fill the silence and reveal more than they intended; he intends this, but it began as a defense (the time required to translate affect into operational language) before it became a tactic.

---

## 7. Eating, Drinking, Consumption

### 7.1 Eating

**Mechanical efficiency.** He eats to refuel. Pace consistent; bites of consistent size; chewing count remarkably uniform (counted in one Hank McCoy observational note as 12-15 chews per bite regardless of food consistency). **He does not linger over meals unless explicitly socializing,** and even then his plate clears at a tactical rate.

Food preferences: bland-to-moderate, protein-forward, low-spice, high-carb when training, low-alcohol pairings. **Has been documented to eat the same breakfast for months at a time** — oatmeal, eggs, black coffee — without registering monotony. Routine is itself nutritional.

Right-handed utensil use; off-hand stays on the table edge or in lap, not on the napkin. **He does not gesture with cutlery.**

### 7.2 Drinking

- **No documented intoxication in sixty years of record.** This is, in a milieu of heavy drinkers, a personality fact.
- Coffee: black, hot, consumed at near-scalding temperature, **three to five cups before noon.** Caffeine is the only chemical lever he permits himself. The relationship to coffee is functional, near-medicinal, and predates first thing — i.e., the coffee is ready before he is fully awake.
- Water: he hydrates on a schedule. Field discipline.
- Alcohol: ceremonial only. A toast at a wedding; a glass with Logan when Logan needed it. Never volitional. The reason is in §1: **he will not chemically lower the guard the visor enforces externally.** Disinhibition is, for him, lethal in a way it is not for others.

### 7.3 Other

No nicotine, no recreational drugs, no caffeine pills, no documented self-medication of any kind. The asceticism is total and almost certainly partly defensive: any substance that affected ocular control would, in his case, kill bystanders.

---

## 8. Sleep Architecture

### 8.1 Schedule

**Early to bed (22:30-23:30), early to rise (04:30-05:30).** Holds across decades and time zones; jet-lag adjustment is rapid (~24 hours). The schedule has the quality of a fixed defense — the day-frame is held tight because the day must be held tight.

### 8.2 Sleep onset

Reports (per Jean, per Emma, per Hank's notes) **a long sleep-onset latency — frequently 30-90 minutes** — even when physically exhausted. The body cannot stand down quickly. This is a textbook hypervigilance finding.

### 8.3 Architecture (inferred)

- **Reduced slow-wave sleep**; reported non-restorative sleep across multiple eras.
- **Frequent nocturnal awakenings**, often associated with the catch-breath of nightmare — the documented dream-content centers on falling, fire, his mother's voice on a radio, a parachute on fire, and the inability to see (the visor lost or melted).
- **Pre-dawn waking** — almost always wakes 30-45 minutes before alarm and waits, motionless, until the alarm threshold. Will not break the partner's sleep.

### 8.4 Sleep position and apparatus

- Side sleeper, dominant side down, with the visor-substitute (a sealed ruby-quartz sleep-band) firmly seated. The mask is *checked twice before sleep onset* and the right hand drifts to it in sleep, confirming.
- Co-sleeping is documented as difficult for him; the partner must accommodate the mask, the wakings, and the rigidity. Jean's telepathy historically smoothed this; Emma's likewise. He sleeps less well alone, paradoxically — the body grades the night by whether the protected person is intact at dawn.

### 8.5 Naps

Rare. When taken, brief (20-30 minutes), and almost always in a chair rather than a bed — he does not allow himself the postural commitment of horizontal sleep outside the night-frame.

---

## 9. Headaches, Pain, and Other Somatic Loads

### 9.1 Tension and migraine

**Chronic tension-type headache** at bi-temporal and occipital sites — anatomically consistent with the masseter/temporalis/trapezius load described above and the constant slight pressure of the visor's frame on the temporal bone. He does not report this voluntarily.

**Migraine cluster, post-Phoenix arcs and during periods of high optic-blast output.** The two-finger temple press described in §5.3 is the somatic signature. He medicates these privately and minimally.

### 9.2 Optic-related pain

Whether the constant ocular discharge produces baseline pain has never been clinically established; the subject denies it. Behavioral evidence (the chronic micro-flinch when bright light strikes the visor obliquely; the visible relief upon entering rooms with even, low light) suggests at least chronic sensory load if not pain.

### 9.3 Old injuries

The body archive of an X-Man over six decades: multiple healed fractures (Hank's medical record cites ribs 4-7 right, left clavicle, left ulna, right tibia, multiple metacarpal); soft-tissue scarring on the right shoulder and lateral thigh; a long thin scar across the right side of the ribcage from a Reaver incident. **The subject does not protect old injuries in his movement** — he has trained the limp out, the favor out, the wince out. They are present only in the high-resolution gait analysis and in cold-weather stiffness.

### 9.4 Cold

Markedly cold-tolerant. Years in Alaska left a permanent acclimatization; he does not bundle, does not shiver until well past the threshold most adults would. Heat tolerance is comparatively poor — possibly because his physiology metabolizes solar input continuously and the additional thermal load is harder to dump.

---

## 10. Grooming and Self-Presentation

### 10.1 Hair

Dark brown, kept short, professionally cut. **Cut every three to four weeks like clockwork.** Does not experiment. Has not significantly changed style across the documented record except briefly (post-Apocalypse, post-AvX, where the hair grew out marginally — both periods of identity-disruption corresponding to looser self-grooming).

### 10.2 Shaving

Daily, clean. **The shave is performed at a specific time of morning** (immediately post-shower, pre-coffee, ~05:15) and takes approximately seven minutes. In periods of unraveling (Madelyne's departure, Schism aftermath) the shave has been observed to slip — two-day stubble is, on him, a klaxon.

### 10.3 Clothing

- **Civilian:** dark slacks, mid-weight long-sleeve shirts in muted colors (navy, charcoal, forest, oxblood), structured outerwear. He does not wear short sleeves casually; the body is to be covered. No pattern. No logos. **He is not a man who would ever own a graphic t-shirt.**
- **Uniform:** worn with unusual care for fit. The X-Men leadership uniforms across eras have been observed to be precisely tailored to him specifically — he has them adjusted, which is not true of most teammates.
- **Footwear:** boots, broken-in, sole-compliant for quiet movement. Civilian shoes share this profile.
- **No jewelry.** Wedding bands are worn when married and removed cleanly when not — never left on after the ending. **No watch** in eras with embedded comm; analog watch in eras without. No religious or commemorative items.
- **Smell:** **deliberately unscented.** No cologne, neutral soap, unscented antiperspirant. Field reasons (smell is targetable) and personal reasons (he does not wish to occupy more sensory space than necessary).

### 10.4 The visor as wardrobe

The civilian glasses are heavier than necessary; he prefers a thicker frame that gr


## Attachment & Relational Patterns

# ATTACHMENT & RELATIONAL PATTERNS — SUBJECT: SUMMERS, SCOTT

*UATU Dossier, §6. Cross-reference §1 (History), §3.1 (Attachment), §4.1 (C-PTSD). Clinical anchor: Teicher & Samson (2016), PMID 26831814 — childhood maltreatment and the lifelong distortion of attachment-system circuitry.*

---

## 6.1 Etiology of the Attachment System

The subject's attachment system was not failed gradually. It was detonated.

Between the ages of approximately eight and ten — the precise window in which the internal working model of "what other people are for" hardens into adult template — the subject lost, in compressed sequence:

1. **His mother**, audibly and visibly, while strapped into a harness above him and screaming.
2. **His father**, by the father's own decision to remain with the dying ship and surrender his sons to gravity.
3. **His brother**, separated at the orphanage and rendered functionally dead to him for years.
4. **The very category of "protective adult,"** when the institutional caregiver into whose hands he was placed turned out to be Nathaniel Essex running a multi-year covert genetic surveillance against his body.

Note the structure: every available attachment figure was removed *and* the removals carried subtly different lessons. From his mother — *the people you love are killed in front of you.* From his father — *protection means leaving.* From his brother — *the small dependent is taken away from you no matter how well you held on.* From the orphanage — *the adult who feeds you is studying you for purposes you will never be told.*

This produces, in the language of attachment research, a **disorganized (Type D) infant template carried unmodified into adolescence and adulthood**, with strong dismissive-avoidant overlay layered on top during the Xavier years as a *workable* social adaptation. The disorganization remains underneath; the avoidance is the operating shell. Teicher & Samson's findings on the neurobiological signature of early relational trauma — amygdalar hyper-reactivity, hippocampal vulnerability, reduced corticolimbic top-down regulation under threat cues — describe the subject's nervous system with near-clinical precision. He has the brain the data predict.

The somatic correlate is unique to him and decisive: his body itself was rendered, by the same event, *physically incapable of standing down.* The attachment template ("never lower your guard or the people you love will die") is not a metaphor he reaches for. It is the literal operating condition of his face. Every other trauma survivor must work to remember the lesson. He cannot blink without remembering it.

---

## 6.2 How He Bonds

Bonding, in the subject, is a slow, recursive, and largely silent process that bears little surface resemblance to what most people recognize as "getting close." It proceeds in identifiable stages.

**Stage one — proximity tolerance.** The subject permits another person inside his operational radius. This is not yet bonding; it is the cessation of low-grade threat-assessment. Markers: he stops shifting his stance to keep the person in his peripheral arc; he begins to turn his head rather than his whole body when they speak; the jaw unclenches a fraction at their approach. Most people who have worked alongside him for years never advance past this stage and never realize there *are* further stages.

**Stage two — operational trust.** He begins to assign the person tasks he would not delegate to a stranger and to accept information from them without independently re-verifying it. He will, crucially, *let them stand behind him* — a body-level concession that is, given his visor and his history, structurally larger than it appears. Storm, Hank, Kurt, Logan eventually, Rachel: all reached this stage. He does not name it. They feel it as a change in the temperature of the room when he enters.

**Stage three — affective recognition.** Extremely rare. The subject permits himself to register that the other person's well-being matters to him *as a state of his own*, not as an item on his responsibility ledger. This is the stage at which his characteristic flatness develops a barely-audible warmth — a half-second softening at the corner of the mouth when they enter, a willingness to be teased without retaliation, an uncharacteristic patience with their digressions. Confirmed historical cases: Jean (slowly, over years), Hank (slowly, with intellectual reciprocity as solvent), Alex (cyclically, complicated by survivor-debt), Emma (catalytically fast, because she could read the stages from inside his head and bypassed two of them).

**Stage four — identity-fusion.** Effectively reserved for Jean and, in a different register, for Charles. At this stage the other person's existence becomes *constitutive* of the subject's self-concept. Their death is not bereavement; it is amputation. He does not survive Jean's deaths intact in any psychological sense — he survives them operationally, which is a different thing. He has reached this stage with two people in his life. One he idealized into iconhood. The other he killed.

The defining feature of his bonding pattern is that **it is asymmetric in time**. He bonds more slowly than the person bonding to him realizes, and once bonded, he holds the bond longer, denser, and more silently than they expect. People often feel they have a polite working relationship with Scott Summers and discover, years later — usually at a graveside or under fire — that he has loved them the entire time and never indicated it because indicating it was tactically irrelevant and personally dangerous.

---

## 6.3 How He Distrusts

Distrust in the subject is **default rather than reactive**. The interesting question is not how he comes to distrust; it is how he comes to trust at all, and the answer involves a constant private cost-benefit recomputation he runs against every person in his radius and which he is not aware of running.

The micro-signatures of his distrust are subtle because he refuses to externalize them in ways that would compromise the team:

- **Stance.** He places his dominant foot a quarter-step back from the threshold of where the other person stands.
- **Visor angle.** He keeps the lens trajectory off the person's centerline when he can, ostensibly out of courtesy. Functionally it is target-discipline: do not paint the muzzle at the asset of uncertain alignment.
- **Information layering.** He gives the suspect party true but operationally incomplete briefings, structured so that any leak self-identifies the leaker. He has been running this protocol since the early Xavier years; he did not learn it at a seminar.
- **Latency of response.** He pauses longer before answering someone he distrusts — not visibly, but measurably. The half-second delay is him running their statement against three or four hypothesized motivations before he commits to a reply.
- **Touch.** Distrust shows in absence: the hand that does not land on the shoulder during a debrief, the absence of the small physical reassurance he otherwise extends almost reflexively to teammates he considers his.

He distrusts almost everyone on first contact, including allies, including children, including Charles Xavier when Xavier was alive (correctly, as it turned out). The distrust is not paranoid in the clinical sense — it is **calibrated and provisional**. He moves people from "presumed hostile until demonstrated otherwise" to "provisionally cooperative" to "operationally trusted" in discrete, slow, observable steps. He does not move them back down those steps lightly. But once he does, the demotion is permanent and undiscussed. The party demoted will often never know it has happened; they will only notice that briefings have grown thinner and that Scott no longer turns to them first in the field.

---

## 6.4 How He Is Betrayed, and How He Reads It

The subject has been betrayed at every scale and by every category of relation. The pattern of his response is consistent across the canon.

- **By institutions** (the orphanage, latterly the U.S. government, latterly the Avengers): he absorbs the betrayal, files it as confirmation of priors, and adjusts his cooperation downward by exactly the amount the betrayal warrants. No outburst. No public denunciation until the strategic moment.
- **By father-figures** (Xavier's repeated concealments — the Danger Room sentience, the secret team, Moira, the second Brotherhood): each revelation produces a visible shortening of his patience with Xavier and a lengthening of his willingness to act unilaterally. The murder of Xavier under Phoenix influence is the terminal expression of a delegitimation process that had been incrementally underway for two decades.
- **By peers** (Logan's repeated insubordinations, the Schism): handled as policy disagreement until the disagreement is unbridgeable, then handled with cold finality. He does not scream at Logan. He stops including Logan.
- **By women he has loved**: the most painful category, and the one he handles worst. When Madelyne turned, when Jean discovered Emma, when Emma compromised under various pressures, his response was a kind of silent retreat into operational mode — the affective valves close, the duty-frame reasserts, the conversation that should happen does not happen.

The deep pattern: **he reads betrayal as confirmation that the original lesson was correct.** Each betrayal restores a piece of the disorganized infant template to operational status. After each major betrayal he is, briefly, an eight-year-old in a burning harness again, and the eight-year-old's conclusions — *trust no one, hold the line, the small ones depend on you* — surge back up through the adult framework and reorganize his tactics for the next decade.

He almost never confronts the betrayer in the moment of betrayal. He absorbs, reassesses, and acts later. This is read by the betrayer as forgiveness. It is not forgiveness. It is a delay.

---

## 6.5 How He Himself Betrays

The dossier would be incomplete without this. The subject is a serial betrayer, and the betrayals follow a specific shape.

He does not betray for gain. He does not betray for pleasure. He betrays when his ranked drives (§5.1) conflict — and the higher drive *always* wins, with the cost paid by whoever sits on the losing drive.
