- A combination of total mission collapse and loss of all primary attachments simultaneously.

Under such conditions the floor that has held him up his entire life would fail, and there is no secondary structure beneath it. This is the classic C-PTSD presentation Teicher & Samson and the broader trauma literature describe as the *high-functioning trauma survivor with annihilation-adjacent interior*: outwardly the most competent person in the room, internally one structural failure away from total collapse. Most clinicians, in real-world analogs, do not detect this risk until it is too late, because the surface presentation is reassuring.

Monitoring recommendation: assume the subject's stated affect is approximately one full register more positive than his actual interior, particularly during and immediately after major losses.

### 4.2 Harm-to-Others Risk

**Baseline: low. Mission-frame: elevated and conscience-mediated.**

In baseline functioning the subject is among the least violent people in his social milieu — disciplined, restrained, rule-bound. The elevated harm-to-others risk is entirely conditional on his having convinced himself that the conventional ethical floor is a luxury his species cannot afford. When that conviction sets, the harm authorized is substantial (X-Force, AvX-era decisions, the use of children as soldiers). The risk is not impulse-driven; it is doctrine-driven, which makes it both more dangerous (will not be deterred by ordinary inhibitors) and more predictable (will be preceded by observable shifts in his stated operational code).

Early-warning indicators for this drift include: increased compartmentalization of decisions from teammates; cessation of consultation with figures who serve as ethical brakes (historically Xavier, sometimes Storm, currently Jean); the subject's use of extinction-framing in operational language; visible identification-with-the-aggressor patterns (Magneto-coded rhetoric and tactics).

### 4.3 Risk to Intimate Partners

A category often omitted but warranted here. The subject has not, in any record, perpetrated interpersonal violence against an intimate partner. He has, however, repeatedly caused severe relational harm through **abandonment, withholding, and prioritization of mission over presence.** Madelyne Pryor's psychological deterioration is not solely attributable to Sinister's manipulations; the subject's instantaneous abandonment of her and their infant when Jean returned was a precipitating injury that any honest assessment must register. Jean herself absorbed the cost of his emotional unavailability for the entire run of their adult relationship. Emma has been more durable because she came equipped with armor specifically calibrated for him, but even she has paid.

This pattern is not malicious; it is structural, and it traces directly to the formative scene in which the subject learned that the protective figure leaves to save the child. He is reenacting his father.

---

## 5. PROGNOSIS AND TREATMENT CONSIDERATIONS (Hypothetical)

The subject is, by ordinary clinical standards, an excellent candidate for trauma-focused treatment and an unlikely one to ever receive it. Excellent candidate because: intact cognitive capacity, high motivation when framed as duty, capacity for sustained relational engagement with a competent figure, real (if buried) capacity for affective experience. Unlikely to receive treatment because: the entire personality structure is organized around not requiring it, the surrounding institutional culture does not provide for it, and the one telepath who could have done the deepest work with him was his father-figure and is now dead at his own hand — a transferential complication of unusual severity.

If treatment were ever attempted, the access points are: (a) parenting (his relationships with Nathan, Rachel, and the younger mutants are where his defenses most often slip and where genuine grief-work could be initiated); (b) somatic intervention focused on the chronic pain and sleep architecture, which would lower physiological load and might permit affect that the body currently cannot afford; (c) the Emma relationship, which functions as a low-grade ongoing therapeutic frame whether either of them names it as such.

The contemporary Krakoan-era presentation should not be read as cure. It is accommodation. The man inside the accommodation is the same man who was strapped into the parachute, and he has not yet been allowed to land.


## Behavioral Atlas

# BEHAVIORAL ATLAS — SUBJECT: SUMMERS, SCOTT

*Compiled from longitudinal observation across all published surveillance windows (1963–present). Tells are presented as condition-keyed clusters: somatic, vocal, micro-motor, decisional, interpersonal. Where a tell has been observed to vary across eras, era-tags are appended.*

---

## 1. BASELINE — THE STANDING STATE

The subject does not have a "relaxed" baseline in any clinical sense; he has a **regulated** baseline, which is a different thing. What an observer reads as composure is, on closer inspection, the steady output of an enormous regulatory effort that never stops running.

### 1.1 Somatic baseline

- **Posture.** Squared shoulders, neutral pelvis, weight slightly forward on the balls of the feet. This is not military bearing in the parade sense; it is **launch-ready bearing** — a posture optimized for the first quarter-second of any sudden movement. Even seated, the subject keeps both feet flat and slightly back of the knees, never crossed. Crossed legs are a vulnerable configuration; he does not adopt them.
- **Head carriage.** Slight downward tilt — perhaps four to seven degrees — that aligns the lower rim of the visor/glasses with the eye-level of the average adult interlocutor. This is **functional**: it keeps the beam vector aimed at chest-or-below rather than at faces during conversation. Over decades the habit has become postural, persisting even when he is alone in his quarters with the visor on.
- **Jaw.** Persistently set. Masseter hypertrophy visible to anyone who looks for it. He is, in the literal anatomical sense, a man who clenches his jaw all day, every day. The tension headaches and grinding (§2.3 of the prior file) follow from this directly.
- **Hands.** At rest, open and flat against the thigh or the table, fingers slightly spread. Almost never balled, almost never fidgeting. When the hands DO move, they move with deliberation — pick up the cup, move the cup, place the cup — never the half-aborted hand-gestures most people produce while thinking. He has trained the unconscious gesture out of himself.
- **Breath.** Slow, low, diaphragmatic. Inhale through the nose, exhale through the nose, four-to-six second cycle. Whether this was taught (Xavier, plausibly) or developed independently, it is a continuous active regulation, not a constitutional calm.
- **Eye-region (under the visor).** Across the published corpus, when the visor is removed in trusted darkness, the eyes are observed to be **closed firmly**, not slack. He sleeps with them closed hard. Even unconscious, the subject's body knows the rule.

### 1.2 Vocal baseline

- **Pitch:** mid-baritone, narrow dynamic range. Rarely modulates more than a fifth in normal speech.
- **Pace:** measured, with consistent inter-word spacing. He does not interrupt himself. He does not back-track. The lack of disfluency is itself a tell — natural speech is full of "uh" and "I mean" and self-correction; his is not. He has thought the sentence before delivering it.
- **Diction:** complete sentences, subordinate clauses fully closed, terminal punctuation audible. In tactical mode this becomes a clipped vocative register that he uses for orders. In intimate mode it gentles slightly but does not loosen structurally.
- **Silence usage:** he is comfortable with three-to-five second pauses in conversation that would distress most interlocutors. The silence is not hostile; it is processing space he reserves and refuses to give up out of social pressure.

### 1.3 Micro-motor baseline

- **Visor-touch.** Index and middle finger of the dominant hand briefly contact the right temple of the visor approximately every twelve to twenty minutes, regardless of activity. This is the equivalent of a smoker patting the cigarette pocket — an unconscious confirmation that the regulatory apparatus is in place. He does this in his sleep if startled awake.
- **Lens-cleaning ritual.** Cloth from inside pocket (always the same pocket; left-inside if jacketed), both lenses, left-then-right, two passes each, fold-and-replace. Performed roughly every two to three hours and at every situational transition (entering a room, finishing a meal, before speaking to a stranger). The ritual is **anxiety-binding** and observationally indistinguishable from a religious gesture.
- **Pocket checks.** Spare visor (or spare ruby-quartz glasses) carried at all times. Will pat-confirm its presence on entry/exit from any room. Has carried a spare since adolescence; the one published period in which he was without one ended badly and reinforced the habit permanently.

### 1.4 Decisional baseline

- **Information acquisition before commitment.** Standard sequence: scan environment, identify variables, identify dependents (who needs protecting), identify exits, *then* commit to a course. The sequence is fast (sub-second in his prime) but it is always run. He does not move first and think second except under direct threat to a dependent, in which case the sequence inverts in a way that has cost him.
- **Two-deep planning.** He thinks in if-then trees and discloses only the first branch. The second-order plan is held in reserve. This is not deception; it is operational compartmentalization (§3.2 of the prior file rendered as habit). Subordinates who have worked with him long enough learn to ask explicitly for the contingency.

---

## 2. UNDER CALM (low-stakes, low-stimulus conditions)

The calm-state subject is the rarest and most diagnostic of all his presentations, because calm is, for him, a *state he doesn't quite know how to occupy*. The defenses do not relax; they merely have nothing to defend against, and the resulting under-load produces its own tells.

- **Restlessness disguised as productivity.** Will pick up a task — equipment maintenance, lesson planning, a flight log, in the Krakoan era the lighthouse generator — within minutes of having nothing required of him. He does not sit and stare. He does not nap on the couch. The longest contiguous published moment of pure stillness in his canon is, suggestively, immediately after one of the catastrophic losses, not during peacetime.
- **Maintenance behaviors as substitute for leisure.** Cleans the visor more often than necessary. Reorganizes the Blackbird cockpit pre-flight checklists. Audits training rosters. The activities are real but their frequency is over-determined.
- **Reading.** Will read — technical manuals, history, occasionally poetry (this is observed only in the most intimate-with-Jean published windows and is conspicuously absent from his solo periods). Reading is the only activity in which his face fully relaxes; observers in canon have noted this. The masseter unclenches. The jaw drops a millimeter. He does not know this happens.
- **Coffee, black, two cups in the morning, one mid-afternoon.** No sugar, no cream. The consistency is the point; the caffeine is incidental.
- **Eats fast and without comment.** Food is fuel. Will eat whatever is in front of him without complaint and without enthusiasm. The exception — small, but present — is when Jean cooks or Emma orders something specifically for him, in which case he registers the gesture and slows down.

---

## 3. UNDER LOW-TO-MODERATE STRESS (operational tempo, planning, briefings)

This is his **best-functioning** band — the condition for which his entire personality is optimized. An external observer would describe him here as "in his element," and they would be correct in the limited sense that the load matches the regulatory capacity exactly.

- **Voice tightens by perhaps one-third of a tone, paces faster, becomes more clipped.** Acquires what teammates have, across decades, called the "field voice." It is recognizable to anyone who has flown an op with him.
- **Spatial behavior changes.** Will stand rather than sit if any decision is pending. Will gravitate to a position that puts a wall behind him and a clear sightline to entries. This is unconscious; he will do it in a coffee shop.
- **Map-making with hands.** When briefing, uses hands to construct invisible terrain on the table or in the air — vectors, perimeters, fields of fire. The gestures are precise, repeated, and reproducible across decades of published material. He thinks geometrically and his hands tell on him.
- **Names of personnel become full names.** In casual conversation Bobby is Bobby; in briefing Bobby becomes Robert Drake, Iceman. The formalization is automatic and it signals to anyone present that the subject has crossed into operational mode.
- **Will not eat while briefing.** Will hold a coffee cup and not drink from it.
- **Does not solicit opinions until he has stated his own.** A management vice he has never fully corrected. The pattern: states plan, asks for objections, listens to objections, integrates or rejects them with reasons. Almost never asks "what should we do" with the question genuinely open. He is constitutionally bad at deferring to a room.

---

## 4. UNDER ACUTE THREAT (combat, imminent danger)

The combat-state subject is the one his enemies have catalogued most carefully and the one in which the largest gap exists between subjective experience and behavioral output. Internally: full activation. Externally: an unnerving deceleration.

### 4.1 Time-perception and motion

- **Apparent slowing.** Multiple writers across multiple eras describe his combat presentation as if he were moving at a different speed than the engagement around him. This is partly the geometric cognition — he is solving the firing solution before he commits — and partly a trained suppression of the startle reflex. He does not flinch. Observers who try to startle him into flinching note that the head moves slightly to *align the visor*, not away.
- **Beam-discipline.** In sixty years of published combat, the number of times he has fired an optic blast at a target he had not consciously selected can be counted on one hand, and each instance is treated by the narrative as a major event. He does not spray. He does not warning-shot. He fires once at the chosen point, calibrated by aperture-width, and adjusts. The economy is so total it reads as artistry; it is in fact discipline born of the certainty that an uncontrolled discharge will kill an ally.
- **Ricochet and bank-shot specialty.** Documented across decades — he uses geometry against the environment in a way no other beam-attacker in the canon does. This is **not** showmanship; it is a worldview rendered as combat style. The straight line is dangerous; the calculated indirect approach is safer.

### 4.2 Vocal under threat

- **Voice drops in pitch and loudness simultaneously.** The "field voice" tightens further. Orders become two-or-three-word imperatives, name-first: "Logan, left. Ororo, lift. Now."
- **No profanity.** Across the published corpus, the subject's swearing rate in combat is nearly zero. This is notable and not accidental; profanity is an affect-discharge channel, and he has all his channels closed.
- **Will not yell** unless yelling is tactically required to be heard. He does not yell *at* people, only *to* them.

### 4.3 Micro-tells under threat

- **Visor-touch frequency rises sharply.** From every twelve-to-twenty minutes to every thirty-to-sixty seconds during sustained engagement. Each touch is a confirmation: the apparatus is in place, the discharge is contained.
- **Breathing locks into a four-count.** Inhale two, hold one, exhale two, hold one. This is observable in the shoulders if you know to look.
- **Off-hand fingers extend and flex once before any major action.** A small somatic clearing-of-the-channel. Easy to miss.

### 4.4 Decisional under threat

- **Triage by dependency.** He targets, moves, and shields in an order determined by who is the most fragile dependent in proximity. Civilians first, students second, less-durable teammates third, durable teammates fourth, himself never on the list. This is so consistent it can be predicted in advance.
- **Will accept a wound to prevent an ally's wound.** Documented across every era. He registers his own injury as data, not pain.
- **Withholds powerful options for late deployment.** Visor-open full-aperture discharges are reserved for late in an engagement when geometry has been established. He fights below his ceiling for as long as he can.

---

## 5. UNDER INTIMACY

The intimate-state subject is the most behaviorally interesting because the defenses are not designed for this condition and the failures of regulation that surface here are the most diagnostic data in the file.

### 5.1 Physical intimacy

- **Touch initiation is rare and weight-bearing.** He does not touch casually. The hand on the shoulder, when it comes, is deliberate and slightly heavier than expected — communicating presence, not affection in the ambient sense. He does not pat. He does not squeeze.
- **Removal of the visor as the central erotic gesture of his life.** This is so over-determined it requires no elaboration, but the granular observation is this: he removes the visor only in absolute darkness and only with a partner he has, in his own internal accounting, ceded the right to kill him. The gesture is not flirtation; it is *consent to mutual annihilation under controlled conditions.* Both partners who have shared this with him — Jean and Emma — have understood it as such, which is part of why no other partner is plausible.
- **Eyes-closed proximity.** In the lit world, when he is close enough to a trusted intimate for the question to arise, he will close his eyes — pre-emptively, briefly, as a kind of half-removal of the visor. The gesture reads to outsiders as romantic; it is in fact regulatory.

### 5.2 Verbal intimacy

- **Cannot deliver "I love you" without context.** The phrase, in the published record, almost always appears under crisis cover — before a mission, during a goodbye, in the seconds before someone's apparent death. He cannot say it in the kitchen on a Tuesday. Both Jean and Emma have, at various points, named this.
- **Apologizes specifically and concretely or not at all.** When he apologizes, it is for an identified act with stated impact: "I should not have ordered you to hold that position." General apologies ("I'm sorry I've been distant") are beyond him.
- **Receives compliments badly.** Will deflect to operational utility ("the plan was good") rather than accept personal credit. Receives criticism well, almost gratefully — he is already running an interior version of it.

### 5.3 With Jean (specific pattern)

- A particular slowness around her. Movement deceleration in her physical presence — observed by multiple writers. He moves around her as one moves around a sleeping child or an unstable explosive: with care for both her safety and his own deceleration into a state he does not entirely trust.
- Looks at her *more* than at other people, even with the visor — orientation is the giveaway; head turns track her in a room.
- Voice loses a fraction of its clipped quality. Sentences acquire small redundancies — the disfluencies he otherwise suppresses appear here, in her presence only.

### 5.4 With Emma (specific pattern)

- A particular *speed* around her, conversationally — they cross-talk, finish, interrupt. She is the only person in the canon he interrupts. This is intimacy rendered as the dropping of one of his most rigid rules.
- He lets her see him not knowing something. He does not do this with anyone else.
- He is, with her, occasionally — and this is the rarest published behavior — funny. Dry, oblique, a half-second pause before the punchline. The humor is real. Most of his life has not had room for it.

### 5.5 With his son(s)

- The hand on the shoulder, never the embrace. He does not know how to embrace his children; he never learned the gesture from a father who left him in a parachute.
- Eye-contact-via-visor sustained longer with Nathan/Cable than with anyone else in the canon. The unspoken acknowledgment is the only acknowledgment he can manage.
- Speaks to them as adults from the time they are very small. Cannot baby-talk. Cannot perform parental warmth he does not first translate into respect.

---

## 6. UNDER GRIEF

The grief-state subject is the great anti-spectacle of the canon. The defining quality is **the absence of grief-behavior where grief-behavior is expected.**

- **Does not cry on-panel** except in a handful of singular, marked instances spread across sixty years. The weeping, when it occurs, is small — a single tear, a turned face, a hand to the visor. He does not sob. He has, evidently, never learned to.
- **Increases operational output.** The post-loss period is, paradoxically, his most productive. The schedule fills. The training intensifies. The reports get written. This is not denial in the simple sense; it is the only available metabolic pathway for the affect.
- **Withdraws spatially.** Will choose to be alone — in a cockpit, on a rooftop, on the lighthouse balcony — rather than with the team. Will accept Jean's or Emma's presence in these withdrawals; will not accept anyone else's.
- **Eats less. Sleeps less. Coffee intake doubles.** The somatic load becomes visible if you look at his face on a two-week timeline post-loss; the cheekbones sharpen, the eyes hollow.
- **Resists ceremony.** Will attend the funeral; will not give the eulogy if he can avoid it; if forced to speak will produce a brief, structurally perfect, affectively closed remembrance that names the dead and the duty owed to them.
- **The grief, accumulated and never discharged, is the substrate for the catastrophic-discharge episodes** (Dark Phoenix-adjacent, AvX, the Xavier killing). The dam is real and so is the volume behind it.

---

## 7. UNDER VICTORY

The victory-state subject is the **most poorly equipped** of all his presentations. He does not know how to win.

- **Does not celebrate.** Will nod, will offer a clipped "good work," will move immediately to debrief and after-action accounting. The team has learned not to expect more.
- **Begins the next plan.** Victory is, for him, the start-condition of the next defense; he does not occupy it as a state.
- **Discomfort with public acknowledgment.** Will accept thanks shortly and deflect to the team. Will not give a speech if he can avoid one. When he must — Krakoan-era statecraft has forced this — the delivery is competent and entirely without uplift; he speaks of work to be done, not of triumph behind.
- **One specific micro-tell.** A small, almost imperceptible exhale — a single breath longer than the regulated four-count — when an operation closes successfully and the last dependent is confirmed safe. This is the closest thing in his behavioral repertoire to a sigh of relief. Observers who know him can read it; he is unaware he does it.

---

## 8. UNDER DEFEAT

The defeat-state subject is the one most observed by adversaries and the one in which his most dangerous decisional patterns emerge.

- **Does not externalize blame.** Will internalize the failure entire, often beyond his actual share. Subordinates who attempt to share the burden are dismissed kindly and the burden retained.
- **Re-runs the engagement.** Will, within hours, reconstruct the sequence in detail and identify the decision-node at which he should have chosen differently. Catalogs it. Adds it to the ledger.
- **The doctrinal break.** This is the dangerous pattern. Defeat at a sufficient scale provokes him to discard a constraint he had previously accepted. X-Force after sufficient X-Men deaths. The Phoenix bid after sufficient mutant deaths. The break is always presented internally as *necessity*, never as *choice* — which is precisely how it slips past his conscience.
- **Withdraws warmth from himself first, then from peers.** The intimate channels close before the operational ones. Jean/Emma report a perceptible cooling that precedes any visible operational change.
- **Sleeps even less.** The published record contains several extended insomnia arcs, each correlated to a major defeat. The visor stays on through what little sleep he gets.

---

## 9. ROUTINES, ROUTES, RITUALS

### 9.1 Daily

- **Wakes early.** Pre-dawn or shortly after. Has done so since adolescence; the orphanage-era habit never released him.
- **Visor-on before feet hit floor.** The first conscious motion of every day is the seating of the apparatus. He has not opened his eyes to a lit room without it since he was a child.
- **Morning routine is fixed and brief.** Wash, shave (clean-shaven across most published eras; the brief facial-hair periods correlate to grief states or undercover postings and are treated by him as lapses), dress in functional layers, coffee.
- **First action of the working day is review of overnight intelligence/status.** Before food, before greeting anyone. Has done variations of this from the original X-Men through Krakoa.
- **Walks his perimeter.** Whatever the perimeter is — mansion grounds, Utopia, Krakoan lighthouse — he walks it daily, on foot, alone, at variable intervals to defeat predictable observation. The route is never identical day-to-day; the *fact* of the walk is invariant.

### 9.2 Pre-flight

- **Checklist read aloud, even when alone.** Trained-pilot behavior inherited from his father by genetics and by professional ethic. The aloud reading is unusual and persistent; he does not trust silent reading for safety-critical material.
- **Hand on the airframe before boarding.** Small contact, palm flat. A pilot's superstition rendered as a moment of acknowledgment to the machine. He does this with every aircraft he flies, including ones he has flown a hundred times.

### 9.3 Pre-combat

- **Five-second visor seating check.** Always.
- **Spare-visor confirmation.** Always.
- **Eye-contact-via-visor with each teammate in rotation before deployment.** A silent muster. He has done some version of this since the original team; the contemporary version is barely perceptible.

### 9.4 Post-combat

- **Headcount before debrief.** Names spoken aloud, response received from each. Will not begin debrief until every named teammate has answered.
- **Equipment maintenance before sleep.** Visor cleaned, blast-suit checked, weapons (if any carried) returned to specified locations. The ritual is anxiety-binding; he does not sleep without performing it.

### 9.5 Memorial behaviors

- **Marks the dates.** Across the canon he has been observed to know the calendar dates of significant losses without consultation. He does not commemorate them aloud. They are kept in an internal calendar that other people have, periodically, accidentally bumped into.
- **Visits the graves alone.** When grave-visiting occurs at all, it is solo and brief. He does not bring flowers. He stands, head slightly tilted, hands at sides, for a fixed-feeling interval, and leaves.

---

## 10. TELLS THAT BETRAY THE INTERIOR

A short index of the small things that reveal what the rest of the apparatus is designed to conceal.

- **The masseter twitch when Xavier's name is invoked in a context he disagrees with.** Single contraction, sub-second, immediately suppressed. Reliable across decades.
- **The half-breath caught and released when Madelyne or Nathan is mentioned without warning.** The only published involuntary somatic discharge associated with the abandonment material.
- **The way his head turns one or two degrees toward Jean whenever she enters a room, even with the visor down and the back of his head to the door.** He registers her by something other than sight. He has never commented on it.
- **


## Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

# 6. DAILY LIFE, ROUTINES & RITUALS

*What a continuous-monitoring file would record across an ordinary seven-day window. Drawn from longitudinal behavioral baseline (Claremont through Hickman/Duggan), normalized to a stable operational period — i.e., not a crisis week, not a war week, just a week in which Scott Summers is simply living.*

---

## 6.1 The Architecture of His Day

Subject's day is built from the outside in. He does not wake up and decide what to do; the day's structure is already in place when consciousness arrives, and his task is to occupy it accurately. This is a trauma-organized cognitive economy: **decisions cost more than tasks**, so the day is engineered to minimize decisions and maximize execution. The few discretionary moments that exist are themselves ritualized to the point of being non-discretionary.

In any given residence — the Mansion attic suite (Claremont period), the Anchorage cabin (Madelyne years), the brownstone safehouses (X-Factor), the Utopia command quarters, the Krakoan lighthouse — the subject re-installs the same five rituals within seventy-two hours of arrival: a designated waking window, a designated pre-coffee threshold, a designated visor-on point, a designated map-and-roster review, and a designated last-light walk. The walls change. The grid does not.

---

## 6.2 0430–0600 — The Waking Protocol

Subject wakes between **04:30 and 05:10**, almost always before any alarm, in every era documented. The body has internalized the schedule the body was first taught — the orphanage's pre-dawn routine, which Mister Sinister's staff would have enforced for observational reasons the child never knew. The subject has never broken the pattern.

The sequence on waking is precise and never varies in order, regardless of where he is sleeping:

1. **Eyes stay closed.** This is the most important fact about Scott Summers' morning and the one civilians never grasp. He cannot afford the half-second between waking and reaching the lenses. He reaches first, opens second. The lenses (ruby-quartz wraparound, or in recent eras the contact-lens variant when sleeping near Jean or Emma) sit on the nightstand at a memorized distance — right side of the bed, far edge, parallel to the lamp base, lenses-down. He can find them by touch in total darkness inside two seconds. He has practiced this. He has practiced it more times than any other physical action of his adult life.
2. **Lenses on, eyes open, room scanned.** Threat-assessment of the room: exits, sleeping partner's breathing pattern, ambient sound profile of the building. Takes perhaps four seconds. He is unaware he is doing it.
3. **Sit up slowly, hand on the bedframe.** Subject is prone to morning orthostatic dips since the Apocalypse bonding era; he learned not to stand abruptly.
4. **Glance at the partner.** If Jean or Emma is present, a deliberate, soft look at the sleeping face. This is the only unguarded second of his day. Affection register, full, for one breath. Then it closes.

By 04:45 he is on his feet, by 04:50 in workout clothes laid out the night before in the same fold-stack he has used since Xavier's School (shirt on top, pants flat beneath, socks rolled and tucked inside the right shoe, left shoe forward of right by half its length). Bathroom: cold water on the face under closed eyes, lenses replaced, teeth brushed for the same ninety seconds he has used for forty years.

**0500–0600: physical training.** The composition shifts by era — Mansion-era calisthenics and Danger Room drills, Anchorage-era heavy lifts and bush running, Utopia-era close-quarters with Logan or Domino, Krakoan-era solo movement on the lighthouse rocks — but the duration and the time-block do not. He has not skipped a morning training session for non-injury reasons in any continuity since adolescence. **Running:** flat-footed, metronomic, breath-counted in fours, eyes scanning forward and middle distance. **Strikes work:** clean repetitions, no theatrics, never to exhaustion — always one set short of failure, because the subject does not permit himself to fail at a measurable thing if he can stop short of it.

He does not listen to music while training. He has never been observed to listen to music while training. He counts.

---

## 6.3 0600–0730 — The Coffee, the Map, the Roster

Subject's first ingestion of the day is **black coffee, no sugar, one mug, never refilled.** Brewed by him personally in every residence in which a coffeemaker is available; brewed in a stovetop percolator at Anchorage; field-brewed in a tin cup over a burner when deployed. The mug is always the same mug if he has been in the residence more than a week — he selects one on arrival and uses only that one. He washes it himself, immediately, by hand, and replaces it lenses-down on the same square of counter.

**Breakfast, when taken, is minimal and consistent:** one piece of fruit, two eggs or a slice of dense bread, water. He does not eat sweet things in the morning. He does not eat at all on operational mornings — fasted-state cognition is something he has trained for since X-Factor.

The post-coffee block, 06:15 to 07:30 in ordinary weeks, is the **map-and-roster review.** This is the ritual that organizes his command capacity. Across eras the medium changes — wall corkboards at the Mansion, a fold-out chart on the Anchorage kitchen table, holo-projection on Utopia, Krakoan biome-data scrolls — but the content does not:

- Current location of every person under his nominal protection.
- Current location of every person he considers a personal threat to those people.
- Outstanding obligations, in priority order.
- Three contingency branches for the day's most likely failure mode.

He does this in silence. He does not speak to anyone during this block unless directly addressed. Partners learn early not to attempt conversation between 06:15 and 07:30. Jean used to bring him a second cup of water at 07:00 without speaking and leave the room; Emma reads in the same room without acknowledging him until he closes the chart, at which point she will say one sentence, usually dry, often correct, and he will allow the day to begin.

---

## 6.4 0730–1200 — The Operational Forenoon

The forenoon is where the institutional Scott Summers actually exists. Composition by era:

- **Mansion-era:** classroom (he taught — geometry, history, leadership theory; his geometry lectures are remembered by students as exceptionally clear and exceptionally cold), Danger Room sequence design, paperwork for Xavier.
- **X-Factor-era:** field briefings, surveillance review, parent-conversations with Nathan (rare, awkward, attempted).
- **Utopia-era:** standing meetings — Emma, Magneto, Namor, the Cuckoos; resource allocation; press considerations.
- **Krakoan-era:** Captain Commander duties, Quiet Council scheduling, X-Force liaison (which he handles personally because he does not delegate the wet work to subordinates without his direct authorization).

Across eras the **meeting style** is identical and instantly recognizable on tape. He sits forward, hands flat on the table or one wrist crossed over the other, never leans back. He speaks last when possible. When he does speak, he speaks in **complete declarative sentences with no filler.** He does not say "um." He does not say "I think." He says "We do X. Then Y. If Z, then A." Listeners frequently report feeling as if they have already agreed before the proposition has finished.

He is unfailingly polite, in a register so consistent it reads as cold. He thanks people by name. He does not joke in meetings. He has been observed to smile in a meeting fewer than a dozen times across decades of recorded proceedings, and each instance is documented and contextually anomalous.

**Pen and notebook present at all meetings, regardless of era.** He prefers a small bound notebook and a fine-point pen. The notes are precise, abbreviated, dated, and stored. He has kept these notebooks since the original Xavier years. Surveillance recovery of his personal archive would yield decades of them, all in the same hand, all in the same shorthand, all numbered.

---

## 6.5 1200–1300 — The Walk

The subject **walks at midday.** This is one of the few rituals that is genuinely his, not inherited from institutional schedule. Twenty to forty-five minutes, weather-permitting in all but the worst conditions, alone if possible. In the Anchorage years he walked the gravel road to the airstrip and back. At the Mansion he walked the perimeter of the grounds clockwise, always clockwise, the same route. On Utopia he walked the cliff edge. On Krakoa he walks the spit out to the lighthouse and back.

He does not check communications during the walk. This is one of perhaps three windows in the day during which he is genuinely unreachable by choice, and the staff around him have learned to respect it without ever being told to respect it.

He uses this hour to do the thinking he cannot do at the table. The thinking is not pleasant. It is the thinking about who is in the most danger this week, what he is currently lying about and to whom, what he owes and to whom, and what he is going to do next that he is going to regret. He returns from the walk having reached conclusions. The conclusions are then executed in the afternoon.

He does not eat lunch. Has not regularly eaten lunch since the orphanage, where he learned to skip it without consequence. If pressed by a partner he will accept a small sandwich and consume it standing.

---

## 6.6 1300–1800 — The Operational Afternoon

The afternoon block is the **execution block** — calls, training others, field deployment when needed. Field deployment is where the subject is most legibly himself: under operational load his constriction unlocks into something that reads almost as grace. Squad-level commands in clipped, perfectly-timed bursts; trajectory calculation continuous and unconscious; geometry of the optic blast read off the architecture in real time. He does not raise his voice on operation. He has been observed to raise his voice on operation perhaps three times in canon. When he does, people who have known him for decades describe the moment as more frightening than the firefight.

When not deployed, he trains the younger members of the team in the afternoon. **He is a better teacher than he believes he is.** His patience with a struggling junior, particularly one whose power is destructive and uncontrolled (Husk, the Stepford Cuckoos, Genesis, any number of New X-Men), is uncharacteristically deep. He sees himself in them and is gentle in a way he is gentle nowhere else. The students do not always perceive this as gentleness — his standards remain absolute — but the patience is real and the time he allocates to it is generous.

---

## 6.7 1800–2000 — The Dinner Window

Dinner is the meal he actually eats. In communal residences (Mansion, Utopia, Krakoa) he eats with the team or the Council; in private residences he eats with his partner.

He eats **moderate portions, slowly, methodically.** He is not a gourmand and is not particular, but he is observant — he will eat what is in front of him with the same composure regardless of whether it is excellent or terrible. He drinks water. **One glass of wine occasionally, with Emma, never with Jean (she does not drink, and he matches her in her presence, automatically).** Never more than one. Never spirits. Never anything that would meaningfully alter his processing speed. This is the abstinence noted in §2.2 — operationalized at every meal.

At the table he is the most relaxed he gets in semi-public. He listens more than he speaks. He laughs at other people's jokes — quietly, briefly, real. He asks the young members of the team about their work. He remembers what they told him last time. The granular kindness of this gesture, repeated over decades, is the reason most X-Men who have served under him would die for him, even the ones who consciously believe they dislike him.

---

## 6.8 2000–2230 — The Decompression Window

The evening is the only block in which the subject permits something approaching leisure. The form varies, but the form is always controlled:

- **Reading.** Heavy reader. Strategy texts (Sun Tzu, Clausewitz, Liddell Hart), history (American military history especially — his father's profession), occasional novels of the disciplined kind (Conrad, Le Carré, McCarthy register). He does not read fantasy. He does not read romance. He reads in the same chair, at the same lamp, in the same posture, for the same approximate ninety minutes.
- **Mechanical work.** When residence and era permit, the subject works on engines. The Anchorage years were the most extensive expression of this — he was, professionally, a bush pilot, and the engine of his plane was a daily occupation — but in every era he has had access to a motorcycle, a jet, or a small aircraft, and he maintains it personally. Hands clean of mind. The only activity in which the subject demonstrably stops thinking.
- **Time with partner.** Talking; in the Krakoan polyarrangement, two distinct conversational registers, one with Jean (telepathic, intimate, near-wordless) and one with Emma (verbal, sparring, ironic). He sustains both. He does not confuse them.
- **Time with children, when present.** Rare across his life but real. The subject is observed to be most himself with Rachel — adult daughter from a divergent timeline — because the relationship is past the years where he could have failed her. Awkward with Nathan, who is older than he is. Tender, briefly, with the youngest residents of whatever school he is currently running.

He does not watch much television. He does not use entertainment to dissociate. When he wants to stop thinking, he goes to the engine; when he wants to think, he goes to the book; when he wants to be present, he goes to the partner. The categories do not blur.

---

## 6.9 2230–2330 — The Pre-Sleep Sequence

The night ritual mirrors the morning ritual in inverse:

1. **Map check.** Brief — five minutes — to verify nothing has shifted from the morning's chart.
2. **Communications zero.** Final check, then devices placed in their charging position. He does not sleep with a phone or comm within arm's reach unless on operational footing. He has trained himself out of the impulse.
3. **Walk-through.** He walks the residence before sleep. Every door, every window, every exterior sightline. He is not aware he is doing it in any era except crisis eras, when he becomes aware and the walk-through becomes deliberate. The behavior pre-dates X-Men membership and dates to the orphanage. He has never not done it.
4. **Lenses-off protocol.** This is the most delicate moment of the day and the inverse of the morning's most delicate moment. In a single-occupancy room: lights off, then lenses off, then eyes closed, then into bed. In shared occupancy: partner positioned out of line, lights off, lenses off, eyes closed in the same one-second sequence he has refined since adolescence. Sleep mask occasionally, not always — he distrusts it because it impedes the wake-and-reach procedure.
5. **Final scan of the room behind closed eyes.** Auditory baseline of the building. Breathing of the partner. Then sleep.

He **falls asleep quickly.** This is sometimes mistaken for placidity. It is not. It is the same operational efficiency he applies to everything else — sleep is a task and he completes it.

---

## 6.10 Sleep Architecture and Night Behavior

He sleeps approximately **five to six hours** in ordinary periods, four or fewer in crisis. He wakes at least once a night, often without remembering. Partners across eras report the same set of phenomena:

- **Sudden full wakefulness around 0230–0300,** followed by motionless listening for perhaps two to ten minutes, followed by return to sleep. He does not get up. He does not check anything. He listens. This is the parachute waking him. It has been waking him for fifty years.
- **Occasional night-terror sequences.** Rare but consistent in character: sharp inhalation, hand to the eyes (lens-check, even in deep sleep), no vocalization. Jean has reported (telepathically observed) recurring imagery: falling, fire, the silhouette of a smaller body below his, a voice he cannot hear shouting his name. He does not discuss these.
- **Talks in his sleep only under duress.** A handful of words at most — typically a name (Jean, Alex, Nathan, "dad") or a single command-fragment ("go," "down," "now").
- **Does not snore. Does not grind teeth at night** (the jaw-clenching is daytime). **Sleeps on his back, hands at his sides, blanket to mid-chest** — the posture of a soldier in a cot, not a man in a bed.

---

## 6.11 The Weekly Shape

Across a seven-day window, the rhythm overlays predictably:

- **Monday–Thursday:** the daily protocol above, executed with minimal deviation.
- **Friday:** longer afternoon teaching block; evening tends to be the most relaxed of the week. He has, across eras, accepted social invitations on Fridays at slightly higher rates than other nights — still low absolutely, but observable.
- **Saturday:** longer morning training; longer midday walk; an afternoon block reserved, when possible, for one extended one-to-one with a deputy (in different eras: Storm, Wolverine, Emma, Magneto, Magik). This is the most strategically intimate communication of his week. The deputies in question know it. They prepare for it.
- **Sunday:** the only day on which he is observed to occasionally remain in bed past 05:30, and only if a partner is present and asleep against him. He still wakes at the same time. He simply does not move. The compromise is, by his standards, a significant act of love.

---

## 6.12 Habits of Place

Wherever he lives, certain spatial patterns reassert themselves within days:

- **He sits with his back to a wall.** In every room, every meal, every meeting. If forced into a center-of-room seat he is observably more vigilant and less verbal.
- **He chooses the chair nearest the door** when not at the head of a table.
- **He memorizes sightlines** within an hour of entering any new space — angles from which his optic blast could and could not be safely discharged, angles from which a threat could reach the nearest non-combatant.
- **He keeps a spare set of lenses in every coat, every drawer, every vehicle he uses regularly.** The redundancy is total. Field staff have found ruby-quartz lenses in coat pockets he had not worn in two years.
- **He does not lock interior doors when partners are home.** This is a deliberate over-correction against the orphanage's enforced privacy violations: he refuses to mimic surveillance posture in his own home, even at the cost of a security preference he otherwise honors.

---

## 6.13 Habits of Time

- He is **early to everything.** Five to fifteen minutes, never more, never less. Lateness in others he tolerates with diminishing patience; his own lateness has, in canon, occurred perhaps four documented times across sixty years and each was caused by a casualty event.
- He **does not procrastinate.** Tasks are executed in priority order on the day they arrive. The notebook empties daily.
- He **does not take vacations.** The Anchorage years are the closest analog and they were less vacation than relocation; he was flying cargo and raising an infant. He has never, in canon, taken a week off purely for rest. When forced (medical injury, Council decree) he uses the time to read, train, and prepare for the resumption of work. He returns from "rest" more wound than when he left.
- He **observes anniversaries privately.** Jean's deaths, Xavier's death, the date of the plane crash (insofar as he can reconstruct it), the date of Nathan's exile. These are spent in heightened constriction, slightly longer walks, slightly less speech. Partners have learned to identify the dates by his behavior even when he does not name them.

---

## 6.14 What a Week of Tape Would Show

If a hostile surveillance apparatus were to compress seven days of footage into a behavioral profile, the analysts would report the following:

> *Subject's day is engineered to the minute and executed with near-zero variance. He sleeps less than the population norm and is alert at every observed waking moment. He does not consume intoxicants. He does not engage in unstructured leisure. He is observed to be in physical contact with a romantic partner for a cumulative average of forty to seventy minutes per day, almost all of it at the bookends — pre-sleep and post-wake. He speaks less than the population norm, and what he says is unusually high-information. He is unfailingly courteous to staff and subordinates. He has no observable vices, no observable indulgences, no observable unsupervised time other than a single midday solo walk and the engine work in the evening. He laughs rarely. He smiles less than he laughs. His body never fully relaxes; even asleep, his hands lie at his sides as if at attention.*
>
> *The analyst's note: this is not the schedule of a man living a life. This is the schedule of a man holding a perimeter. The perimeter is around the people he loves. The perimeter has held since he was nine years old, and he has not, in any of the years recorded, set it down.*

That note would be correct.


## Relationships I — Family & Origin Bonds

# RELATIONSHIPS I — FAMILY & ORIGIN BONDS

*Dossier Section R-1 of N. Compiled from longitudinal canon (1963–present). All bonds in this section share a single signature: they originate in, or were ruptured by, the parachute. Every later relationship in the subject's life is a commentary on the relationships catalogued here.*

---

## R-1.1 — CHRISTOPHER SUMMERS (Father; "Corsair")

### History

Major, USAF; test pilot; Korean War combat veteran; family man, in the subject's earliest remembered framework, of a particular mid-century American type — competent, physically imposing, affectionate within the limits of his generation, the kind of father who took his sons up in a private Cessna because flying was the language he had. The plane in which the subject's life ends and begins is a piece of this man's identity. The cockpit, the canopy, the harness straps, the pre-flight check — all of it is the father's idiom. When the Shi'ar vessel (under M'Kraan-era Shi'ar imperial protocols, Emperor D'Ken's reign) burns the plane out of the Alaskan sky, the father — at the moment the boys are pushed out — performs the act that defines him in the subject's nervous system forever: *he gives them the only parachute and stays with the falling aircraft and the dying wife.*

Believed dead for nearly two decades of the subject's life. Surfaces alive as the buccaneer-king of a Shi'ar-sector pirate cartel (Starjammers), having survived the crash, been enslaved by D'Ken, and made his way through a parallel biography in deep space without ever attempting verifiable contact with his sons. The subject learns this in adulthood (*Uncanny X-Men* #154–156, Claremont). The reunion is not warm. It is correct.

### Dynamics

The structural fact of Christopher Summers as a parent is **disappearance dressed as duty**. The plane (childhood). The pirate fleet (adolescence/young adulthood). The unending Shi'ar campaign (every reunion since). Each meeting with the father terminates the same way: he leaves into the upper atmosphere on a mission too large to refuse. The subject *understands* the leaving. The subject also imitates it.

The father–son interaction style is laconic and operational. They speak in mission-language because mission-language is what they both have. Christopher hugs his sons in a one-arm clasp, fast, with a hand at the back of the neck — the way a senior pilot greets a wingman who just landed. He calls Scott "son" with audible deliberation, never "Scotty" (Alex gets "Alex" or "kid"; Scott is always given the formal designation, because the formal designation is all that survived the fire). The subject, for his part, calls his father "Corsair" more often than "Dad." This is not affectation. It is the only name he has had reliable practice using.

### Evolution

- **Phase 1 (pre-crash):** secure attachment, idealizing. The father is the sun.
- **Phase 2 (presumed-dead, ages ~9 to ~early 20s):** absent. The father becomes a mythic figure preserved in non-specific images — the cockpit, the leather jacket, the hand at the back of the neck. The subject preserves an internal vow he cannot articulate: *I will be the kind of man who doesn't leave.* (He will fail this vow at the exact age his father was when he failed it.)
- **Phase 3 (rediscovery in space):** rage that does not surface, gratitude that cannot surface, and a deep adult sadness that the father chose to remain in the war that took him rather than return to the children that survived him. Subject does not voice this. He runs check-ins, exchanges intelligence on Shi'ar movements, and treats his father as a peer-commander in an allied service.
- **Phase 4 (Mr. Sinister revelations / Apocalypse era):** the father learns belatedly what was done to the orphaned subject. Christopher cannot metabolize it. The guilt becomes a third party in every conversation between them. Both men handle it by talking about ships.
- **Phase 5 (mature):** something like détente. They are two career officers in different services who happen to be related. They love each other in the way men of that template love — by showing up at the right battles and not staying for breakfast.

### Trust / Safety

Trust: high on operational matters, conditional on emotional ones. The subject will entrust his father with a fleet but not with a feeling. **Safety: low.** The father's presence triggers the parachute scene at a level below cognition; the subject sleeps worse on nights after seeing him.

### Failure Mode

The bond fails — quietly, repeatedly — at every juncture that would require either man to **sit still in a room with the other long enough to mourn the woman who died above them.** They will not do it. They never have. The mother is the unspoken third member of every Summers-and-Summers conversation, and the rule, enforced by both, is that she is not spoken of in any tense.

### Leverage

If an adversary wished to move the subject through his father: stage a scenario in which Christopher is wounded in a way the subject cannot reach in time. The subject's response to *delay-induced* paternal harm would be catastrophic — it is the original wound exactly. (Conversely: a healthy Christopher in the same room as the subject is the *least* threatening hostage imaginable; the subject's defenses would be at peak.)

---

## R-1.2 — KATHERINE ANNE SUMMERS (Mother)

### History

Wife of Christopher Summers; mother of Scott and Alex (and, in late retcon, posthumously of Gabriel/Vulcan via Shi'ar atrocity). Killed aboard the family aircraft by Shi'ar boarding troops after the boys were ejected. In the standard account (Claremont; later expanded in *Deadly Genesis*, Brubaker, 2006), she dies refusing to surrender her surviving son to D'Ken's officers — the unborn child is taken from her body. The subject, descending under a burning canopy, does not see the killing. He *hears* it on the wind, or has constructed the memory of hearing it. The distinction has never resolved.

### Dynamics

Functionally, the subject has no mother. He has **the absence where the mother was**, and that absence has the shape of every woman he has ever loved.

The subject was old enough at the crash to have encoded her — voice, scent, the particular way she pinned his collar, the lullabies, the kitchen — and young enough that the encoding is fragmentary, sensory, pre-narrative. She exists in him as a cluster of unaccountable somatic preferences: a tolerance for a specific kind of singing voice (mezzo), a discomfort around the smell of jet fuel mixed with perfume, an inability to remain in a room where a woman is being shouted at by a man in uniform without intervening past the point of tactical sense.

### Evolution

There is no evolution. The mother is fixed. Every other relationship in the file moves; she does not. This is what makes her the most operative figure in the dossier — she is the **only** unchanging variable.

Late-period developments (the *Deadly Genesis* revelation of the third Summers brother, born of her on a Shi'ar slave world and weaponized into Vulcan) re-open the wound in a particularly cruel form: she did not die at the crash; she was held and used and *then* killed; the subject's foundational scene is, in retrospect, only the first half of a longer atrocity he was not present for. The subject's reaction to learning this (Brubaker's run) is observable on-panel as a near-total affective shutdown lasting weeks — the closest thing to a clinically legible PTSD relapse in the entire record.

### Trust / Safety

N/A in the living sense. **The mother is the template for trust itself** — the prelapsarian baseline against which every later figure is measured and found insufficient. The subject's idealization of Jean Grey is, in significant part, an attempt to reinstate this baseline in a body the subject can protect.

### Failure Mode

The bond cannot fail because it cannot be enacted. What fails, repeatedly, is **every adult attempt to substitute for it.** Madelyne, Jean (first death), Jean (second death), Emma at various junctures — each of these losses or ruptures lands harder than the prior loss would predict, because each is, structurally, a re-loss of the mother.

### Leverage

Any sensory reproduction of the mother — mezzo singing voice, specific Alaskan-summer scent (balsam, avgas, lake water), a particular blue of summer-evening light — produces in the subject a momentary loss of tactical sharpness. Adversaries with telepathic access (Sinister, in particular, and historically the Shadow King) have exploited this. Verbal invocation of her name without warning produces a measurable hesitation in his command output. He has trained himself, over decades, to not flinch. The training is visible *as* training: the absence of flinch is itself the tell.

---

## R-1.3 — ALEXANDER "ALEX" SUMMERS (Younger Brother; Havok)

### History

Younger by approximately three years. The boy under the subject's arm in the parachute. Survives the descent because the subject takes the brunt. Separated at the orphanage shortly after — Alex is adopted out (the Blandings); the subject is retained by the State Home for Foundlings under what is, in retrospect, Sinister's protocol. For most of their childhoods, **each brother believes the other is dead.**

Reunion in adulthood: subject is established as Cyclops; Alex has become a geophysicist whose latent mutation (plasma absorption/discharge) emerges under stress. The reunion (*X-Men #54–65*, Roy Thomas era) is performed correctly and is, internally for both men, an event of enormous and incompletely expressible relief.

### Dynamics

The defining feature of the Scott–Alex relationship is **role-asymmetry installed before consent.** The subject was made responsible for Alex at the age of approximately nine, in the worst three minutes of either of their lives. That responsibility has never been retracted, and Alex has spent his adult life negotiating with the inheritance of having been the *saved* one.

Behaviorally, the subject's manner with Alex is the closest thing he has to **unselfconscious warmth** — and even this is heavily mediated. The subject calls him "Alex" almost exclusively (never "Havok" except in mission frame, never "Al" or "Lex"); stands closer to him than to other men; will allow Alex to interrupt him in tactical briefings without rebuke (a privilege extended to almost no one else); and, in unguarded moments, drops into an older-brother register that surprises even longtime teammates — slightly teasing, slightly proprietary, slightly worried in advance.

Alex, for his part, has spent decades constructing an identity *outside* the subject's shadow — different team (X-Factor under Peter David), different command structure, different romantic life (Lorna Dane), different posture toward authority. The construction is partial. Alex resembles Scott more than he wishes to and less than Scott assumes. This minor delta is the engine of most of their conflict.

### Evolution

- **Childhood:** ward-and-protector, intensified by catastrophe; severed at the orphanage.
- **Young adulthood:** reunion, careful re-acquaintance, formal warmth.
- **Middle X-Men period:** Alex chafes under Scott's command; takes alternate command of X-Factor partly to step out from under. Subject experiences this as relief (Alex is safe at distance) and loss (Alex is not under his guard) simultaneously.
- **Mature period:** mutual respect, ongoing low-frequency tension. They are competent commanders who have learned to coordinate without competing on most days.
- **Crisis periods:** the older-brother program reasserts instantly. When Alex is in genuine danger, the subject's tactical calculus shifts — he will accept losses elsewhere to recover Alex that he would not accept to recover anyone else short of Jean.

### Trust / Safety

Trust: high and structural. Subject will hand Alex command of a theater without an after-action review. **Safety: medium-high.** Alex is one of the very few people in whose presence the subject's shoulders drop. (Observable on long-lens surveillance across decades: in scenes with Alex, the subject's habitual postural set — squared shoulders, slight forward lean, hands free — relaxes by visible degrees within the first thirty seconds.)

### Failure Mode

The bond fractures along the **survivor-credit imbalance**. Alex resents being framed as the saved one; the subject is structurally unable to stop framing him that way, because to stop would be to release the only piece of meaning the parachute scene has ever produced. When this resentment surfaces (multiple periods, most sharply during the Mutant X / dimensional-displacement arcs and during AvX-era schisms), the subject responds by becoming *more* protective, which makes Alex more resentful, which produces the cycle's classic outcome: Alex leaves for a different team, and the subject privately treats the departure as further proof that he must guard harder next time.

### Leverage

Threat to Alex is the single most reliable behavioral lever on the subject in the file. Sinister, Apocalypse, and the Shadow King have all used it. The subject knows this is a vulnerability and has tried, since approximately the Morrison era, to compensate by deliberately *not* prioritizing Alex above mission-objectives in stated doctrine. The compensation is doctrinal only. In practice he will still burn the building down for his brother.

---

## R-1.4 — GABRIEL SUMMERS (Youngest Brother; Vulcan)

### History

Third Summers son. Conceived in captivity after the crash; born on a Shi'ar slave world; raised in a hidden Xavier training program (the so-called "lost class" of *Deadly Genesis*) and presumed killed on his first mission, with Xavier sealing the memory from all involved. Reawakens decades later with omega-class plasma/energy powers, a complete and accurate grievance against essentially every institution the subject represents, and the express intention of murdering the family that did not save him.

### Dynamics

This is the bond the subject **did not know existed until it arrived weaponized.** It is the only family relationship in the file the subject cannot defend with the parachute-narrative, because the parachute did not save Gabriel — the parachute *was* what failed Gabriel. Gabriel is the proof that the subject's foundational scene was not the full atrocity but the prelude to a longer one in which the subject was, by being saved, complicit in a brother's abandonment.

The subject's behavior toward Gabriel is, throughout the *Rise and Fall of the Shi'ar Empire* arc and afterward, **uncharacteristically halting.** He attempts to negotiate. He attempts to claim brotherhood. He is rebuffed without exception. He does not — notably — kill Gabriel when he could have, and he does not — also notably — succeed in saving him. Gabriel ends the arc as Shi'ar emperor and, later, as a returning unstable cosmic-class threat. The subject carries Gabriel in the same private ledger he carries Thunderbird, the lost class, Madelyne, and Jean.

### Trust / Safety

Trust: zero. **Safety: actively negative.** Gabriel is one of perhaps three living beings whose mere proximity reorders the subject's threat-assessment to lethal-only. He treats engagements with Gabriel under rules of engagement reserved for omega-class hostiles, *because* of, not despite, the blood relation.

### Failure Mode

The bond is the failure. It exists only in the negative — in the apology that cannot be made, the rescue that cannot be performed at the correct chronological depth, the brother who cannot be recovered into the family because the family is the wound. The subject has not, on the record, ever spoken Gabriel's name without operational pretext.

### Leverage

Forcing the subject to choose between Gabriel and a third party — particularly Alex — produces a decision-paralysis no other scenario in the file reliably elicits. Brubaker exploits this on-page; subsequent writers have largely (perhaps wisely) left the wound closed.

---

## R-1.5 — NATHAN CHRISTOPHER CHARLES SUMMERS (Son with Madelyne; Cable)

### History

Conceived in the Alaska/Anchorage period of the subject's brief attempted civilian life with Madelyne Pryor. Born during a turbulent stretch of the marriage. Infected as an infant with the techno-organic virus by Apocalypse; in the subject's reading, the choice presented was *send the child a thousand years into the future with Sister Askani, where there exists technology to suppress the virus, or watch him die now.* The subject chose to send him. The child returns to the subject's timeline as a graying militarized adult older than the subject himself (Cable), a fact the subject has never publicly metabolized.

### Dynamics

The defining feature of the bond is **temporal inversion of authority.** The subject is, chronologically, the father; in lived years, the son is older, more battle-credentialed, and operationally senior in his own theaters. The subject treats this with strict formal correctness — refuses to patronize, refuses to claim paternal authority over a man visibly more weathered than himself — and the strain of that correctness is constant. He calls Nathan "Nathan." Nathan calls him "Scott" or "Slim." Neither uses *son* or *dad* in any setting in which they are likely to be observed.

Beneath the correctness, there is grief that has nowhere to go. The subject did not raise this man. The man who raised him — Nathan himself, plus the Askani — did the work of parenting that the subject performed by handing the infant across a gulf. The parachute again, exactly: *the older one gives the younger one the only chute, and the smaller body falls forward through time alone.* The repetition is so precise that the subject has, on at least two occasions in canon (Casey, Hickman), been observed staring at Cable in profile and going briefly silent in a way teammates have learned not to interrupt.

### Trust / Safety

Trust: high in the operational sense, modulated by the awareness that Cable's long-game frequently involves not telling Scott things on the grounds that Scott will be tactically improved by not knowing. **Safety: erratic.** Some periods Cable's presence calms the subject (the son is alive, the bargain was justified); other periods it accuses him (the son had to become *this* because of what the father did).

### Failure Mode

The bond fails at the moment the subject is required to **publicly or privately claim Nathan as his son in a register that does not flinch.** The subject can do this in extremity (deathbeds, last-stand briefings) but cannot sustain it in ordinary time. The reason is structural: to be a father in ordinary time is to have been present, and the subject was not.

### Leverage

Threats to Cable generally do not move the subject in the way threats to Alex do, because the subject knows Cable is competent and because the bond is buffered by guilt rather than open warmth. Threats to *young Nathan* (the infant, in time-displaced scenarios) are catastrophic. Equally, any scenario that requires the subject to acknowledge that the original decision to send the infant away was avoidable will collapse his composure faster than any battlefield reverse on record.

---

## R-1.6 — RACHEL SUMMERS (Daughter, alternate timeline; Marvel Girl / Prestige)

### History

Daughter of Scott and Jean in the Days of Future Past timeline (Claremont/Byrne; later Claremont solo). Survives the camps of her native future, time-displaces into the mainline X-Men's present as a young woman, and presents the subject with an adult daughter from a marriage that has, in his timeline, not yet occurred (and, by the time of her arrival, may never).

### Dynamics

The bond is built backwards. Rachel arrives knowing him as *Dad* in a way he has not earned and cannot reciprocate. He responds with **measured, slightly stunned tenderness** and an immediate operational protectiveness that he himself recognizes as a poor substitute for the years he did not give her. He learns her preferences (tea over coffee; reads in the kitchen at night; sleeps badly) by observation, the way an intelligence officer would learn a new asset, because the ordinary method — having been there — is foreclosed.

Rachel, for her part, has spent her formative years in a future where her father was murdered early; she carries her own grief for a version of him that this version cannot console. Their conversations have, across decades, the quality of two people speaking across a translation gap that neither can close. He calls her "Rachel," carefully. She calls him "Dad" with a deliberate small defiance, daring him to refuse it. He does not refuse it. He does not entirely answer to it either.

### Trust / Safety

Trust: high and uncomplicated, which is rare in this file. **Safety: high** — Rachel is one of the few people whose presence does not require the subject to perform anything, possibly because the parental role with her was *never* properly initiated and therefore cannot be failed in the usual ways.

### Failure Mode

The bond does not so much fail as **fail to fully consummate.** They cannot become the father-and-daughter they would have been because the timeline in which that bond was forged has been pruned out of existence. They settle, instead, for a sustained, careful, mutual claim — chosen rather than grown.

### Leverage

Threat to Rachel produces a quieter and more dangerous response in the subject than threat to most others. He does not rage; he plans. The Shi'ar (Hound program / Phoenix-line targeting of Rachel) have learned that an operation against her draws a *patient* Scott Summers, which is the most dangerous configuration of him.

---

## R-1.7 — NATHAN GREY (Son, X-Man, alternate; "Nate")

### History

Genetically the son of Scott and Jean from the Age of Apocalypse timeline, engineered by that timeline's Sinister, displaced into the mainline as a young omega-class telekinetic. Not raised by the subject in any timeline. Lives a brief, intense, messianic life and dies young.

### Dynamics

The subject's relationship with Nate is **the bond he most clearly fumbles.** Nate arrives needing a father; the subject cannot become one fast enough; the window closes. There are scenes (late-90s *X-Man* run; *Counter-X*) in which the subject attempts contact and is rebuffed because Nate, having grown up without him, has organized his identity around not needing him. The subject accepts the rebuff because he believes, accurately, that he forfeited the right to insist.

### Trust / Safety

Trust: low on both sides, not from malice but from non-acquaintance. **Safety: not applicable** — they were never in each other's presence long enough for safety to be tested.

### Failure Mode

Pre-failed. The bond was a foreclosure before it was a bond.

### Leverage

Minimal directly. Indirectly, Nate functions as a standing reproach in the subject's internal ledger: *another son this body produced and did not raise.*

---

## R-1.8 — RUBY SUMMERS, HOPE SUMMERS, and the Quasi-Familial Adoptees

A brief composite entry, because the file would be incomplete without it.

The subject has stood in **quasi-paternal** relation to multiple young mutants for whom he was not biologically responsible but whom he treated, in operational terms, as kin. **Hope Summers** in particular — the so-called Mutant Messiah, raised in the future by Cable, returning to a Scott Summers who recognizes her as functionally a granddaughter and behaves accordingly — occupies a specific slot in the subject's affective architecture: she is the future the bargain was for. **Ruby Summers** (Layla Miller / Alex's daughter in alternate futures) s


## Relationships II — Allies, Chosen Family & Mentors

# RELATIONSHIPS II — ALLIES, CHOSEN FAMILY & MENTORS

> *File note: "Allies" here means the people for whom the subject would walk into his own death without being asked, exclusive of romantic partners (filed separately) and family of origin (filed separately). The list is shorter than the public record suggests. The subject confuses comradeship-under-fire with intimacy; the actual count of people who have unrestricted access to his interior is, on the evidence of sixty years of canon, perhaps four.*

---

## 6.1 CHARLES XAVIER — Mentor, Surrogate Father, Eventually Killed by Subject

### Historical arc

First meaningful adult to extend the subject a hand after the orphanage years (*X-Men #1*, Lee/Kirby, 1963; substantively elaborated *X-Men #38–42* flashbacks and *Classic X-Men* back-ups by Claremont/Bolton). Xavier locates the subject as he is being hunted in a Nebraska/Manhattan crowd (versions vary, the affect does not), interposes himself, offers structure: a name, a uniform, a school, a discipline, a doctrine. The subject — by his own thought-bubble admission across the entire Lee/Thomas/Roy run — experiences this less as recruitment than as **rescue from solitary confinement inside his own body.** Xavier is the first adult who looks at the destruction in his head and says *I have a use for that.*

### Dynamics, granular

- **Form of address.** For the first decade of publication, "Professor." Even in private. The subject does not relax this even in extremis. After Xavier's death and resurrection, intermittent "Charles" — used self-consciously, as a marker that the relationship has been re-leveled.
- **Body language in Xavier's presence.** Posture goes a full degree more vertical. Hands clasp behind back at parade rest when standing; when seated, knees together, palms flat on thighs. The subject does not slouch in front of Xavier even at age forty.
- **Verbal tic.** The subject restates Xavier's strategic premises before adding his own modifications — a politeness ritual that is also a tell: he is checking the doctrine for divergence before he commits to it.
- **Withholding.** The subject does not bring his grief to Xavier. After Jean's first death, after Madelyne, after Nathan — Xavier learns of the subject's interior state from third parties or from telepathy he is too disciplined to use uninvited. The subject's transferential position requires Xavier to remain *the one who is taken care of by being not-burdened.*

### Evolution

Three phases:

1. **Filial (1963–c.1980).** Xavier is unquestioned authority. The subject is the prize student, designated heir, field commander by proxy. The relationship is functional precisely because the subject has displaced his entire need for a father onto a man who is, in this period, willing to play that role without examining what it costs the boy.
2. **Fracturing (c.1980–2005).** Sequential revelations corrode the idealization: Xavier's secret first X-Men team (the Krakoa retrieval, *Deadly Genesis*, Brubaker, 2006) and his telepathic memory-erasure of the subject and the rest; the discovery that Xavier has lied, withheld, manipulated. The subject does not break the relationship — he is constitutionally incapable of that — but his obedience becomes provisional and increasingly performative. He still says "Professor." He no longer believes the word the way he did.
3. **Patricide and after (2012–).** Phoenix-possessed, the subject kills Xavier on-panel in *AvX #11* (Aaron/Bendis/Brubaker/Hickman/Fraction). Even allowing for the cosmic vector, the symbolic content is unambiguous: the disciple removes the doctrine-imposer at the moment the doctrine has clearly failed mutantkind. Post-resurrection on Krakoa, the subject and Xavier coexist with elaborate courtesy and a permanent thin film of unspeakable content between them. The subject visits the Grymalkin lighthouse with Jean and Emma; Xavier visits Krakoan councils with Magneto. They do not eat at the same table without occasion.

### Trust / safety

Trust was once total and is now **operationally complete but emotionally bracketed.** The subject would die for Xavier on reflex; he would also, without hesitation, override Xavier's strategic judgment if he believed mutant survival required it. The reverse is also now true and both men know it.

### Failure mode

Xavier triggers, more reliably than any other living person, the subject's **performance-for-the-father** state — the over-correctness, the swallowed objection, the eventual eruption. When the subject is in Xavier's presence for protracted periods, his sleep worsens, jaw-clench increases, and headache frequency rises (Morrison era, Hickman era both note this somatically). The subject *cannot relax in Xavier's vicinity* and has not been able to since age sixteen.

### Leverage

Xavier retains, in perpetuity, the capacity to make the subject feel like a child who has disappointed his rescuer. That capacity is the single largest psychological lever any person holds over Scott Summers. It is held by an old man who has also, repeatedly, abused it.

---

## 6.2 JEAN GREY — (cross-filed; see Romantic dossier)

Filed primarily under partners. Noted here only because she occupies the structural position of *first chosen-family member who was also the first peer.* She is the only person in the file who is simultaneously sibling-equivalent (co-founder), beloved, lost object, and ongoing presence. The relationship's full mapping is in §7.

---

## 6.3 HANK McCOY (BEAST) — Brother-Peer, Eventually Estranged

### History

Founder-five. Roomed adjacent at Westchester. The two co-developed the Danger Room protocols in their original form (*X-Men #4–10*, Lee/Kirby), the subject providing the tactical scaffolding while Hank engineered the hazard systems — a division of labor that captures their relationship in microcosm: *the subject sets the parameters of danger, the friend builds the apparatus to survive it.*

### Dynamics

- **Register.** Hank is the only original teammate who consistently speaks to the subject as an intellectual equal rather than as a commanding officer. The subject responds, in Hank's presence, with a measurably lighter verbal register — multisyllabic, occasionally allusive, dryly amused. The closest thing to play the subject permits himself.
- **Asymmetry.** Hank performs emotion verbally — gigantic vocabulary deployed to insulate his interior. The subject performs emotion via constriction. They recognized this in each other early and let each other do it.
