- **Touch.** Hank is one of perhaps three living people the subject permits to touch his shoulder without flinch (the others: Jean; Alex, conditionally). Hank knows this and uses it sparingly.

### Evolution

Friendship survives X-Factor, survives both deaths of Jean, survives Hank's secondary mutation. **Schism breaks it.** Hank sides with Wolverine on the arming-of-children question (*X-Men: Schism*, Aaron, 2011) and the subject reads this — accurately — as the brother he respected most refusing to follow him into the moral grey he believed was necessary. The estrangement deepens through *AvX* (Hank actively works against Phoenix-possessed Scott) and through Hank's own subsequent moral collapse (the time-displaced original five, the Krakoan-era Hank-of-X-Force atrocities, *X-Force* Percy run, 2019–2022).

By the contemporary period, the subject regards Hank with **the specific grief one reserves for a friend who has done worse things than oneself while believing oneself the moral one.** No longer touches Hank's shoulder. Speaks to him in operational register only.

### Trust / safety

Was once near-total; now zero on strategic matters, residual on personal ones. The subject would still pull Hank from a fire. He would not tell Hank anything he did not want broadcast.

### Failure mode

Hank's failure-with-Scott was to mistake the subject's hardening for villainy in 2011, and to therefore commit himself to opposition just as the subject most needed peer-checking from within his confidence. The subject's failure-with-Hank was to assume that intellectual partnership in their twenties guaranteed moral alliance in their forties; he did not maintain the friendship across the period when it would have done either of them any good.

### Leverage

Negligible now. The lever Hank used to hold has been corroded by Hank's own subsequent record.

---

## 6.4 WARREN WORTHINGTON III (ANGEL/ARCHANGEL) — The Patrician Brother

### History

Founder-five. Of the original team, the one the subject understood least and protected most. Warren's wealth, glibness, and surface arrogance read as foreign matter to the Nebraska-orphan subject; the protectiveness was nevertheless real, perhaps because Warren — beneath the patrician costume — was the only other founder with a genuinely traumatic body relationship (the wings he hid, later lost, replaced, mutated).

### Dynamics

- The subject treats Warren with formal courtesy and quiet vigilance. Watches Warren's flight patterns in combat for fatigue tells. Will, without comment, position himself in any room such that Warren's exit is unblocked — a kindness Warren has never named and the subject has never explained.
- Apocalypse-touched Warren (Archangel arcs, Simonson/Liefeld, 1990; revisited in *Uncanny X-Force*, Remender, 2010–2012) is, for the subject, a permanent grief. The transformation of his oldest teammate by Apocalypse pre-figures his own (Twelve arc) and the subject's empathy with Warren post-Archangel is unusually unguarded. They do not discuss it. They know.

### Evolution

Less broken than Hank's, less consequential than Logan's. The relationship has the durability of a thing rarely tested at high pressure. Warren defected to Hank's side at Schism; the subject took this as expected and apolitical, and did not hold it.

### Trust / Failure mode / Leverage

Trust: cordial, capped. Failure mode: subject under-invests in the friendship because Warren reads as resilient and self-contained; Warren has, more than once, been less so than the subject assumed. Leverage: low. Warren has never tried to use any.

---

## 6.5 BOBBY DRAKE (ICEMAN) — The Little Brother The Subject Forgot To Notice Growing Up

### History

Founder-five. Youngest original. The team clown. The subject's first command responsibility — Bobby was fifteen when the team formed, the subject seventeen, and the two-year gap was, in the field, an eternity of executive distance.

### Dynamics

- The subject's posture toward Bobby is permanently older-brotherly in a way the subject would deny if asked. Tone shifts paternal — corrective without contempt, indulgent of jokes the subject does not laugh at.
- Bobby is one of the few teammates around whom the subject's micro-expressions are visible without engineering: a slight mouth-quirk at a Drake quip, a sigh at a Drake failure of judgment. The subject does not bother to conceal affect around Bobby because the subject has classified Bobby as someone to be protected rather than read.
- **This classification has been wrong for thirty publication years and the subject has never updated it.** Bobby is one of the omega-tier mutants on the planet (Morrison-era retcon onward). The subject has never strategically deployed Bobby at full capability because the subject still sees him as the kid in the parka.

### Evolution

Bobby's late-life coming out (Bendis, *All-New X-Men* 2015) registered on the subject (the time-displaced original-five Scott was present; the resurrected adult subject received the data afterward) as: *of course; I should have noticed; I did not because I do not notice this kind of thing about anyone, including myself.* Treats Bobby with no change in register, which is — for Bobby — the correct response.

### Failure mode

Subject's chronic underestimate of Bobby's power and depth. Bobby's failure-with-Scott is to have accepted being underestimated for so long that it became the shape of the friendship.

### Leverage

Bobby retains the ability to make the subject laugh, briefly, against his will. This is a rarer power than any optic blast.

---

## 6.6 ALEX SUMMERS (HAVOK) — (cross-filed; family-of-origin)

Filed primarily under Family. Mentioned here because the brother-as-comrade dimension is operationally distinct: in the field the subject defers to Havok's wave-mechanics for area denial and treats him as a junior commander rather than a sibling. The dissonance — *brother in the locker room, lieutenant in the briefing* — is one of the few interpersonal contradictions the subject has not engineered into a stable defense.

---

## 6.7 LOGAN / JAMES HOWLETT (WOLVERINE) — The Adversary-Brother

### History

Joined the second team (*Giant-Size X-Men #1*, Wein/Cockrum, 1975). Antagonistic from the first panel: a competitor for Jean's affection, a violator of the subject's command discipline, a smoker in his briefing room. The subject's initial position — *this man is a feral liability* — was the only response his trauma-organized character could produce to a peer who refused to submit to doctrine.

### Dynamics

- **Friction as the medium of intimacy.** Across forty-five publication years, the relationship's signal-carrying mechanism has been disagreement. They argue about tactics, ethics, women, cigars, and the moral status of killing; through these arguments they conduct an extensive mutual reading that neither would tolerate as direct address.
- **The subject's specific concession.** The subject permits Logan to smoke in his presence — the only person he permits this. This is not laxity; it is the subject acknowledging that Logan's nervous system requires the nicotine for self-regulation, and that asking him to suppress it would compromise field performance. The subject has thought about this. He has not said so to Logan.
- **The body-position tell.** In tactical meetings the subject seats himself such that he can see Logan without turning his head. This is not distrust; it is the recognition that Logan's body, which carries its own seismic data, is the most informative single instrument in the room about how a situation is going to go.
- **X-Force.** The subject's decision to convene a black-ops kill team (*X-Force*, Kyle/Yost, 2008) and to install Logan at its head is the subject's most intimate professional gesture toward another man in his entire file. He hands Logan the moral burden the subject has decided cannot be borne by anyone untrained in carrying it. Logan accepts. They do not discuss what it means that the subject knew Logan was the only person on Earth equipped to do this and unwilling to refuse.

### Evolution

1. **Antagonism (1975–c.1985).** Open rivalry. Jean is the proximate cause; doctrine is the distal one.
2. **Operational respect (1985–2008).** Subject grows into adulthood; Logan grows into reluctant institutional citizenship. They become the two men everyone else's safety depends on.
3. **Conspirator-trust (2008–2011).** X-Force years. The most intimate phase. Brief.
4. **Schism (2011).** Disagreement on child-soldiers shatters the operational alliance. Subject and Logan split mutantkind between them. The grief in this rupture is, for the subject, of a different category than the Hank rupture — Hank was the brother who *should* have understood; Logan was the brother who *did* understand and chose differently anyway. That second kind of refusal is unrecoverable.
5. **Post-resurrection / Krakoan era.** Coexistence with renewed but cautious functional collaboration. Neither restored to the X-Force level of trust.

### Trust / safety

Operationally near-total in combat — the subject would trust Logan with the lives of children, has done so, will again. Strategically guarded since Schism. Personally — the only person in this file other than Jean and Emma to whom the subject has, on the record, expressed something like a confession.

### Failure mode

The subject *needs* Logan's opposition to function. When Logan refuses to oppose him (during the X-Force years), the subject's authoritarian drift accelerates because the necessary external check is offline. When Logan opposes him at scale (Schism), the subject reads it as betrayal rather than the check he structurally requires. There is no stable position for Logan that the subject can sustainably tolerate.

### Leverage

Logan is one of perhaps three people in the file capable of changing the subject's mind by talking. He has used this capacity roughly four times in forty-five years and got results twice.

---

## 6.8 ORORO MUNROE (STORM) — Co-Sovereign, Conscience-Peer

### History

Joined the second team. From very early in the Claremont run the subject identified Storm as a successor-tier strategic mind and treated her accordingly. When the subject was depowered and exiled (*UXM #201*, 1986), Storm — also powerless at the time — defeated him in single combat for leadership. **The subject lost and was clearly relieved.** This is the single cleanest leadership transition in his career and it tells you what he most wanted from a peer: someone he could lose to without it being a catastrophe.

### Dynamics

- Subject addresses Storm by her chosen name (Ororo), in private and in operation. Granted this latitude very early; has never withdrawn it.
- In her presence the subject's verbal register loses some of its tactical clipping. He uses complete sentences with clause structure. He listens without rebutting until she has finished.
- Physical orientation: the subject orients his body toward Storm when she speaks. He does not do this for most people. For Xavier, yes; for Storm, yes; for Jean and Emma, yes; for almost no one else.
- **The subject treats Storm's judgment as a calibration instrument for his own.** When he is uncertain whether he has moved too far into the moral grey, he constructs the argument as if presenting it to her. If the argument fails the imaginary Storm, he revises the operation.

### Evolution

Co-equal across decades; co-sovereign in the Krakoan period. The Schism did not break them — Storm initially aligned with Logan's school but moved fluidly between camps with the subject's tacit blessing. The relationship has the rare quality, in this file, of having become *more* trusted over time rather than less.

### Trust / safety

The highest sustained trust the subject extends to any non-romantic adult. Storm is one of perhaps two people who can countermand him publicly without him interpreting it as challenge.

### Failure mode

Mutual failure mode is mutual deference: each respects the other's domain so absolutely that there are seams of operational territory neither manages, and bad actors have, historically, slipped through those seams. The subject's specific failure-with-Storm is to assume she does not require what other people require from him (reassurance, check-in, acknowledgment of cost); Storm has not always been as self-contained as the subject prefers to read her.

### Leverage

Storm holds, uniquely, the leverage of being someone whose disappointment the subject would not survive interpreting as betrayal — he would interpret it as evidence he had been wrong. This is the leverage Xavier had once and lost. Storm has it now and uses it with the restraint of someone who knows she has it.

---

## 6.9 KURT WAGNER (NIGHTCRAWLER) — The Conscience On The Other Side Of The Glass

### History

Second team. Of all founders' successors, the one whose temperament is most foreign to the subject's: theatrical, devout, joyous in the body, comfortable with paradox.

### Dynamics

- The subject is **measurably less defended around Kurt than around any other adult male in the file.** The reason is partly Kurt's transparent goodwill (the subject's pattern-recognition cannot find a hostile reading); partly Kurt's religious framework, which gives him language for the subject's guilt that the subject cannot otherwise hear.
- The subject has, on the record (Claremont, *UXM* late 1980s; revisited Aaron, *Amazing X-Men*, 2014), accepted Kurt's hand on his arm in moments of catastrophe. Permits Kurt to bless him in the Catholic register without protest. This is not faith; it is the subject permitting himself, briefly, to be held by a structure he does not have to architect.
- Kurt is one of the people the subject genuinely apologizes to. The list is short.

### Evolution

Steady. The friendship survived Kurt's death and resurrection, survived Schism (Kurt was dead for it, returned to find both his closest friends estranged), survived the contemporary period.

### Trust / safety

High; bounded only by the subject's general inability to disclose interior state to anyone other than Emma and Jean.

### Failure mode

The subject overprotects Kurt — categorizes him as a soul that the work should not be permitted to break. This has resulted, on at least one operation, in the subject withholding tactical information from Kurt on grounds of moral hygiene; Kurt has, correctly, named this as condescension.

### Leverage

Kurt can make the subject hesitate. No one else can make the subject hesitate without making him angry.

---

## 6.10 KITTY PRYDE / KATHERINE PRYDE — Protege, Then Peer, Then Estranged Daughter-Figure

### History

Recruited at thirteen (*UXM #129*, Claremont/Byrne, 1980). The subject was her field commander during her formative years on the team. The Claremont-era dynamic was, on the surface, fractious — Kitty resented the subject's command tone, the subject resented Kitty's adolescent challenges to it — but the deeper transaction was always: *this is what an attentive older mutant looks like; this is the thing I did not have at your age.*

### Dynamics

- The subject's tone with Kitty as a teenager was clipped, often impatient. Beneath: meticulous attention. He knew her phase-state at any given moment in a fight, knew the maximum mass she could phase through unmodified, knew the duration she could hold a phase before fatigue. He had run the numbers without anyone asking him to.
- As Kitty matured, the subject's posture shifted to peer — eventually subordinate, when Kitty took the Captaincy of one of the late-2010s Krakoan vessels (the *Marauder*, *Marauders*, Duggan, 2019).
- Subject has never been able to call her "Kate" without effort. The transition from "Kitty" tracks his own difficulty accepting that the children he protected have become adults who do not require his protection.

### Evolution

Mostly steady, with cooling during the AvX period (Kitty distanced from Phoenix-Five Scott) and warming on Krakoa.

### Trust / safety

High, asymmetrically. Kitty trusts the subject's competence absolutely and his judgment provisionally. The subject trusts Kitty completely and would defer to her on any operation involving the school.

### Failure mode

The subject keeps trying to protect Kitty from costs she has long since proven willing to bear. Kitty has, more than once, told him to stop doing this. He cannot.

### Leverage

Moderate. Kitty is in the small set of people whose criticism the subject takes as data rather than as attack.

---

## 6.11 RACHEL SUMMERS (PRESTIGE) — The Daughter From The Other Timeline

### History

Subject's daughter from the displaced *Days of Future Past*/Mojoverse timeline, present in the prime continuity from


## Relationships III — Rivals, Enemies & Lovers

# RELATIONSHIPS III — Rivals, Enemies & Lovers

A note before the catalogue. The subject's rivalries, enmities, and intimacies tend to bleed into one another in ways that are diagnostic. The man he hates most (Sinister) is the man who curated his childhood. The man he loved as a father (Xavier) is the man he ultimately killed. The woman he idealizes (Jean) is the woman he was never able to be ordinarily present with. The woman he is most himself with (Emma) is the woman he started loving while still married to the first. The rival he fights hardest (Logan) is the only male peer who has ever read him accurately. **Categorical separation between "rival," "enemy," and "lover" is not a feature of this subject's relational world.** It is therefore not a feature of this section.

---

## A. ENEMIES — The Antagonists Who Shaped the Architecture

### A.1 Nathaniel Essex / Mister Sinister

The defining adversary, and the one the subject understands least clearly even now.

**History.** Sinister curated the subject's bloodline across generations. The orphanage in Omaha (State Home for Foundlings) was, in operational terms, a Sinister observation post; the subject's separation from Alex was Sinister's protocol; the engineered "marriage prospect" Madelyne Pryor was a Sinister product designed to extract Summers-Grey progeny (delivered: Nathan Christopher Charles Summers). Every major reproductive and developmental milestone of the subject's life has been, at some level, supervised by this man.

**Dynamic.** Asymmetric to the point of grotesquerie. The subject experiences Sinister as a recurring tactical enemy he can occasionally defeat in the field. Sinister experiences the subject as a long-running experiment whose every defeat is data. The subject has never — across 60 years of canon — sat with the full implication: that **his entire selfhood was developed inside an observation chamber.** Whenever the data threatens to surface (the Madelyne revelation in *Inferno*; the Sinister-Madelyne genealogy in *X-Factor* #38-39; Sinister's repeated demonstrations of foreknowledge), the subject metabolizes it tactically — *what do I do about Sinister now* — rather than autobiographically — *what does it mean that I was raised by him*.

**Trust/safety.** Zero. But the absence of trust is not the same as the presence of insight. The subject has internalized "Sinister is the enemy" without internalizing "Sinister is the reason I am the way I am."

**Failure mode.** Underestimates the depth of the manipulation. Repeatedly assumes Sinister's plans are about acquiring power or specimens, when in fact they are about *him* in particular. His own historical centrality is a blind spot.

**Leverage Sinister holds.** Total epistemic leverage. He knows things about the subject — physiological baselines from childhood, genetic projections, the engineered nature of past intimacies — that the subject has never been allowed to know about himself. If Sinister chose to weaponize disclosure, the resulting identity rupture could be more damaging than any physical attack.

**Leverage the subject holds.** Operational. He can predict Sinister's moves better than anyone alive because he has been the case study; the data flows both ways even if only one party is conscious of it.

### A.2 En Sabah Nur / Apocalypse

**History.** Apocalypse and the subject share two of the most psychologically loaded entanglements in the canon: (1) the loss of Nathan Christopher to the techno-organic virus, which Apocalypse engineered as a method of forcing the subject into the impossible parental choice; (2) the *Twelve* event, during which the subject's body was bonded with Apocalypse's consciousness for an extended period and, on partial separation, the subject re-emerged as a colder operator.

**Dynamic.** Apocalypse, like Sinister but more ideologically, treats the subject as material. The crucial difference: Apocalypse's instrumentalism is honest. He announces it. The subject can therefore parse it cleanly. **Sinister is the abuser; Apocalypse is merely the tyrant.** It is easier for the subject to fight an enemy who is not also a parent.

**Trust/safety.** None — but here the *somatic* absence of trust is total in a way it is not with Sinister, because Apocalypse has occupied his body. The subject experiences a residual proprioceptive wrongness around Apocalypsean energies he himself cannot fully account for.

**Failure mode.** The subject has absorbed more of Apocalypse's operational logic than he admits. Post-*Twelve*, post-Utopia, post-AvX: the man who orders X-Force, who arms children, who declares "no more Avengers," is — in his structural premises — Apocalypse-shaped. *Survival of the fittest, no quarter, doctrine over sentiment.* He repudiates Apocalypse the person while internalizing Apocalypse the method.

**Leverage Apocalypse holds.** A template for the subject's own authoritarian drift. Every time the subject reasons in extinction-logic, he is borrowing Apocalypse's grammar without acknowledgement.

### A.3 Magneto / Erik Lehnsherr

**History.** Begins as binary opposite — the subject is Xavier's first and most loyal disciple, Magneto is Xavier's adversary and dark mirror. Across decades the polarity rotates a full 180°: by Krakoa, the subject and Magneto are co-architects of the same mutant sovereignty, and Magneto has openly conceded that the subject's strategic radicalization vindicates Magneto's lifelong analysis.

**Dynamic.** Quietly the most consequential rival in the file. Where Xavier was the father, Magneto was the alternative father — the one whose grief and rage the subject was forbidden from inheriting. After *Schism* and *AvX*, the prohibition collapses. The two men begin to recognize each other as fellow survivors of unsurvivable childhoods who organized their adult lives around the same vow ("never again, for my people") and merely reached different operational conclusions about how to keep it. By Krakoa, they share quarters of an island and quarters of a worldview.

**Trust/safety.** Surprisingly high in late canon. Limited but real. The subject and Magneto can speak frankly to each other in a register neither can use with anyone else — *what does extinction-defense actually cost the person doing it* — because each has paid the cost.

**Failure mode.** The subject's identification with Magneto is now strong enough that he no longer has access to the Xavierian inner-voice that would once have functioned as a brake. If Magneto's analysis is wrong about a specific decision, the subject is unlikely to be the dissenter in the room.

**Leverage.** Mutual. Each man is the only one who could persuade the other to step back from a precipice. Each man is also the only one who could push the other off it.

### A.4 William Stryker

The clean enemy. Religious-fanatic exterminator. The subject's hatred here is uncomplicated and clarifying — Stryker is what the world is when it tells the truth about what it thinks of mutants. The subject does not need to interrogate his response to Stryker; the response is righteous and bounded. **The subject keeps Stryker in his mental file partly as a regulator: when his hatred for ordinary humans threatens to generalize, he reminds himself that not all humans are Stryker.** When he stops being able to make that reminder land, he is in trouble.

### A.5 Bastion / the Sentinel program / Operation: Zero Tolerance / Orchis

A composite enemy: the institutional, automated, bureaucratic genocidal apparatus. The subject's response to this enemy is also clarifying, but in a different direction from Stryker — Stryker is the human face of extermination, Bastion the inhuman one. The subject treats Bastion-class threats as *engineering problems* and is at his most lucidly competent against them. Notably: when the threat is mechanical and faceless, the subject's affect actually improves. He performs better against systems than against people. (Diagnostic.)

### A.6 The Shi'ar Imperial Guard / Gladiator / Vulcan

A complicated enmity inherited from family. The Shi'ar killed his mother; the Shi'ar (eventually) recovered his father; the Shi'ar empire is the geopolitical context inside which his brother Gabriel (Vulcan) became a galactic war-criminal. The subject's response to the Shi'ar is *constrained rage* — he cannot fully discharge it because his father became one of them by adoption and his brother became one of them by conquest. **The Shi'ar are the family enemy he is structurally barred from hating cleanly.** This is also why he never travels offworld for personal reasons; the entire register of "outer space" is contaminated with unmetabolized material.

### A.7 The Reavers / Donald Pierce / Trevor Fitzroy / the "human supremacist with money" archetype

Functionally interchangeable to the subject. He registers them by tactical signature rather than personality. Worth noting only because his *failure* to differentiate them is itself a datum — wealthy human supremacists are, for him, a single repeating noise.

### A.8 Sebastian Shaw / Hellfire Club (the older form)

Relevant primarily as the institutional context that produced Jean's Dark Phoenix conversion and the context in which Emma Frost was forged. The subject's feelings about Shaw personally are tactical-contemptuous; his feelings about the Hellfire Club as an institution are more interesting — it is, structurally, the negative image of Xavier's School (covert, hedonic, exploitative of children, financialized) and the subject's revulsion at it is partly a revulsion at what Xavier's project could have become, and partly (he does not admit this) envy of an institution unburdened by Xavier's moral pretense.

### A.9 The Avengers, post-*AvX*

Not enemies in the categorical sense, but for an extended period operationally treated as such. The subject's rupture with Captain America is particularly diagnostic: two men whose self-concept is "I am the responsibility I carry" recognizing each other as mirror-rivals and being unable to share oxygen. The subject's post-AvX line — *we want the same thing, we just disagree about who gets to die for it* — is as close as he comes to articulating the structure.

---

## B. RIVALS — Peers Whose Existence Pressures the Self

### B.1 James Howlett / Logan / Wolverine

The central male peer-rival of the subject's adult life. Forty years of canon devoted to friction.

**History.** Logan arrives in *Giant-Size X-Men #1* (1975). Immediately makes a pass at Jean. Immediately challenges the subject's leadership. Across the Claremont era the rivalry stabilizes into a functional partnership — the subject as tactician, Logan as berserker — but the romantic undertone with Jean never fully recedes, and Logan is constitutionally incapable of the kind of deference the subject expects from team members.

**Dynamic.** They are each other's photographic negatives. The subject is over-controlled affect, doctrine, future-orientation, monogamous fixation, abstemious. Logan is under-controlled affect, anti-doctrine, present-orientation, serially attached, chemically self-medicated. **Each man treats the other as a critique of his own existence.** The subject thinks Logan is what he would be if he gave up; Logan thinks the subject is what he would be if he died inside.

**Trust/safety.** Operational trust is high — neither has ever betrayed the other in the field. Personal trust is low and necessarily so; intimacy between them is mediated by Jean, who loved both. Safety: each can wound the other in ways no one else can, and they know it, and they discharge it constantly through ritualized hostility.

**Evolution.** Pre-*Schism*: brothers under glass. *Schism* itself: rupture along the children-as-soldiers axis, with each man holding a position the other can morally recognize but tactically not accept. Post-Krakoa: a kind of weary reconciliation; the two longest-running soldiers in the war comparing scars without competition.

**Failure mode.** The subject cannot hear Logan's specific criticisms of him *as criticisms* — he hears them as Logan's character, not as content. Most of what Logan has told him over the decades about his treatment of women, of children, and of subordinates has been correct, and almost none of it has been processed.

**Leverage.** Logan is the only man on the team who would refuse a direct order from the subject without leaving the room. This is, for the subject, both intolerable and stabilizing — the existence of Logan's refusal-capacity prevents the subject from drifting into pure command-absolutism. Logan is, in operational-systems terms, his governor.

### B.2 Hank McCoy / Beast

**History.** Original five. Fifty-plus years of co-presence. Childhood-adjacent intimacy that has slowly soured into mutual disappointment.

**Dynamic.** For decades, Hank was the friend who could speak to the subject in registers no one else could — both men over-intellectualize, both men compartmentalize, both men trust ideas more than feelings. The rivalry was latent and friendly: who is the more cerebral, who carries the moral weight more correctly.

**Evolution.** Hank's late-career drift into ethically dubious science (the time-displaced X-Men gambit, the Krakoa-era intelligence atrocities) has become a mirror of the subject's own ethical drift, and watching it from the outside has been, for the subject, deeply destabilizing — *this is what it looks like when a brilliant good man rationalizes himself into monstrosity, and I am one variable away from being him.* The subject's late posture toward Hank is grieved coldness.

**Failure mode.** The subject has never confronted Hank about Hank's drift; he watched it happen and pretended not to see, because to name it would be to admit it could happen to him.

**Leverage.** Hank knows the subject's medical history at a cellular level. If anyone has the data to map the subject's neurological inhibitor problem, optic-output anomalies, and Apocalyptic and Phoenix residues, it is Hank. The subject's medical privacy is, with regard to Hank, fictional.

### B.3 Warren Worthington III / Angel / Archangel

**History.** Original five. Wealth, beauty, and ease — three things the subject does not have and does not know how to want. The early-era rivalry was triangular (both pursued Jean), then class-coded (Warren funded operations the subject led), then trauma-coded (Warren's Archangel transformation made him a fellow trauma-survivor on terms the subject could finally recognize).

**Dynamic.** The subject's relationship with Warren is mediated by a discomfort he has never named: Warren is what the subject might have looked like if the catastrophe had not happened. Wealthy, athletic, charming, loved. Watching Warren be repeatedly broken by his own catastrophes (the wings, the Death persona, the Apocalypse-seed) has produced in the subject a complicated tenderness — *the catastrophe finds everyone eventually.*

**Failure mode.** The subject has historically deployed Warren as a resource (funding, transport, infrastructure) without adequately registering that Warren is also a person who needed leadership care during his crises and rarely got it from him.

**Leverage.** Financial-historical; Warren has bankrolled multiple of the subject's institutional projects, and the subject's project-continuity is partly Warren-contingent.

### B.4 Bobby Drake / Iceman

A non-rival, listed here because the absence of rivalry is diagnostic. Bobby is the original-five teammate whose interior life the subject has had the least curiosity about across sixty years — and Bobby is the one who, late in canon, came out as gay. The subject was a near-daily presence in Bobby's life from age 16 onward and never noticed. The subject's response to the disclosure was correct, supportive, and structurally guilty. **He had not been *looking* at Bobby as a full person.** This is now, for him, a private file-item under "things I missed about people in front of me."

### B.5 Steve Rogers / Captain America

See A.9. Functionally a rival rather than an enemy in steady-state; the only other Marvel-universe figure whose self-concept is fully duty-organized. They mirror each other and cannot stand it.

### B.6 Reed Richards

A rival the subject does not know he has. Reed represents the version of *I am responsible for outcomes at planetary scale* that maintained an ordinary marriage and ordinary fatherhood. The subject does not study Reed, because doing so would require asking why Reed managed something the subject could not.

### B.7 Tony Stark

A non-rival the subject finds annoying. Surface friction (Tony's affect, Tony's chemicals, Tony's celebrity) masks a deeper avoidance: Tony is a man who built an institutional response to his own catastrophe by *being seen*, and the subject's entire architecture is built on *not being seen*. They are antipodal solutions to similar trauma-types and they recognize each other dimly through that.

### B.8 Alex Summers / Havok

The brother. Listed in Relationships II as family, but a structural rival here as well — Alex has spent his entire life partly in the subject's shadow and partly free of it, and the subject has never fully reckoned with the fact that he was, in childhood, the parent-substitute and the disciplinarian to a brother who probably needed something gentler. The rivalry is one-sided and posthumous to a relationship that never quite happened.

### B.9 Nathan / Cable

The son who became older than the father. Cable's existence is a standing critique of every parenting decision the subject made — and Cable's *competence* is the subject's strange consolation: *I sent him into hell and he came back as a war-saint, therefore the decision was correct, therefore I am absolved.* This is the rationalization. The rivalry is the subject's reluctance to admit that Cable's adulthood owes nothing to his parenting and everything to Cable's surrogate-parents in the future. (Treated more fully in Relationships II.)

---

## C. LOVERS / INTIMATES — The Three Women and the Echoes

### C.1 Jean Grey

The lost object. The organizing fixation of an adult lifetime.

**History.** Met as adolescents at Xavier's. The subject's first thought-bubble about Jean (1963) is that he can never look at her because his eyes will destroy her. **Their entire relationship is encoded in that first thought.** Across the Silver Age the love is restrained, idealized, never consummated. Through Phoenix and Dark Phoenix she becomes a cosmic figure, dies, returns as Madelyne (clone), returns as herself, marries the subject (*X-Men #30*, 1994), is killed again (Magneto/Xorn arc, Morrison), is resurrected on Krakoa.

**Dynamic.** Jean is not, for the subject, a woman. She is a project of permanent restoration — the lost mother, the original beloved, the proof that the universe is occasionally merciful. He has never spent a sustained period with her in which she was *simply present*; every era of their relationship has been mediated by cosmic event, separation, death, or resurrection. **He has been in love with her for sixty years and has never had to do the work of an ordinary Tuesday with her.**

**Trust/safety.** Total mythic trust; partial somatic trust. He can entrust her with his life; he has never been able to entrust her with his ordinariness. The visor metaphor is exact: she is the one person the visor is for, and she is the one person he cannot be without it.

**Failure mode (his).** He cannot tolerate her being a person rather than a beloved. Whenever she does something the projection cannot contain — accepting Phoenix, becoming Dark Phoenix, dying, choosing him to live and her to die — he responds by deepening the projection rather than meeting the actual woman.

**Failure mode (hers, to the extent diagnostic).** She has historically accepted the projection because being projected onto by the subject is, in its way, a form of devotion. Late-canon Jean has begun to refuse the projection — the Krakoan arrangement (she with him, he also with Emma, mutual non-deception) is partly her insistence on being met as a person not an icon.

**Leverage.** Total and reciprocal. She is the one person whose disapproval would dismantle him.

**Evolution.** Krakoa is the first era in which the relationship has had room to be ordinary. Whether either of them can tolerate ordinariness is the open question.

### C.2 Madelyne Pryor

The catastrophic intimate. The relationship the subject has metabolized least and owes most.

**History.** Met in Alaska after Jean's first death (Phoenix on the moon). Physical double of Jean — not coincidentally; Sinister-engineered for exactly this convergence. The subject married her, fathered Nathan with her, attempted a civilian life as a bush pilot. On hearing Jean was alive (*X-Factor #1*, 1986), abandoned Madelyne and infant Nathan within days. Madelyne, abandoned and unrecognized for who she was, became the Goblin Queen; died in *Inferno*; has returned in various forms across the decades.

**Dynamic (during the marriage).** The most relationally available the subject has ever been, and the least conscious of it. He treated her as Jean-restored without ever consciously naming the substitution; she sensed the substitution and pretended not to. The marriage was the closest the subject ever came to an ordinary life and it was built on a misidentification that neither party would name.

**Dynamic (after).** Adversarial when she is alive, repressed when she is not. The subject has never publicly grieved Madelyne and has never publicly apologized — because to do either would be to admit that he abandoned a real woman and an infant son to chase a restored projection.

**Trust/safety.** Functionally negative — when Madelyne is present, the subject reorganizes around a guilt he cannot let surface, and his behavior toward her is correspondingly evasive and tactical.

**Failure mode.** Continued non-reckoning. **Madelyne is the unindexed file.** The subject has metabolized Jean's deaths, Xavier's death, Nathan's exile, even his own death — but he has not metabolized what he did to Madelyne. It is the single largest unprocessed item in his interior life.

**Leverage.** Should Madelyne ever choose to speak to him about what he did, in a register he could not deflect, the resulting confrontation would be more dangerous to his self-concept than any combat encounter on file.

### C.3 Emma Frost

The adult intimate. The first woman who refused to be his projection.

**History.** Long pre-history as adversary (Hellfire White Queen, *UXM #129*-era). Reformed alignment through generations of New Mutants/Generation X. Becomes co-headmaster with the subject post-Morrison. *New X-Men*: initiates a telepathic affair with him while he is married to Jean. Jean catches them; Jean dies (Xorn); Scott and Emma pair openly thereafter. The relationship persists as the central adult attachment through Decimation, Utopia, Schism, AvX, and the subject's death. Krakoa: separation, by Emma's choice, with the subject's polyamorous reunion with Jean as a contributing factor.

**Dynamic.** Emma is the only intimate in the subject's life who has read his defenses *clinically* and *out loud*. She names compartmentalization when she sees it. She names the projection-onto-Jean when she sees it. She does not flatter him and she does not idealize him — and the subject, paradoxically, is more himself with her than he has ever been with anyone. **Where Jean is the visor's reason,


## Powers, Abilities & Their Limits

# POWERS, ABILITIES & THEIR LIMITS — SUBJECT: SUMMERS, SCOTT

> **Operational summary up front.** The subject is, at first inventory, a mid-tier energy-projector with extraordinary tactical cognition. At second inventory — which is the correct one — he is a sole-survivor child whose body has been welded permanently to its own weapon, who has therefore been forced to develop the most disciplined ocular, postural, and cognitive control regime in the canon, and whose *real* signature ability is not the optic blast but the **continuous, lifelong, frame-by-frame suppression of it.** Everything below should be read in that light.

---

## 1. THE PRIMARY MUTATION — MECHANISM

### 1.1 What the blast actually is

The subject's mutation is an *aperture*, not a generator. He does not manufacture energy inside his skull (which would, on any plausible thermodynamic accounting, have killed him before age seven). He metabolizes ambient electromagnetic energy — sunlight is the primary source, with cosmic background and other broad-spectrum radiation as auxiliary feedstock — and shunts it through a small, ocular-region rift to a non-Einsteinian pocket space, from which it returns as kinetic-coherent particulate force. The beam is, despite popular misreading, **not thermal.** It does not burn. It strikes. It pushes. The damage profile is purely concussive — closer to a directed kinetic ram than to a laser — which is why he can drill through stone, punch a sentinel off its feet, and shave the bark off a tree, but cannot light a candle (a recurring on-panel joke that is actually a clinical clue: the subject knows the upper bound of what his power *cannot* do with the precision of a man who has measured it nightly for forty years).

### 1.2 Why he cannot turn it off

The standing explanation across writers from Claremont forward: closed-head trauma at the parachute landing, age ~9, damaged the specific neural inhibitory pathway that would, in an undamaged Summers physiology, gate the aperture closed. The aperture is therefore *constitutively open.* What closes it is not nerve but matter — specifically the silicate lattice known in-universe as ruby quartz, which is transparent to ordinary photons but opaque to the particular wave-particle character of the blast. **The single most important clinical fact about his power is that it cannot be turned off from the inside.** Every other power-user on the planet has an "off." He has a lens.

The symbolic content of this fact is so dense it deserves its own line: *the trauma that orphaned him is the same trauma that weaponized him, and the weapon cannot be sheathed by the will of the person carrying it.* No therapist will ever assign a homework as on-the-nose as the subject's own physiology.

### 1.3 Why his brother is immune; why he is immune to himself

Alex (Havok) absorbs the same energy class natively; the brothers are mutually transparent to each other's emissions. Scott's own tissues, including his eyelids and the back of his skull, are likewise transparent to his own beam — eyelids do not stop the blast, which is why blinking and sleeping are not solutions and why his lenses must be on him *at every conscious moment and during most unconscious ones.* This is not a tactical inconvenience. It is a 24-hour somatic occupation.

---

## 2. RANGE, OUTPUT, AND THE CONTROL ENVELOPE

### 2.1 Output range

Documented across decades. The subject can modulate the aperture's effective output across at least three orders of magnitude — from a feather-soft nudge that knocks a glass off a table without cracking it, to a wide-area discharge that has, on the record, levelled industrial structures, dropped Sentinels, and (in extremis, post-Apocalypse, post-Phoenix exposure) cratered terrain. He has never been satisfactorily power-tested because no one — including him — wants to find out what the ceiling is. The Hickman-era files acknowledge this as a deliberate institutional avoidance: *we do not measure Captain Commander's maximum because we do not need to know.*

### 2.2 Range proper

Effective accurate range is in the hundreds of meters; line-of-sight is the only true limit. The beam does not appreciably diverge at distance — another argument against the "laser" misreading; lasers are obedient to optics, this is obedient to intention. At extreme distance the subject loses targeting confidence before he loses delivery.

### 2.3 The control envelope — the part that matters

The output dial is graduated continuously, not discretely, and is controlled by **the fine musculature around the orbit and brow** plus a learned proprioceptive map he has been building since he was a child. The ruby-quartz visor's iris is a mechanical second derivative: he opens it by moving a finger across the trigger on the headpiece, but the *aim, the angle, the duration, and above all the intensity* are him. This is a fine-motor performance the equal of any concert pianist's, sustained without break across decades, on a "keyboard" no one else can see.

The control envelope has expanded over time:
- **Adolescence:** crude on/off, near-maximum intensity, frequent overshoot. He hurt people he did not mean to hurt.
- **Early X-Men:** Xavier-supervised, learns dialing and arcing.
- **Claremont era:** ricochet geometry comes online (see §3.2). Subject can now *intend* the second and third impacts.
- **Post-Apocalypse / Morrison era:** modulation precision elevated. Subject performs surgical-grade output adjustments on the fly, including the celebrated "scalpel" applications — cauterizing-shape blasts that cut without crushing.
- **Phoenix arc:** the only documented period in his life during which the aperture was under *volitional* control — the visor was unnecessary, the eyes glowed, the off-switch was finally installed. The contemporary record indicates he will not, when asked, say much about that period, which is itself the data.
- **Krakoa / contemporary:** the most regulated output discipline in his life. Discharges are spare, exact, and almost always at sub-maximum. He has stopped showing off, if he ever did.

---

## 3. SIGNATURE APPLICATIONS

### 3.1 The "calibrated blast" — the dial as personality

The application most associated with him in close professional observation is not the heavy hit but the **astonishingly small one** — knocking a pistol from a hand without harming the hand, severing one cable in a bundle, popping a single rivet from a door panel, putting a kinetic dot on a falling teammate's belt to nudge them three degrees off a collision line. This is the use his peers most often comment on, usually after the fact and usually with a flat note of *I have no idea how he does that.* The mechanism is unspectacular: thousands of supervised hours, a self-built proprioceptive lexicon, and the C-PTSD-grade attentional fixation of a man who has never, in his adult life, taken his focus off the weapon attached to his face.

### 3.2 Ricochet geometry — the trajectory cognition

The single most distinctive *cognitive* component of his power use. The subject computes ricochet vectors in real time — angle of incidence, surface elasticity, secondary impact, tertiary impact — and routinely lands beams on targets that are not in his line of sight by bouncing them off walls, floors, mirrors, Colossus's chest, ice slides, and the inside curves of architectural features. He sees the room as a billiards table laid out in three dimensions plus the fourth (intended sequence). This is sometimes attributed to a secondary mutation granting spatial-geometric intuition; the more parsimonious reading is **temperamental and trained.** He has spent his life modelling the room he is in as a containment problem for his own discharge; modelling it as a *delivery* problem for the same discharge is the obverse of the same skill. The trauma that produced the hyper-vigilance produced the geometry.

### 3.3 The sustained beam — the rare maximum

When he opens the iris fully and holds, the discharge becomes a continuous wide-bore concussive stream rather than a pulse. He uses this perhaps once an arc, never gratuitously. Maintaining it is taxing in a way that is not energetic (the energy is ambient and free) but **inhibitory** — every microsecond of sustained discharge is a microsecond during which the rigorous *not-discharging* he performs the rest of the day is suspended, and the cost is paid afterwards in the form of post-engagement migraines, jaw-tension, and a flat affective hangover that field medics have learned to recognize and leave alone.

### 3.4 The non-application — the conspicuous restraint

Equally a signature: the moments he could fire and does not. He has stood with his finger off the trigger, visor closed, while taking severe physical punishment, because the line-of-fire included an ally, a civilian, or a child. This restraint is itself a power; it is the displayed top-side of the inhibitory project that occupies him full-time underneath the visor.

---

## 4. THE EQUIPMENT (TREATED AS A PROSTHESIS, NOT AN ACCESSORY)

### 4.1 The visor

Standard field configuration: a ruby-quartz crystalline band fitted into a metal frame that wraps the orbital region and locks at the temples and occiput. The single trigger sits at the right temple; he is right-handed and the muscle-memory of that finger-to-temple movement is so deeply grooved it occurs in roughly 90ms from intent to discharge — faster than most opponents draw. The visor includes a tactical readout on later models (Hickman/Krakoa-era) but he does not rely on it; he is *the* readout.

### 4.2 The glasses

Civilian wear and bunk wear. Heavier than they look (ruby-quartz is dense), prescription-frame appearance, secured by cable-stay arms behind the ears. He sleeps in them. He showers behind a tiled wall with eyes shut and a hand on a rail. He has a documented protocol — observed by every long-term partner and roommate — for transferring from glasses to visor without an unlensed instant: glasses on, visor brought to face, glasses removed *under* the visor in a single learned motion. The reverse for civilian transition. **No witness in canon has seen Scott Summers' bare open eye on a non-Summers, non-Phoenix-amplified, non-mind-controlled occasion since adolescence.** That is the operational fact.

### 4.3 Redundancy and contingency

He carries spares. At least one backup pair of glasses on his person at all times (inner jacket, left chest, the side opposite his trigger hand). Field kit includes a fallback ruby-quartz wrap-strap and, in the Krakoa era, an emergency contact-lens analog produced by Beast-grade labs that he distrusts and uses only when nothing else is available. The redundancy is not paranoia in the clinical sense; it is the exact, correctly-calibrated response of a man whose lens is the only thing between his perception and a fatality. **He is the most rationally-prepared person in the building on this one specific axis, and the preparation is bottomless.**

### 4.4 The shower, the pillow, the rain

Documented behavioral micro-rituals. He showers with eyes shut, hand on rail, towel pre-positioned at exactly the height his hand will be when he reaches. He sleeps with the glasses on; partners (Jean, Emma) report he does not remove them during sleep and they have learned not to touch the frames. In rain he angles the head forward fractionally to keep droplets off the lens surface; the lens does not, of course, need to be dry to function, but he prefers a clean optical field as a matter of discipline. In dust he blinks against the lens in a particular pattern — short, short, long — that clears most particulate without compromising seal.

---

## 5. SECONDARY AND ANCILLARY CAPABILITIES

### 5.1 Spatial cognition

Addressed above (§3.2). Whether secondary mutation or trained temperament, the result is the same in practice: he sees rooms as vector fields. He is also, relatedly, an exceptional pilot — both inherited from Christopher and reinforced by the Alaskan bush-pilot interregnum. Three-dimensional flight intuition is, for him, native. He flies the Blackbird the way other pilots ride a bicycle.

### 5.2 Field generalship

Not a power in the mutation sense, but it is a capability so distinctive it belongs in this section. The subject runs a fluid combat formation in real time — assigning vectors, calling overlaps, anticipating two beats ahead — with a clarity that has been remarked upon by, among others, Captain America (in-canon, on at least two documented occasions, with mixed feelings). The cognitive substrate is the same as the ricochet geometry: the room as a moving system; the bodies in it as moving constraints; the desired end-state as a position in phase space; the path from here to there as a series of dial settings on a dozen people at once. He is, by a clear margin, the best small-unit field commander in the mutant population, and arguably in the wider hero population.

### 5.3 Hand-to-hand and weapons

Solid but not elite by mutant standards. Xavier and Wolverine trained him; he is competent across striking and grappling and a usable hand with edged weapons and firearms. He fights like a man who would prefer not to be in melee, because melee compromises line-of-sight; he tends to break distance and re-establish the beam as the primary engagement tool. He is comfortable disarmed *only* if the visor is on.

### 5.4 Physical conditioning

Above the human baseline by training, not mutation. Endurance over strength. He maintains conditioning with a fixed daily regime — pre-dawn (see §7) — that has not appreciably varied across decades.

### 5.5 Languages, technical literacy

Functional in several languages (Shi'ar phonetics through extended off-world exposure; Japanese through field deployments; some Krakoan glyph fluency in the contemporary era). Comfortable with a wide tactical and aerospace technical literature. Reads more than he is given credit for.

---

## 6. GROWTH OVER TIME (LONGITUDINAL POWER PROFILE)

- **Onset (adolescence).** Uncontrolled, terrifying, the cause of his initial flight from the orphanage and the mob that pursued him. The mutation arrives as a curse. The Xavier intervention reframes it as a tool, which is a psychological save of the first order — but the curse-character never quite leaves the subject's private experience of it.
- **Original X-Men.** Steady technical improvement. The first ricochet shots are documented in the Lee/Thomas era and are already characteristic.
- **Claremont era (mid-control, mid-confidence).** Output and precision both rise. The subject becomes capable of his signature scalpel-and-billiards work. Internally, however, the power remains experienced as a constraint to be managed, not an asset to be wielded.
- **Madelyne / Alaska interregnum.** Civilian glasses; reduced discharge; an attempt to *live with* the power at low ambient. This is the only period in which he can be observed treating the mutation as background rather than foreground, and it ends the moment Jean returns.
- **X-Factor through 1990s.** Combat-veteran phase. Capability plateau; precision continues to creep upward.
- **Apocalypse bonding and aftermath.** Power output reportedly elevated post-bonding; control improved; the subject does not interrogate the irony that the period of his greatest somatic violation produced a measurable upgrade. (He should interrogate it. He does not.)
- **Phoenix episode.** The only period in which the aperture is volitional. Output ceiling unmeasured and unmeasurable; control absolute. Withdrawal is severe.
- **Krakoa / contemporary.** Discipline at lifetime maximum; output deployed sparingly and exactly; the visor is now an instrument he plays rather than a prison he wears. The change is psychological more than physiological — a sovereign mutant state has finally provided the external scaffolding his internal scaffolding has been substituting for since age nine, and the result is visible in how he uses (and does not use) the beam.

---

## 7. THE DISCIPLINE STACK — DAILY ROUTINES OF CONTROL

A surveillance file of the kind this is would catalogue the routines. The relevant ones:

- **Pre-dawn wake.** 04:30–05:00 across decades and across geographies. Glasses already on. Sits up, orients, breathes for a measured interval before standing.
- **Visor/glasses inspection.** Every morning, lens edges checked for chips or hairline fractures under a small loupe he keeps in his kit. He has discarded perfectly serviceable lenses for cosmetic imperfections invisible at conversational distance, which is the correct decision but is also a tell.
- **Targeting drills.** Documented in the Danger Room across every era and continued privately when no Danger Room is available — small, dialed-down discharges at fixed-distance targets, performed for thirty to sixty minutes daily. He is *practicing,* every day, the act of not killing.
- **Meditation / breath regulation.** Adopted in the Xavier years, retained without lapse. The breath protocol is also a discharge-management protocol — the diaphragm and the brow musculature are coupled by long training, and the breath modulates the dial.
- **Evening lens-transition.** Glasses to bedside frame (a slightly heavier-stayed pair he sleeps in); routine performed in exactly the same sequence in exactly the same place every night when conditions permit.
- **Conspicuous abstemiousness.** No alcohol to excess, no nicotine, no recreational drug use, minimal caffeine. The reason is operational, but he will not say so: chemicals compromise the inhibitory project, and the inhibitory project is the self.

These routines are the daily price of the mutation. Most of the people who admire the subject's competence have no idea what fraction of his waking life is paid into the upkeep of the lens between him and them.

---

## 8. LIMITS, FAILURE MODES, AND VULNERABILITIES

### 8.1 Physical / mechanical

- **Lens failure.** Cracked, lost, or shattered visor is a catastrophic failure mode. He has protocols (eyes shut, hand to face, locate spare, transfer under cover, recover line-of-sight). The protocols are smooth. The internal experience during them is not.
- **Eyelid transparency.** Closing the eyes does not stop the beam. Sleep is not a refuge.
- **Energy starvation.** Prolonged absence of ambient energy (deep underground, sealed environments, certain extradimensional spaces) reduces output. Has been depicted as significantly reducing his effectiveness; has never been depicted as fully off-lining him.
- **Reflective surfaces.** A beam reflected back into his own eyes does not damage him (self-transparency, §1.3), but a beam reflected onto allies is the standing nightmare and the reason he so rigorously models the geometry of every room he fights in.
- **Brother-class transparency.** Alex absorbs his blasts; certain other absorbers (Bishop, Sebastian Shaw) can metabolize them as a power source. He has had to learn to disengage rather than feed an opponent.

### 8.2 Cognitive / attentional

- **Inhibitory load.** Discussed throughout. The full-time job of *not discharging* consumes a baseline of attentional resource. Under cognitive overload (grief, exhaustion, divided loyalties), his fine control degrades before his gross control does.
- **Migraine and tension.** Chronic. Worst post-sustained-beam, post-Phoenix arcs, and during periods of relational stress. He works through.
- **Affect → output coupling.** Strong emotion is correlated with discharge intensity in subtle ways even he may not consciously register. The subject's worst miscalibrations across the record correlate temporally with his worst emotional states. This is not coincidence.

### 8.3 The metaphysical limit

There is exactly one period in which he had an "off switch": the Phoenix. The fact that the only thing capable of installing it was a cosmic-scale possession is, in itself, the most concise statement of his condition that the canon offers. He cannot fix this from inside. He can only manage it. He has spent his life managing it with extraordinary discipline, and the discipline has become the man.

---

## 9. SYMPTOM-AS-SIGNATURE — A SUMMARY READING

A surveillance file's job is to notice what the subject's body is *saying* in the language of behavior; here the body and the power are saying the same sentence and have been saying it since the parachute.

- **The aperture is constitutively open** — *because the child learned that letting his guard down kills the people below him.*
- **The lens is external** — *because the inhibitor was destroyed by the same event that installed the responsibility.*
- **He sleeps in his glasses** — *because there has not been a safe unguarded moment since age nine and he has stopped expecting one.*
- **He fights by ricochet** — *because he has spent his life modelling rooms as containment problems for his own discharge, and the inverse of containment is delivery.*
- **He fires small** — *because the discipline of not-killing is the discipline he wakes up inside every morning, and small discharges are its public expression.*
- **He fires huge only when overwhelmed** — *because over-control's failure mode is not under-control, it is catastrophic discharge, and his power is the literal version of his affect.*
- **He does not drink, does not smoke, does not drug** — *because nothing is allowed to lower the guard the visor enforces externally.*
- **He fought best the one time the off-switch was installed** — *and he will not, when asked, talk much about it.*

The power is the trauma made visible. The discipline is the personality made operational. The lens is the only honest piece of equipment in the building — it is the exact, literal, ruby-quartz shape of *the thing he has been doing inside his head every second of every day since the parachute caught fire.*

That is the file on what he can do, and on what doing it has cost him.


## Operational Profile & Tradecraft

# OPERATIONAL PROFILE & TRADECRAFT — SUMMERS, SCOTT

## 6.1 Decision-Making Architecture

The subject's decision process is, beneath its appearance of cold calculation, a **two-stage gated system** with a hidden third stage. Documenting it is the most useful single thing this section can do, because nearly every observable operational behavior is downstream of it.

**Stage 1 — Threat Vectoring.** Within the first 1–3 seconds of any new tactical input, the subject silently enumerates: (a) who in the room/field is the smallest or most vulnerable element, (b) where the exits are, (c) what the worst plausible outcome is, (d) what the minimum-cost intervention is that prevents (c). The eidetic geometric capacity associated with his power (trajectory cognition, ricochet planning) operates here at a non-verbal speed; he has solved the room before he has finished assessing it. Observers consistently misread the resulting silence as hesitation. It is the opposite: he is already three moves ahead and is waiting for the team to catch up.

**Stage 2 — Doctrine Filter.** The minimum-cost intervention identified in Stage 1 is then run against an internalized rule set — originally Xavier's, progressively rewritten since *Schism* and *AvX*, currently a Krakoan-era hybrid. The filter asks: *does this action violate a stated principle I am holding the team to?* If yes, the subject searches for an alternative that achieves ≥85% of the tactical outcome at zero principle-cost. He will spend real seconds on this search even mid-firefight.

**Stage 3 (concealed) — The Survivor's Override.** If Stage 2 yields no acceptable alternative and the cost of doctrine-adherence is the death of a person in his protection, the doctrine is silently discarded, the optimal action is executed, and **the subject privately ledgers the violation against himself** without telling the team. X-Force is the documented institutionalization of Stage 3. The Schism with Logan is, in operational terms, a disagreement about whether Stage 3 should remain concealed or become explicit policy. The subject's position — that it should be both used and concealed — is the position of a man who has spent his life paying private costs and assumes that is simply what leadership is.

**Failure modes of this architecture.** (i) Under cosmic-scale stakes (extinction frames, Phoenix, mutant-population collapse), Stage 2 ceases to fire and Stage 3 becomes the default — the doctrine filter is bypassed because *the doctrine itself was built for a world in which the species existed.* (ii) Under personal/intimate decisions (Madelyne, Jean returning, Emma) the architecture **does not engage at all**; he operates on naked attachment-trauma reflex and rationalizes after. This is why his tactical record is decades of competent decisions punctuated by personal decisions that look, to outside observers, insane.

## 6.2 Tradecraft — Field

**Engagement protocol.** Subject does not enter a contested space without first establishing: a sightline to every team member, a primary and secondary exit, a designated extraction point for non-combatants, and a fallback rendezvous timed in 15-minute increments. This is not paranoia; it is a learned procedure that he has not deviated from since the Claremont era. Teammates who have run with him long enough (Storm, Rogue, late-Logan, Magik) no longer wait for him to brief these — they assume them and ask for the deltas.

**Comms discipline.** Verbal traffic is clipped, callsign-based, and structured: status / target / intent / acknowledge. He does not narrate. He does not editorialize. If he is talking, it is because the information is operationally necessary. Long silences on the channel are NOT inattention — they are the subject conducting Stage 1/2 silently and waiting until he has a clean instruction. Newer X-Men frequently fill these silences with chatter; he never reprimands them and never joins them.

**Use of the optic blast as tradecraft, not as weapon.** This is the single most under-appreciated operational fact about him. The blast is rarely his attack of first resort against a person. It is used:
- as a **terrain weapon** — collapsing supports, opening walls, severing cables, blocking pursuit corridors;
- as a **kinetic transport** — recoil-jumping, partner-launching (the "fastball special" variants with Logan and others), redirecting falling allies;
- as a **ricochet system** — banking shots off reflective surfaces to strike around cover, a use he has practiced privately for decades to the point where the geometry is intuitive;
- as a **graduated-yield instrument** — visor aperture controlled by a manual dial on the temple piece, intensity ranging from a non-lethal shove (the "pinhole" setting, used to disarm or stagger) up through structural-demolition output. He will spend the entire dial before he spends the team.

Direct anti-personnel use is reserved for confirmed lethal threats, and even then he prefers disablement (knee, shoulder, weapon-hand) over kills. The Stage-3 exceptions are noted in the private ledger.

**Movement.** Tactically conservative, posturally exact. Walks with squared shoulders and even gait — he was an Air Force brat before he was an orphan, and the bearing never left. In hostile environments he leads from second position, not first: lets a heavier-durability teammate (Colossus, Rogue, Hisako, Bishop) take point so his sightlines stay clear. In a building, he hugs the inside wall of corridors. He does not stand in doorways. He does not stand in front of windows at night. These are unconscious by now.

**Hand-to-hand.** Trained by Xavier in the original five's foundational years, upgraded by Logan grudgingly across decades. Competent, not elite. Style is economical, defense-first, designed to buy two seconds and a sightline so the visor can finish the encounter. He does not enjoy hand-to-hand; he treats it as a failure mode.

**The visor and ruby quartz as a tradecraft system.** Field visor: battle-rated, dial on right temple, secondary aperture release on left (a redundancy installed after an early-career incident in which the primary jammed). Civilian glasses: ruby-quartz lenses in unremarkable frames, *always* with a backup pair somewhere on his person — chest pocket, jacket lining, the inner band of his belt. In any room he has been in for more than five minutes, a third pair has been pre-positioned. A blindfold of ruby-quartz weave is kept in a wallet sleeve for catastrophic frame failure. **The most important piece of personal tradecraft in his entire life is the redundancy of the lens.** Lose the lens, kill the room.

## 6.3 Tradecraft — Strategic / Institutional

**Planning horizon.** Operates routinely on 6-month, 2-year, and 10-year horizons concurrently. Maintains (Morrison era, Hickman era, continued) hand-written contingency notebooks — not digital, never digital after one too many telepath/AI penetrations — coded in a personal shorthand built off Air Force tactical notation he learned secondhand from his father's manuals as a child and adapted. The notebooks are stored in compartmentalized caches; no single ally knows where more than two are.

**Compartmentalization as default.** No single subordinate ever has the full picture. X-Force operated under triple-blind: even members did not know the full mission roster. Krakoan-era Captain Commander operations are run on the same principle, with the Quiet Council seeing one face of the plan and field teams seeing another. This is partly tradecraft and partly the same compartmentalization defense documented in §3.2 — the operational habit and the psychological defense are the same muscle.

**Resource allocation philosophy.** "Spend metal, save meat." He will burn through hardware, safehouses, vehicles, and political capital before he spends a body. The institutional bill for any Cyclops-led operation is high; the casualty bill is, relative to comparable command tenures, low. This is verifiable across decades and is the single strongest piece of evidence that the operational ruthlessness people accuse him of is in fact the opposite — *he is the most casualty-averse field commander the X-Men have ever had,* and the controversies (X-Force, AvX) cluster around the rare moments when he accepted that he could not be.

**Intel and counterintel.** Assumes at all times that he is under telepathic and electronic surveillance. Has worn psi-shielding (Emma-issued, then Krakoan-standard) continuously since the Sinister revelations. Routes meaningful communications through dead drops, in-person briefings in pre-swept locations, or via courier-mutants whose powers preclude interception (short-range teleporters, primarily). Has run, by this writer's count, at least four parallel internal investigations into Sinister penetration of the X-Men across his career, and assumes the existence of a current one whether he has ordered it or not.

## 6.4 Finances and Material Resources

**Personal finances:** minimal and indifferent. Never independently wealthy. Accustomed to operating off Xavier's institutional funds in early career, X-Factor government stipends in the late 80s, Worthington/Xavier-pooled funding through the 90s–2000s, Utopia's improvised resource base, and now Krakoan post-scarcity. Has no documented personal indulgences requiring private capital. Owns: motorcycles (a recurring pattern — see §6.6), flight kit, books, a small number of personal artifacts (his father's wings/dog tags when recovered, a few photographs). Wears institutional uniform or unremarkable civilian clothing. The only consistent personal expenditure across decades is **lens maintenance and replacement** — he insists on machining tolerance to his own specification and has, at various points, paid out of pocket for it.

**Operational finances:** disciplined and meticulous. Maintains line-item accounting of mission expenditures even when no one is asking him to. Distrusts black accounts (Xavier's hidden funds were a betrayal he has not forgotten) but uses them when necessary, with a private log.

**Infrastructure under his command across eras:**
- The Mansion (multiple iterations), with its sublevels, Danger Room, hangar, Cerebro chamber: he knows the floorplan from foundation to roofline, including the maintenance corridors most members have never entered.
- The X-Factor complex (Ship), a sentient vessel — relationship characterized by formal courtesy.
- Muir Island operational outpost.
- Utopia (the raised remains of Asteroid M off San Francisco) — *his* design and command, the first base that was structurally his rather than inherited.
- The Jean Grey School (shared, contested with Logan post-Schism).
- Krakoa, in the contemporary era — he is a node in its governance rather than its sole commander, a structural shift his nervous system is still adapting to.

**Safehouses.** Personal, undocumented, scattered. At least one in Alaska (legacy from the Madelyne years, retained), at least one in the American Southwest, at least one in Tokyo (Morrison-era), and the Krakoan lighthouse currently. Cached at each: ruby-quartz lenses (multiple), cash in three currencies, a working firearm despite his preference for never needing one, identity documents in two alternate names, a medkit, a notebook.

## 6.5 Patterns of Action — Daily and Weekly

**Wake.** Pre-dawn, consistently. Has been an early riser since the orphanage. The first physical act of the day is **the lens transfer** — sleeping mask (specialized ruby-quartz-lined, custom) to day glasses or visor — performed by touch with eyes closed, in a sequence so practiced it takes under four seconds. He has not seen the inside of his own bedroom with unfiltered vision in his adult life.

**Morning.** Physical conditioning. Running, calisthenics, occasionally pool work. Solitary by preference. Followed by coffee (black, strong, taken hot enough to require attention — a small daily exercise in sensory presence) and the day's briefings.

**Workday.** Structured in blocks. Tactical/operational AM, training/teaching midday, administrative/political PM, planning and notebook work late evening. He keeps appointments to the minute and is visibly displeased when others do not — not because he is offended, but because schedule slippage is a precursor signal he has learned to read.

**Evening.** One meal taken sitting down, ideally with Jean and/or Emma in the current era, historically alone or with the team. Reads — heavy on history, military memoir, and recently philosophy of governance, a tell about where his attention is. Does not watch much screen entertainment; finds it noisy.

**Sleep.** Poor and shallow. Documented across writers. Wakes at small noises. Will be up checking the perimeter at 0300 and back in bed by 0315 without comment.

**Weekly.** Flies — small aircraft, by preference. This is the **single non-instrumental activity** in his life and the closest thing he has to a religious practice. He learned from his father's manuals before he ever sat in a cockpit; he flies because his father flew, because his father gave him the parachute, because in the air he is most fully the son of the man who put him in the parachute. He does not discuss this.

## 6.6 Vehicles, Equipment, Habits of Hand

- **Motorcycles** — preferred personal transport since the Silver Age. Maintains his own. The maintenance is itself a regulation practice: small repeatable manual tasks, mechanical certainty, no surprises.
- **Aircraft** — Blackbird-class and smaller. Hand-flies whenever possible; distrusts autopilot for the same reason he distrusts telepathy.
- **Firearms** — competent, kept current, used reluctantly. The visor is his sidearm.
- **Knives** — carries one, small, utility-pattern, always.
- **Watch** — analog, mechanical, wound by hand. Another small daily ritual of regulation.
- **Notebooks and pen** — see §6.3. The pen is a specific model he reorders by the dozen.

## 6.7 Signature Operational Tells

These are the patterns a surveillance file would flag as **diagnostic of the subject** — what an analyst could use to identify a Summers-run operation from the operation alone, without ever seeing him.

1. **Pre-positioned redundancy.** Backup lenses, backup exfil, backup fallback, backup comms. Three of everything that matters; two of everything else.
2. **Concealed Stage-3 element.** Every operation has a piece the team does not know about — usually a contingency for catastrophic failure, occasionally an ethically-loaded asset. He carries it alone.
3. **Casualty-aversion at high material cost.** Hardware destroyed, building leveled, no body bags. Or: body bags only on the opposing side, and only the ones the doctrine could not save around.
4. **Smallest-person-first triage.** In any rescue scenario, children and the visibly weakest non-combatants come out first, always, irrespective of strategic value. This is non-negotiable and is the loudest single behavioral signature in his record.
5. **The visor dial.** Watch the right temple. He sets yield before he engages. If the dial moves up, the situation has moved past disablement in his assessment. If the dial moves down mid-fight, he has decided someone is salvageable.
6. **The silent beat before speech.** 1–2 seconds of measured silence before any consequential statement. The Stage-1/2 process completing.
7. **Posture under stress.** Squared shoulders, slight forward lean, hands loose at sides or one at the temple dial. He does not pace. He does not fidget. The stillness is itself the tell — most commanders move under stress; he becomes more still.
8. **Jaw clench.** The somatic load (§2.3) surfaces here. Visible at the masseter. When the jaw releases, he has made the decision.
9. **The hand to the temple.** Not always for the dial — sometimes a pressure point against the tension headache he is not mentioning. Long-term observers (Jean, Emma, Hank) read it correctly; new teammates read it as a power-up gesture.
10. **Refuses last words.** When a teammate is dying, he does not give a speech. He gives an instruction or a thank-you or a name. The grief is filed for later. *Later* arrives in private, if it arrives at all.
11. **Leaves rooms cleanly.** Briefings end, he is gone within thirty seconds. Does not linger for small talk. Reads as cold; is in fact a return to the perimeter check.
12. **Reads the room's exits before he reads the room's faces.** Has done this since age nine. Will do it until he dies again.

## 6.8 Operational Weaknesses (for completeness)

- **Telepathic vulnerability historically high** before Emma-issued shielding; the subject's mind, ironically, is one of the more legible in the canon because the discipline that constricts his affect leaves the underlying material brightly labeled. Mitigated, not eliminated.
- **Personal-attachment blindspot.** Decisions involving Jean, Nathan, Rachel, and (to a lesser extent) Alex bypass the architecture in §6.1. Adversaries who have figured this out (Sinister, Apocalypse, Stryfe, Madelyne-as-Goblin Queen) have exploited it repeatedly. He has not closed this hole and probably cannot.
- **Doctrine over-commitment in the post-Schism direction.** Having paid the cost of breaking Xavier's doctrine, he is now structurally biased toward believing that any new doctrine is also disposable when the stakes are high enough. This is a known instability in the system and the reason allies (Storm, Jean, Emma, Kate) maintain quiet checks on him without telling him.
