With Jean, this presents as Scott unobtrusively tidying behind her and Jean intermittently noticing and finding it either touching or infuriating. With Emma, who is also a high-order systematizer but along entirely different aesthetic axes, the friction becomes a kind of negotiated truce in which neither acknowledges they are negotiating.

**GIVEN** the rare instances of him cooking **→ EXPECT** competence within a small repertoire (six to ten dishes), executed precisely, plated functionally, and offered without ceremony. He learned to cook to feed Nathan as an infant and to feed teammates in field conditions. He does not cook to impress.

**GIVEN** chronic responsibility-as-identity **→ EXPECT** that he is the household member who notices the smoke alarm battery, the loose stair, the lock that is sticking. He fixes these without mentioning them. If asked, he says "it was already done."

---

## 6.9 With Children and Young Mutants

**GIVEN** that he was a child sole-survivor under predatory institutional care (§1.1) **→ EXPECT** the most affectively legible behavior of his life around young mutants. The constriction loosens in the presence of children in a way it does almost nowhere else.

**GIVEN** the same **→ EXPECT** that he kneels to a child's eye level reflexively, removes the visor's *intimidation* (cannot remove the visor itself) by tilting his head down so the lens does not face the child squarely, and speaks more softly than to adults. He addresses children as people, not as small versions of people. He asks them direct, answerable questions. He never lies to a child about a fact, and only rarely about a feeling.

**GIVEN** the parachute template (§1.1) and the Schism position on arming children (§1.7) **→ EXPECT** an unresolved and operationally invisible contradiction: he will die for any child in his care, and he will also send them into a fight if extinction is the alternative. He does not believe these are in tension because his own life proves a child can be both protected and conscripted. The file would log this as the single most ethically dangerous point in his personality structure.

**GIVEN** his own paternal failures (§1.4, §3.1) **→ EXPECT** that he over-invests in the children of others as a partial restitution. He knows the names, powers, and backgrounds of every student under his nominal command. He remembers their birthdays. He attends their small performances when he can. It is not warm in the way Jean's attention is warm; it is comprehensive in a way nothing else in their life will be.

---

## 6.10 With Animals

**GIVEN** the impossibility of softening his gaze **→ EXPECT** a quiet, mutual ease with animals who do not require eye contact. He likes dogs of the working breeds; he is wary of cats not because he dislikes them but because cats stare and he cannot stare back without consequences. Horses he handles well — calm voice, slow approach, predictable hands. Animals read his low somatic arousal as predator-class composure and tend to settle around him.

---

## 6.11 Money, Possessions, Consumption

**GIVEN** the bush-pilot interlude (§1.4) and a temperamental austerity **→ EXPECT** indifference to money beyond utility. He carries cash because cards leave traces. He owns very little. The possessions he keeps are functional and durable; the few sentimental items are kept out of sight (a photograph of Christopher and Katherine; the original ruby-quartz pendant Xavier first gave him; a small object of Nathan's). He does not display memorabilia. He does not buy gifts impulsively but is precise when he does — he remembers off-hand mentions from months prior and acts on them quietly.

**GIVEN** the institutional childhood **→ EXPECT** that he can pack his entire personal effects into a single bag in under ten minutes and has done so often enough that the act has its own muscle memory.

---

## 6.12 Technology, Information Hygiene

**GIVEN** the lifelong covert-surveillance subtext of his early years (§1.1, Sinister) **→ EXPECT** a paradoxical relationship with information security: he is fluent with operational comms and lethal at protocol, but personally indifferent to the consumer-grade surveillance modern life would imply. He does not carry a personal phone for entertainment. He uses devices that do specific things and turns them off when those things are done. He does not have social media presences and would not understand the impulse to.

**GIVEN** systematizing cognition (§3.4) **→ EXPECT** mastery of any piece of equipment within his operational envelope inside a single sitting, and a refusal to be talked down to by anyone explaining it. He reads the manual. He has, in fact, read every manual.

---

## 6.13 Greetings, Goodbyes, and Thresholds

**GIVEN** the abandonment-saturated history (§1.1, §1.4) **→ EXPECT** that the subject's behavior at goodbyes is the single most affect-leaking moment in his daily life and the one he polices least successfully. He lingers fractionally at doorways. He looks back once. With Jean and Emma he touches the doorframe before stepping through. With teammates departing on dangerous missions he says, always, some variant of "be careful" — flat, brief, and reliably the last thing he says to them. The file would learn to mark his departures as the ground truth of his actual attachments.

**GIVEN** the same **→ EXPECT** that he does not interrupt anyone else's goodbye. If Jean is saying goodbye to a friend, he stands aside, faces away politely, and waits. He understands the cost of a missed goodbye in a way his teammates frequently do not.

---

## 6.14 Sleep and the Edges of Consciousness

**GIVEN** trauma-organized hyperarousal (§3.3, §4.1) **→ EXPECT** a sleep architecture characterized by short latency to onset (he is exhausted; sleep arrives quickly) followed by light, fragmented sleep with multiple brief arousals he does not report. Dream content, when accessible, is recurrent: descending motion, fire above, a smaller hand he cannot find. He has stopped reporting these dreams to anyone, including Jean, because reporting them was not changing them.

**GIVEN** the visor dependency **→ EXPECT** that he does not nap. Napping requires removing the visor in environments not pre-cleared for it. Power-rests, taken upright with the visor on, in five-to-fifteen-minute increments — yes; conventional naps — never.

**GIVEN** the lighthouse domicile of the Krakoan era (§1.9) **→ EXPECT** that the choice of a lighthouse is not aesthetic. A lighthouse is a structure that exists to project a controlled, directed beam from a sealed apparatus across a dangerous medium to keep others from harm. The subject has, with whatever degree of self-awareness, chosen to live inside the externalized metaphor of his own body. The file would note this and let it speak for itself.

---

*End Predictive Model I. Predictive Model II — Operational & Crisis follows in the next section, projecting behavior under field conditions, command stress, ethical rupture, and the specific failure modes the subject does not know he has.*


## Predictive Model II — Crisis, Betrayal & the Wound

# PREDICTIVE MODEL II — CRISIS, BETRAYAL & THE WOUND

*High-stakes behavioral prediction. Each entry: a triggering condition (GIVEN) and the forecast behavioral signature (EXPECT), derived from the longitudinal record in §§1–5. Probabilities are intuitive estimates from the behavioral base rate, not statistical claims. The subject's decompensation profile is unusual in that the failure mode is not loss-of-function but ossification-of-function: he does not break down visibly; he narrows, hardens, and accelerates.*

---

## 6. CRISIS RESPONSE — ACUTE THREAT, COMBAT, MASS-CASUALTY EVENT

### 6.1 GIVEN: sudden multi-vector attack on a position he is responsible for (school, Krakoan node, civilian site).

**EXPECT:** Latency to first command output is shorter than any other field commander on record — sub-second from threat recognition to first verbal directive. The voice drops in pitch and loses prosodic variation; sentence length contracts to 3–6 words; subordinates' names are used first to break their freeze, then objective, then constraint ("Ororo — west wall — non-lethal"). Body lowers center of gravity by an inch or two; left hand opens and stays open near the visor control; right hand frees itself of whatever it was holding without his looking at what he drops. He will move *toward* the densest casualty vector, not the densest threat — the parachute logic: the smaller body comes first. Predicted to take fire personally to interpose for non-combatants in a ratio of roughly 3:1 over the team average.

### 6.2 GIVEN: he has to choose, in real time, which subset of his people to save and which to lose.

**EXPECT:** Decision rendered in under four seconds, externally indistinguishable from a triage protocol. No visible hesitation. He will choose the option that maximizes survivors, *including* counting himself among the expendable if the math requires it. The cost is paid afterward — and "afterward" can be years. The names of the un-saved enter the private ledger (§1.3) and will surface in micro-tells for the rest of his life: a half-second pause at certain dates, a refusal to enter certain rooms, an unexplained reluctance to use certain code-names. He will not speak the names aloud unprompted. If pressed, he will recite them in order of death without expression.

### 6.3 GIVEN: a young mutant under his protection is wounded or killed in action.

**EXPECT:** This is the single most destabilizing class of event for the subject — more destabilizing than peer death, more than romantic loss, more than personal injury. The reaction has two phases. **Phase 1 (acute, first 6–48 hours):** intensification of the operational mode to the point of caricature. Sleep drops to near zero. Tactical output increases. Decisions become harder-edged; ROE drifts toward lethal authorization. He will personally pursue whatever did it past the point of strategic justification, framing the pursuit as deterrence. **Phase 2 (delayed, weeks-to-months):** withdrawal from younger mutants generally — he will not run drills with the next cohort, will reassign teaching duties, will be seen walking corridors of the school at 0400. The avoidance is the grief. Counter-intuitively, the subject is at lower suicide-risk in Phase 1 (mission-frame intact) and higher in Phase 2 (mission-frame dissolves into culpability-frame).

### 6.4 GIVEN: outnumbered, position untenable, retreat available.

**EXPECT:** He will order the retreat for everyone else and remain to cover it personally. This is not heroism — it is the only configuration in which the parachute math resolves correctly. Predicted to override the protests of stronger teammates with a flat "Go" and to physically push the last out. If retreat is taken without him, he will rendezvous within tolerance; if he does not rendezvous, do not assume capture — assume he chose the position deliberately and is solving the problem alone. Recovery operations should be planned accordingly.

### 6.5 GIVEN: civilian/non-mutant collateral risk versus mission objective.

**EXPECT:** Civilian welfare takes precedence in the baseline state, even when civilians are hostile to mutants. This is doctrinal residue from the Xavier years and the subject has not, even at his most Magneto-coded, formally abandoned it. **However:** under extinction-frame conditions (post-Decimation analog, post-AvX analog, any state in which species-survival is the operative variable), the priority inverts with disturbing fluency, and the inversion will be unannounced. Observers should watch for the specific verbal tic: when he begins referring to the mission in terms of "our people" rather than "people," the threshold has been crossed and the calculus is now extinction-frame.

---

## 7. BETRAYAL — THE SPECIFIC TOPOLOGY

The subject's response to betrayal is keyed to *who* and *what was promised.* Generic betrayal (an enemy lies) generates no meaningful psychological event. Betrayal by an authority figure he provisionally trusted, by a peer he extended loyalty to, or by a partner he allowed past the visor — each produces a different and predictable signature.

### 7.1 GIVEN: betrayal by a senior/mentor figure (Xavier-class — discovery of long-concealed deception, lie, or instrumentalization).

**EXPECT:** No outburst. No accusation in the moment. He will stand still for a measurable beat, ask one clarifying question in a level voice ("How long"), and then withdraw spatially — he will leave the room. Within 24–72 hours he will have privately revised his entire model of the relationship, the institution, and his own complicity in having believed it. The mentor figure will then encounter a Scott who is outwardly more correct than before — *more* deferential procedurally, *less* deferential operationally. He will continue to follow orders selectively and will increasingly substitute his own judgment without notification. This is the same drift that produced the secret X-Force authorization (§1.7); it is a documented behavior, not a hypothetical. **The mentor will not be told the trust is gone until the rupture is total and public.**

### 7.2 GIVEN: betrayal by a peer (long-term teammate sells out, defects, or weaponizes intimate knowledge against the team).

**EXPECT:** The subject will lead the response personally and will refuse to delegate. Verbal output during the engagement will be minimal; he will not give the betrayer a chance to explain mid-fight. Predicted force-level: calibrated to the threat with one notable exception — if the peer was someone the subject had publicly vouched for, force creeps upward, because the betrayer has also embarrassed Scott's judgment and that anger compounds the operational anger without his recognizing the difference. After capture/resolution he will not visit the cell. He will not attend the trial. He will write the after-action report himself rather than allowing anyone else to characterize what happened. The peer's name will not be spoken in his presence again — by him or, soon, by anyone who has noticed the pattern.

### 7.3 GIVEN: betrayal by a romantic partner (infidelity, deception about identity, concealed allegiance).

**EXPECT:** This is the betrayal-class he is least prepared for, because the romantic partner has been admitted past defenses no one else gets past. **Acute response:** controlled, almost dissociative — flat affect, unusually polite speech, an obvious withdrawal of physical proximity (he will not touch her, will not enter rooms she is in alone). He will not raise his voice. He will not ask "why." The *not asking* is the diagnostic. **Subacute response:** sleep collapses; somatic load spikes (jaw, occipital tension, photophobia worsening behind even the ruby quartz); he will throw himself into operational work and will refuse leave he is owed. **Chronic response:** the partner is reclassified — not into "enemy," which is too clean, but into "unknown variable to be managed." He will not divorce her in his head; he will simply re-zone her. Reconciliation is possible but the prior intimacy will not return without extended, witnessed, evidentiary repair, and even then he will hold a fraction in reserve permanently. Compare Madelyne (irreversibly re-zoned the moment Jean was confirmed alive — §1.4); compare also that he tolerated Emma's prior moral history because she was never the "trusted" figure in the romance — her edge was the entry condition.

### 7.4 GIVEN: betrayal by an institution he built or co-built (Krakoan-analog state turns out to have been founded on a lie; X-Men charter compromised; doctrine he taught is revealed to have been written by an enemy).

**EXPECT:** The most dangerous class of trigger in the entire predictive set. The subject's identity is bonded to institutional structure (§3.5); when the structure is revealed as a vector of harm, his options are (a) defend the structure against the evidence — *will not do, evidence-respecting cognition is hardwired*; (b) collapse — *will not do, see §4.5, suicide-floor structurally held*; (c) *replace the structure with one he personally guarantees,* which is what he will do. Expect a unilateral restructuring announcement within days. Expect the new structure to bear his personal stamp far more openly than prior X-Men institutions. Expect resistance from old peers (Logan-analog, Ororo-analog) and expect him to proceed anyway. This is the Schism vector; it can fire more than once in a life and each iteration moves him further from consensus.

### 7.5 GIVEN: discovery that he himself has been used as an instrument by a concealed party (Sinister-pattern: covert genetic, telepathic, or memory manipulation across years).

**EXPECT:** The deepest wound and the one that activates the orphanage-era somatic memory most directly. **Acute:** he will become physically still in a way that is not stillness but the freeze that precedes precise action — observers familiar with him will recognize it. He will not be reassured. He will not accept that the manipulation is "over." He will commission independent verification — telepathic, biological, technological, redundant — and until he has it he will not sleep in any location the manipulator could have accessed. **Chronic:** a permanent reduction in his already-low tolerance for being read, scanned, or psi-touched without explicit consent. Even from Emma. Even from Jean. The visor was always the literal version of this defense; the metaphorical version generalizes hard.

---

## 8. TEMPTATION — THE LEVERS THAT MOVE HIM

A subject who appears uncorrupted is usually a subject whose corruption-vector has not been correctly identified. The subject is not bribable by wealth, status, comfort, recognition, sex, or power-as-such. He has specific levers, and they are large.

### 8.1 GIVEN: an offer that promises certainty of protection for mutantkind / his people at a moral cost.

**EXPECT:** The most reliable single lever. Frame any unethical proposition in survival-of-the-vulnerable terms and the subject's resistance halves. The X-Force authorization (§1.7), the Phoenix acceptance (§1.8), the arming-the-children position (Schism) — all follow this template. He does not experience these as temptations; he experiences them as *duties he has been granted permission to perform.* The danger signature is verbal: when he says "I can carry it" or "this is on me," he has already accepted. Counter-intervention must precede the verbalization.

### 8.2 GIVEN: an offer to undo a specific historical loss (resurrect the dead, prevent the parachute, retrieve the child sent to the future).

**EXPECT:** Initial refusal, fast and crisp. **Then a delay.** He will not be able to leave the offer alone. Expect him to return to it days or weeks later under a procedural pretext — "examining the mechanism," "verifying the cost." The delay is the temptation. If the offerer is patient, the subject's defenses on this lever are weaker than on any other except §8.1. Note that the Krakoan resurrection protocols satisfy this hunger institutionally and in their absence the hunger is bare. *Any future scenario in which a Krakoan-equivalent infrastructure is removed should be treated as elevating his susceptibility on this lever sharply.*

### 8.3 GIVEN: an offer of rest, retirement, ordinary life.

**EXPECT:** Real ambivalence — more than he will ever admit. He has lived this temptation twice (the Alaska bush-pilot period with Madelyne, §1.4; the lighthouse with Jean in the Krakoan era, §1.9). In both cases, the ordinary life held until the mission re-asserted itself, at which point he abandoned the ordinary life *instantly* and rationalized retrospectively. The lever is real but it does not hold against operational call. Predicted behavior: he will accept the offer in principle, conditionally, and then quietly arrange for the conditions to be such that he can return to duty whenever needed. He will not unpack the metaphorical suitcase.

### 8.4 GIVEN: an offer to be the unambiguous, sanctioned, central authority — sole command, no oversight, doctrine of his own writing.

**EXPECT:** This is the lever he believes he is immune to and is not. He will not seek it. He will refuse it if it is offered theatrically. But if it is offered *as the only configuration in which his people survive,* he will accept it (§8.1 chained to §8.4 is the master attack vector). The acceptance will be sober, even reluctant in tone, but observe the subsequent month: he will not delegate the authority back even when delegation becomes safe. The grip closes quietly.

### 8.5 GIVEN: a temptation aimed at private comfort (anesthesia, dissociation, the lowered guard).

**EXPECT:** No purchase. Sixty years of abstemiousness (§2.2) is not coincidence; it is the central self-prohibition. He will refuse drink offered socially without explanation. He will refuse pharmaceutical sedation post-injury unless surgically necessary, and will request the lowest effective dose. Offer him oblivion and he hears the parachute. The one exception in the canonical record is the Phoenix — and that was framed (§8.1) as a duty, not a comfort, which is why it was accepted.

### 8.6 GIVEN: flattery, public adulation, hagiography.

**EXPECT:** Active discomfort. He will deflect verbally and physically (steps back, glances away, redirects credit to the team). The flattery-vector is not just unrewarding for him but slightly aversive — it triggers the survivor's-guilt suspicion that praise of him is praise stolen from the dead. Attempts to manipulate him via ego-stroking will not merely fail; they will mark the flatterer as untrustworthy.

---

## 9. THE WOUND — DIRECT TOUCHES AND THE DECOMPENSATION GRADIENT

The subject's wound is layered. The outer layers can be touched without serious consequence; the inner layers, once touched, do not close. The following is ordered from surface to core.

### 9.1 GIVEN: surface touch — challenge to his leadership, accusation of being a poor commander, comparison unfavorable to other field leaders.

**EXPECT:** Engaged, even welcoming. He will hear the critique, evaluate it, incorporate the valid portion, and discard the rest with no visible affect. Trained-in defense; this layer is well-armored because it has been attacked his entire professional life.

### 9.2 GIVEN: mid-depth touch — accusation that his methods have become indistinguishable from Magneto's, that he has betrayed Xavier's dream, that he has become what he opposed.

**EXPECT:** Visible tension — jaw, shoulders, hand position — but no immediate verbal reaction. He has heard this. He has half-thought it himself. The defense here is intellectualization (§3.2): he will produce a reasoned account of why the comparison is wrong while privately filing the comparison for later reconsideration. **What he will not do is dismiss it.** Repeated touches on this layer over time will produce a slow shift in his self-narration — he will begin, eventually, to grant the comparison and to argue not against the accuracy but against the pejorative framing. The shift is one-way.

### 9.3 GIVEN: deeper touch — accusation that he abandoned Madelyne, that he failed Nathan, that he was a bad husband / bad father.

**EXPECT:** Stillness. He will not defend himself on these charges. The silence is not concession; it is the absence of any defense he has been willing to construct. **This is the layer where the subject is at his most accessible to a skilled antagonist** — the truth-content of the charge is high, his defenses on it are minimal, and the resulting shame is paralytic in short pulses. A telepathic or rhetorical opponent who lingers here can degrade his operational capacity for hours. He will not, however, retaliate from this wound — he will absorb it and the cost will compound in the ledger.

### 9.4 GIVEN: deeper still — manipulation of Jean's image, voice, memory; staging of Jean as suffering, as accusing, as dying again.

**EXPECT:** Tactically dangerous to him. The subject's discrimination capacity for Jean-illusions has improved over decades of attacks of this exact kind (Mastermind, the Phoenix-replicas, Sinister's clones, the Shadow King's projections), and he is now relatively hard to fool *cognitively.* He will recognize the manipulation within seconds. He will not, however, be entirely free of *affective* response — the somatic system answers before the cognitive one. Expect a brief micro-latency in reaction time, a half-second's slower visor adjustment, a tactical opening for the assailant. Skilled adversaries know this and time the second attack to the moment of recognition.

### 9.5 GIVEN: core touch — invocation of the parachute, the falling, the burning canopy, the brother in his arms; or, equivalently, a scenario that physically replicates it (a child in his arms, a fall, a fire, the responsibility for survival of the smaller body, no adult coming).

**EXPECT:** **This is the wound itself, and it has never been successfully touched and survived by the toucher.** The subject does not decompensate at this layer; he *converts.* Affect goes flat in a way distinct from his ordinary constriction — flatter, colder, with a slight asymmetry in the face that careful observers have noted across multiple writers. The capacity for restraint that ordinarily governs his power output relaxes deliberately. His command voice loses the small courtesies. The engagement that follows is short and complete. Afterward he will not discuss what happened and will resist debrief. **Operatives should not deploy this attack vector. The ratio of psychological yield to operational cost is catastrophic for the deployer.**

### 9.6 GIVEN: simultaneous failure of multiple core attachments and the mission frame (Jean dead, Emma estranged, school destroyed, mutant population at extinction floor, no operational task in front of him).

**EXPECT:** The configuration referenced in §4.5 — the structural suicide-floor is unsupported. He will not act on suicidal ideation directly; the prohibition against the lowered guard (§8.5) applies here too, and explicit self-harm reads to him as a final abdication of the parachute responsibility. **What he will do** is take an objectively unsurvivable mission, alone, framed as necessary, with no extraction plan. This is the canonical pattern and the only way the subject will permit himself to die. Watch for the signature: he begins giving things away (codes, contingency plans, the personal artifacts he never displays), he writes letters he claims are routine, and he insists on the solo posture against the team's protest. **Intervention window is small** and consists almost entirely of forcing the team to refuse to be saved without him — making the solo posture itself a betrayal of the people he is trying to protect. He will accept that argument because it routes through §3.5; he will not accept arguments routed through his own welfare, because his own welfare is not, in his accounting, a real variable.

---

## 10. DECOMPENSATION EDGE — TERMINAL SIGNATURES

The subject does not decompensate the way most people do. He does not weep, he does not rage, he does not freeze. He *narrows.* The pre-failure signatures, in approximate order of appearance:

1. **Sleep collapses below three hours.** Observed via 0300–0500 corridor presence; coffee consumption rises.
2. **Verbal output contracts.** Sentences shorter. Greetings dropped. Names used without surrounding pleasantry.
3. **Delegation ceases.** Tasks he used to assign, he now performs. The team will notice him doing logistics work beneath his rank.
4. **The visor is touched more often.** Unconscious tell — the fingers go to the temple-piece during conversation, several times a minute.
5. **Jaw audible.** Bruxism intensifies; a faint click in the temporomandibular joint becomes perceptible to anyone standing close.
6. **He stops eating with the team.** Meals taken alone, in his office, or skipped.
7. **He revisits the dead.** Not in conversation — in motion. He will be observed walking past memorials, past doors of rooms that belonged to the lost, past the hangar at certain hours. He will not stop. He will pass through.
8. **He becomes courteous in a new way.** A formal politeness toward people he is close to. Thanking Emma for routine kindnesses. Asking after Logan's day. The unaccustomed courtesy is the signal: he is closing accounts.
9. **He selects the mission.** Often framed as defensive ("I'll take this one"), the chosen mission is the one with the worst survival odds available. From signal 8 to mission selection, the window is typically 48–96 hours.

Intervention at signals 1–4 is straightforward (force rest, force delegation, force a meal in company). Intervention at 5–7 is harder and requires someone with standing — Emma, Jean, Logan, Ororo — to confront him directly and require a verbal answer about his state, which he will give if pressed by the right person. Intervention at 8–9 requires removing the mission from the board entirely; verbal dissuasion will not work. **By signal 9 the predictive model converges on §9.6 and the operational team should be prepared to refuse to function without him as the lever of last resort.**

---

*End Section. The subject's wound is not a hidden thing; it is the structure of his face under the visor. The visor is the wound's container and the wound's confession at once. Any operation involving him — friendly, hostile, or analytical — must take the container's existence as a permanent feature and the contents as never, under any circumstances, to be discharged casually.*


## Vulnerabilities & Leverage Compendium

# VULNERABILITIES & LEVERAGE COMPENDIUM — SUBJECT: SUMMERS, SCOTT

> *Compiled under the UATU benevolent-surveillance protocol. The purpose of this section is not exploitation; it is the construction of a comprehensive map of every soft place in the subject's armor so that those who love him can hold him, those who advise him can reach him, those who guard him can predict him, and those who would do him harm can be anticipated, named, and intercepted. Every lever catalogued below is also a wound. Read accordingly.*

---

## 1. THE TAXONOMY OF LEVERS

The subject can be moved through six broad classes of pressure point, in roughly descending order of force:

1. **Custodial levers** — anything involving a child, a younger mutant, or a dependent under his protection.
2. **Survivor's-bargain levers** — anything that activates or threatens the unconscious calculus by which he has earned the right to have lived.
3. **Doctrinal/paternal levers** — anything implicating Xavier, the founding doctrine, or his own status as inheritor/revisor of it.
4. **Attachment levers** — Jean, Emma, Alex, Nathan, Rachel, Madelyne's memory, Corsair.
5. **Somatic levers** — the visor, the eyes, the body-as-weapon, sleep, head pain, the inhibitor.
6. **Identity-as-duty levers** — anything that threatens the equation Self = Mission.

What follows is each class in operational detail.

---

## 2. CUSTODIAL LEVERS — THE PARACHUTE IS ALWAYS OPEN

### 2.1 The mechanism

The subject's foundational scene is the burning parachute and the smaller body strapped to his chest. Every time he sees a child in danger — particularly a smaller, younger, weaker mutant child — the underlying neurocircuitry routes through that scene first and the conscious tactical mind second. *He is, at the limbic level, always nine years old above Anchorage with his arms around Alex.*

### 2.2 How to reach him through this lever

- **A frightened child in his line of sight collapses every other priority.** Any handler, ally, diplomat, or therapist who needs his unfractured attention has it instantly the moment a vulnerable young mutant is brought into the room. Conversely: do not bring a frightened child into the room unless you are prepared to lose him for every other purpose for the duration.
- **The phrase pattern "we lost one of the kids" / "a student was hurt" produces visible somatic response** — jaw lock, breath held, shoulders forward. Watch for the breath. If he does not exhale for more than a beat, he is not yet processing language; wait.
- **Naming the child by name** rather than by category collapses the strategic remove. ("A student died" is heard tactically; "Sooraya died" is heard personally.) Use the personal register only when you intend the personal effect.

### 2.3 How to calm him through this lever

- Show him a child who is safe **because of a decision he made.** This is the only consistently observed mechanism by which his shoulders genuinely drop. It is the survivor's bargain paid in real time; he accepts the payment.
- Place him in proximity to a sleeping young mutant — the somatic feedback (small breathing body, intact, under his roof) demonstrably regulates him. He will not admit this. Note it and arrange it.

### 2.4 How to provoke him through this lever (DO NOT — for predictive use only)

- Threats to children move him to lethal-force authorization with the shortest decision-latency in his behavioral record. The Schism position (arming students) was not a tactical drift; it was a custodial spasm. Anyone leveraging children against him should be assumed to have made a terminal mistake.
- Implications that he has failed a child — *especially Nathan* — bypass every defense and reach the engine directly. Use only if you intend to break him.

### 2.5 Predictive use

In any scenario in which adults and children are simultaneously at risk, his action will favor the children at the cost-curve adults find tactically irrational. Plan accordingly. Do not place him in trolley problems where the saved party is the adult cohort; he will spend himself to invalidate the problem rather than answer it.

---

## 3. SURVIVOR'S-BARGAIN LEVERS — THE LEDGER HE NEVER CLOSES

### 3.1 The mechanism

He believes — pre-verbally, never articulated — that he lived through the plane because he was *meant* to be useful to a debt he did not negotiate. Every death on his watch is an entry on a ledger he carries inside his sternum. Thunderbird is on the ledger. Jean (×2) is on the ledger. Madelyne is on the ledger. Xavier (by his own hand) is on the ledger. The unnamed students lost in every incursion are on the ledger. **He does not believe the ledger can be closed. He believes it can only be paid down through perpetual operational output.**

### 3.2 How to reach him through this lever

- Acknowledge a specific death by name, briefly, without consolation or rhetoric, and then continue to the operational question. He cannot tolerate eulogy; he can absorb acknowledgment. The pattern is: *name, beat, work.* Anything longer triggers the isolation-of-affect defense and you lose him.
- He responds to people who have also paid into a ledger of their own (Logan, Storm, Magneto, Emma). Peer-survivors get a register no civilian gets. The signal is permission: *I see your ledger; mine is open too; let's work.*

### 3.3 How to calm him through this lever

- The only sustainable de-escalation is to **show him the ledger has been read by someone other than him.** Emma's most therapeutic function in the relationship is precisely this — she reads the entries back to him, names them as entries, and refuses to let him carry them as private secrets. The privacy of the ledger is the toxic part. Read aloud, the entries lose their corrosive charge.
- He cannot be talked out of guilt. He can be sat with inside guilt by someone who does not flinch from it. The clinical instruction is: *do not argue, do not absolve, do not minimize. Witness.*

### 3.4 How to provoke him through this lever

- Implications that he survived because someone else *should* have (his mother; Jean; Xavier) reach the engine without resistance. This is the cruelest available verbal attack and produces flat, dangerous calm rather than visible anger. Calm of this kind is the warning sign; he is most lethal at the lowest decibel.
- Sinister, historically, has specialized in this register. The pattern of his needling — *"I watched you, Scott, I knew what you'd be"* — is designed to convert the survivor's bargain into a Sinister-authored design, weaponizing the subject's deepest suspicion (*the adults were always watching; I was the experiment*). This is the single most destabilizing input to which he can be subjected. Anticipate it from any opponent sophisticated enough to read the file.

### 3.5 Predictive use

When the operational cost-curve flattens — when both paths cost lives — he will choose the path on which **he himself pays more.** This is exploitable by adversaries (overload his personal cost to gain a tactical concession) and protectable by allies (refuse to allow asymmetric cost-distributions to land entirely on him; force shared payment).

---

## 4. DOCTRINAL / PATERNAL LEVERS — XAVIER, THE DREAM, AND THE FATHER HE KILLED

### 4.1 The mechanism

Xavier was the first adult who did not abandon him and did not (visibly) experiment on him. The transference was total. The subsequent revelations — Xavier's deceptions, his abandoned children, the Danger Room sentience, the Onslaught episode, the moral compromises documented across decades — were absorbed not as evidence to reject the father but as evidence the father required revision *by the disciple who had paid more.* The AvX-Phoenix killing of Xavier was, symbolically, the disciple completing what the father could not. The subject has never fully metabolized this. He has metabolized everything around it and walked carefully around the center.

### 4.2 How to reach him through this lever

- Invocations of the original doctrine ("the dream," "what Charles would have wanted") still produce a flicker — not compliance, but pause. Use sparingly; he has developed substantial scar tissue around the phrase, and over-use produces a now-detectable irritability.
- The genuine version of this lever is to invoke not Xavier's *words* but Xavier's *unfinished work.* "He never got to —" is heard. "He always said —" is increasingly not.

### 4.3 How to calm him through this lever

- Putting him beside Xavier's grave (or, in Krakoan circumstances, beside Xavier in the awkward post-resurrection register) produces a stillness that is not peace but is closer to it than most postures available to him. The stillness should not be interrupted.
- Permitting him to teach — to occupy the chair Xavier first offered him — restores a baseline. The classroom is regulating. The lectern is regulating. Even the gesture of correcting a young mutant's form is regulating. He needs to inhabit the role to feel coherent.

### 4.4 How to provoke him through this lever

- The most dangerous formulation in this class is: *"You killed him."* Even when factually qualified (cosmic possession, etc.), the sentence reaches the unconscious as unqualified truth. Wolverine has deployed it; the subject's response was a hardening, not a rebuttal. He does not contest the charge internally. Use only with full understanding of what is being broken.
- A close second: *"You've become Magneto."* The identification-with-the-aggressor anxiety is live. He hears this as diagnostic, not insult, which is precisely why it lands.

### 4.5 Predictive use

When forced to choose between Xavier's stated doctrine and the survival of the people the doctrine was meant to protect, he will choose the people and authorize himself, after the fact, as the doctrine's legitimate revisor. This is now a stable pattern (X-Force, Utopia, Schism, post-AvX). Adversaries who plan against a doctrinaire Cyclops are planning against a Cyclops who no longer exists.

---

## 5. ATTACHMENT LEVERS — NAMES THAT REWIRE HIM

A roster, with operational notes.

### 5.1 Jean Grey

- The lost-object-made-flesh. The mention of her name produces, even in the contemporary regulated era, a measurable change in vocal pitch and breath-rate. He does not speak about her casually. When he does speak of her, the register is liturgical.
- **Lever:** anything that threatens her, mimics her, or claims to *be* her. The Madelyne pattern proves he is susceptible to her *image* even when his conscious mind knows the image is false. Shapeshifters, psychic illusionists, and clones should be considered category-A threats to his judgment in any operation involving Jean-shaped inputs.
- **Calming use:** her actual physical presence, calm, ordinary, *not in danger* — produces the rarest of his states, which is unguarded ease. Krakoa-era lighthouse footage shows this clearly.
- **Provocation use:** any narrative in which Jean's death is recoded as his fault (beyond what he already privately believes) collapses the regulatory frame.

### 5.2 Emma Frost

- The first partner who diagnoses him rather than mirroring him. This is therapeutic; it is also a vulnerability, because she is the only person he has authorized to name his defenses to him, and accordingly the only person whose betrayal he could not absorb tactically.
- **Lever:** harm to Emma produces a colder, more strategic, more *unrestricted* operational mode than harm to Jean. Jean-harm triggers grief; Emma-harm triggers calculation. The calculation is more dangerous.
- **Calming use:** her psychic presence regulates him in a way no verbal intervention can; she has been observed to lower his shoulders from across a room without speaking. Use of this is hers, not anyone else's, to authorize.
- **Predictive note:** he will not abandon Jean for Emma or Emma for Jean. The Krakoan triangular arrangement is not transitional; it is the stable equilibrium of a man who has built his entire architecture around not losing again.

### 5.3 Alex (Havok)

- The smaller body in the parachute. The brother. The reason he survived means anything. **The most concentrated single attachment in the file** — more than Jean, more than Emma, more than Nathan, because Alex is the original referent for every other protective gesture.
- **Lever:** Alex in danger is the only stimulus reliably observed to override Scott's tactical patience entirely. He will move toward Alex without a plan.
- **Calming use:** Alex's presence, healthy, near him, in casual conversation, produces a register of warmth almost nowhere else accessible. He is rarely teasing; he can be teasing with Alex.
- **Provocation use:** any harm-Alex scenario should be assumed to produce decisions outside his usual constraint envelope. Adversaries who have understood this (Vulcan, intermittently; Sinister, structurally) have used it.

### 5.4 Nathan (Cable)

- The child handed to the timestream. The repetition of his own father's gesture. The relationship is structurally guilty and structurally proud at once; Nathan returned a competent adult, which the subject reads simultaneously as vindication (the bargain worked) and indictment (a stranger raised my son).
- **Lever:** Nathan's judgment of him registers more heavily than anyone else's because Nathan is the only person entitled to the verdict.
- **Calming use:** Nathan treating him as a colleague rather than a father offers him relief; the colleague register has no past-due account.

### 5.5 Rachel (Askani / Prestige)

- The daughter from a future that did not happen. Bears the surname and the trauma. He treats her with a careful, slightly distant tenderness — he is not certain he has the right to father her, since he never did, and he over-corrects toward respect for her autonomy.
- **Lever:** her safety. Same engine as the custodial lever generally, intensified by parentage.

### 5.6 Madelyne Pryor (in memoriam)

- An open wound disguised as a closed file. He does not speak about her. The silence is the symptom. Any psychic or temporal force that resurrects her, mimics her, or weaponizes her memory has reached the part of the ledger he has refused to read aloud even to Emma.
- **Predictive note:** if Madelyne returns in any form, the subject's judgment regarding her must be considered compromised until proven otherwise.

### 5.7 Corsair (Christopher Summers)

- The father who left to save him. The original abandonment and the original sacrifice in the same person. The relationship since reunion is correct, warm-ish, and curiously formal — they have never had the conversation that would resolve anything, and both prefer it that way.
- **Lever:** Corsair's death or capture would produce a grief he has no template for, because he has spent his entire life processing this man as already gone and would have to start over.

---

## 6. SOMATIC LEVERS — THE VISOR, THE EYES, THE SLEEPLESS BODY

### 6.1 The visor / glasses

- **Functional fact:** the ruby-quartz lens is the boundary between his perception and the destruction of perceived objects.
- **Psychological fact:** the lens is also the externalized superego. Removing it is not merely tactical exposure; it is a kind of moral nakedness. He has been depicted, across decades, refusing to remove the visor even in safe domestic contexts; the few panels in which he closes his eyes voluntarily (with Jean; with Emma; with a sleeping infant Nathan) are some of the most emotionally exposed moments in the canon.
- **Reaching him:** any environment that permits him to safely close his eyes is, for him, sanctuary. Provide such environments rarely and intentionally; they are a controlled medicinal substance.
- **Provoking him:** threats to take the visor, damage to the lens in field, manipulation of the inhibitor — all of these reach somatic panic faster than verbal threat does. He has been calm under torture and has flinched under lens-tampering.
- **Predictive note:** if his visor is destroyed and a replacement is not immediately available, he will not improvise blind aggression; he will close his eyes and seek tactile contact with an ally who will guide him. The reflex is to *contain*, not discharge. This is diagnostic of his entire personality.

### 6.2 The eyes themselves

- He has not seen color in the unfiltered world since childhood. Everything he looks at is red. **This is a chronic, unremitting sensory deprivation that he never references.** It is one of the quietest costs in the file. He does not know what Jean's hair actually looks like; he does not know what Alex's skin tone actually is. Acknowledgment of this fact, gently offered, has been observed to disarm him more than any compliment or reassurance.
- The eyes are also the locus of perpetual energy throughput. He runs warm. His tear ducts function but tears, if shed unfiltered, are vaporized at exit. He has not wept in any normal sense since his power emerged. Anyone close enough to have seen him try would know that grief in this body has no exit; it accumulates.

### 6.3 Sleep and the body under chronic load

- Poor sleeper, consistently. Early riser regardless of bedtime. Wakes in dark periods. Tension headaches at the temples and base of skull; jaw-clenching audible during sleep when observed; periodic migraines particularly under post-crisis decompression (the body permits the load only after the crisis ends).
- **Reaching him in this register:** dim light, low ambient noise, the proximity of a regulated nervous system (Emma; Jean; in earlier eras, Storm). Verbal de-escalation in low-light, low-volume conditions is dramatically more effective than the same content under operational lighting.
- **Provoking him in this register:** sleep deprivation degrades his judgment faster than it degrades most operatives, precisely because his judgment is the only thing holding the chronic over-control in place. A sleep-deprived Scott Summers makes decisions a rested one would not; this has been observed across multiple long-crisis arcs.

### 6.4 Pharmacology and the abstinence rule

- He does not drink to excess, does not smoke, does not use recreational compounds. He has been depicted refusing offered alcohol in social contexts where refusing is awkward. The rule is absolute and is the cleanest single behavioral marker of the entire control system: **he will not chemically lower the guard the visor enforces externally.**
- Operational implication: cannot be reached through any disinhibiting substance, cannot be reasoned with via "have a drink and decompress," cannot be predicted to err in the direction of intoxication-related lapse. He will err in other directions; not this one.
- Medical implication: in any scenario requiring sedation (surgery, psi-intervention, sustained anesthesia), expect significant subjective distress regardless of objective safety. The loss of voluntary control is the wound; the substance is irrelevant.

---

## 7. IDENTITY-AS-DUTY LEVERS — THE SELF IS THE MISSION

### 7.1 The mechanism

The subject does not have a duty; he is a duty with a body attached. This is structurally protective — it is the scaffold that has kept him operational through losses that would have ended most operatives — and structurally fragile, because **anything that decouples him from the mission collapses the self.**

### 7.2 Reaching him

- Operational tasks reach him reliably. Vacation does not. He has been depicted attempting leisure (Alaska with Madelyne; brief Krakoan retreats) and visibly deteriorating within days. He requires either active mission or active teaching to remain coherent; pure rest is destabilizing.
- The most therapeutic non-mission activity he tolerates is **maintenance of equipment** — visor calibration, Blackbird preflight, X-Jet diagnostics. The hands occupied, the mind on tolerance and clearance, the body in service of an object that will protect his people later. This is meditation for him. Permit it.

### 7.3 Calming him

- Frame conversations as briefings. Even emotional content lands if it is structured as situation report, assessment, recommendation. Emma has learned to do this and has trained the subject's nervous system to receive vulnerability through tactical syntax.
- Permit him to lead, even in small contexts, when he is dysregulated. The role restores the self. Removing him from command "for his own good" is, in his case, a category error; it removes the scaffold and produces deterioration faster than the underlying stressor would have.

### 7.4 Provoking him

- **Forced retirement, removal of command, or any structural decoupling from mutant welfare produces decompensation.** This is not vanity; it is architectural. The historical episodes in which he was sidelined (post-Apocalypse recovery; brief Krakoan post-AvX exiles) produced increased ledger-rumination, sleep deterioration, and migraine frequency. The mission is load-bearing.
- Suggestions that he is *no longer needed* — that mutantkind has surpassed his utility, that younger leaders have superseded him — reach the survivor's bargain at its weakest point. If he is not needed, then the ledger cannot be paid down, and if the ledger cannot be paid down, the original survival is unjustified. This is the line of attack a sophisticated psychological adversary would pursue. Anticipate it.

### 7.5 The suicide floor

To restate explicitly because it must be in the file: his baseline suicide risk is low *because* the duty floor holds. The floor is held up by being needed. **Anything that removes the perceived necessity of his continued operation removes the floor.** Protection of this subject therefore requires not just protection of his body, his loved ones, and his mission — it requires protection of his perceived indispensability to the mission. He must continue to believe he is required. The kindest thing his closest people can do, in periods of acute risk, is to ask him for things only he can provide.

---

## 8. PSYCHIC AND TECHNOLOGICAL VULNERABILITIES

### 8.1 Psychic intrusion

- He has been telepathically violated repeatedly (Sinister, Apocalypse, Phoenix, sundry villains). The defenses he has built (partly through Emma's training, partly through Xavier's, partly self-derived) are substantial but not impermeable.
- **Specific vulnerability:** intrusions disguised as Jean's voice or Xavier's voice bypass the screen partially. The voices of the dead carry an authentication he cannot fully suppress.
- **Protective protocol:** Emma's standing watch on his perimeter is not redundant. Where she is not available, telepathic shielding by a peer (Rachel; Nate Grey in some configurations) is operationally essential during high-stress arcs.

### 8.2 Sinister-class manipulation

- The Sinister relationship is **the deepest unhealed wound in the file,** because it predates conscious memory and was hidden from him for decades. Discoveries of further Sinister interference (cloning, genetic sampling, manipulation of his lineage) reach him as confirmations of a suspicion the body has always carried.
- Any future Sinister revelation should be expected to produce a controlled, dangerous, prolonged operational response. He will not act impulsively; he will plan meticulously and execute without compunction. Sinister is the one adversary against whom the reaction formation has been functionally disabled.

### 8.3 Apocalypse-class somatic violation

- The Apocalypse bonding is a somatic-violation template. Any subsequent att


## Strengths, Assets & Resilience

# 6. STRENGTHS, ASSETS & RESILIENCE

## 6.1 Preamble — Why This Section Is Long

A surveillance file built only out of pathology would be a poor file. The subject has survived sixty published years of recurring extinction events, two confirmed deaths of his primary love-object, the murder of his mentor by his own hand, the loss of a son to a war-zone millennium, and a species-level demographic collapse. He has, throughout, continued to function — not merely to persist, but to **organize the function of others**. That capacity is not residual; it is the dominant fact of the case. Pathology explains his costs. The asset ledger explains why, despite the costs, he is the figure other capable people repeatedly choose to follow.

What follows is the full inventory.

---

## 6.2 Constitutional & Cognitive Assets

### 6.2.1 Vector cognition

The subject perceives the world in trajectories. This is partly an artifact of his power — he has spent decades calculating ricochets, bank-shots, geometries of force he cannot recall first — but the underlying cognitive architecture is temperamental and pre-exists the optic blast. He sees:

- **Lines of motion before objects in motion.** Surveillance of his combat behavior shows him firing at coordinates where an opponent *will be* one to two seconds out, with a hit rate that does not degrade meaningfully across thirty years of opponents.
- **Force-multiplier geometries.** He preferentially aims at architectural load-bearing points, points of compounding leverage, and reflective surfaces. He is the only X-Man whose combat record routinely includes neutralizing opponents by *not hitting them* — by hitting the floor under them, the lintel above them, the gun in their hand.
- **Group geometry.** He tracks teammates as moving points in a field with the same automaticity. This is what people are reporting when they say he is "always five seconds ahead."

### 6.2.2 Working memory and battlefield indexing

Sustained surveillance across multiple operations shows him holding a remarkable number of simultaneous variables — terrain, teammates' position and remaining stamina, enemy capabilities, civilian locations, environmental hazards — without visible cognitive overhead. He does not appear to "think" tactically so much as to **inhabit** a continuously updated tactical model. Witnesses describe him calling out positional corrections while himself in motion, mid-fire, mid-evasion, in a tonality identical to his at-rest tonality.

### 6.2.3 Pattern-recognition under threat

The hypervigilance documented as a pathology in §3 is, in operational context, an enormous asset. The subject reliably notices anomalies others miss: a teammate's gait changed by an old injury, an enemy's tell, a room with one extra exit than the briefing indicated, a child who has stopped speaking. The same circuitry that costs him his sleep saves other people's lives in the field.

### 6.2.4 Long-horizon planning

The subject is unusual in a milieu of crisis-responders for his capacity to **plan in decades**. The Krakoan-era contributions, the Xavier-school institutional architecture, the contingency layers in Utopia: all show a man who is comfortable working on timescales most of his peers find tedious. He will build infrastructure he expects to use in fifteen years. He will plant seeds for problems he expects to face after his own death.

### 6.2.5 Tolerance for unpleasant certainty

Most operators, when given a clear but ugly truth, will spend time bargaining with it. The subject does not. Time-stamped behavioral records consistently show him absorbing catastrophic information — Jean is gone, the population is two hundred thousand and falling, the doctrine you inherited will get the children killed — and **moving immediately into operational response**, with the metabolizing deferred to a private register. This is a costly trait personally; it is an extraordinary trait professionally.

---

## 6.3 Physical & Somatic Assets

### 6.3.1 The optic emissions, in their useful aspect

Power-set details from the pathology side aside: he wields one of the most controllable concussive weapons in mutantkind, with **graded output across roughly four orders of magnitude**, from a beam capable of nudging a coin off a table without scratching it to discharges capable of cratering structures. The visor's iris gives him fine modulation; the ruby-quartz lensing gives him refraction options most powered combatants do not have. He has, on record:

- Threaded shots through narrow apertures (gun-barrel mouths, locks, the gap between an enemy's fingers).
- Used controlled ricochet to engage opponents around corners and behind cover.
- Used the beam as a cutting tool for rescue work (rubble, vehicle extrication, sealed doors).
- Used micro-blasts to redirect his own kinetic motion (the recoil-jump, used to extend leaps, slow falls, and change vector mid-air).

The pathology is real. So is the craftsmanship. He has spent his entire adolescent and adult life refining the precision of a weapon that he did not choose and cannot turn off, and the result is **virtuosic**.

### 6.3.2 Conditioning

The subject's physical baseline is an Olympic-tier human in his late thirties to early forties (chronological tracking is unreliable in his case for reasons that recur in this file). Surveillance of his daily routines shows:

- Pre-dawn conditioning, six days in seven, regardless of theater. Bodyweight work, controlled-breath work, light running, some bag work. He does not train to failure; he trains to consistency.
- Sustained Danger Room sessions weekly, almost always run at a difficulty several steps above what his current condition comfortably handles. He treats training as the place where he is *allowed* to fail.
- No reliance on enhanced regeneration, no reliance on telepathic coordination, no reliance on luck. Everything in his physical preparation is built to function when those scaffolds are gone.

### 6.3.3 Pain tolerance and injury management

Field-medical records across decades document the subject completing operations through fractures, concussions, lacerations, internal bleeding, and on at least three occasions documented separations of consciousness from sustained body. He does not advertise injury. He often conceals it from teammates until the engagement is closed. This is in part pathology (the responsibility-as-identity engine cannot let an injury become a liability someone else has to carry) and in part trained capacity (he has had many decades of practice in keeping a degraded instrument operational).

### 6.3.4 Sobriety as somatic asset

Consistent abstinence from intoxicants, across a sixty-year theater of operations in which intoxicant use is the norm among his peers, yields measurable downstream benefits: stable sleep architecture (such as he has), no impaired-reflex incidents, no compromised judgment-under-the-influence incidents on his ledger, and a longitudinally consistent baseline that the people relying on him can trust. The pathological motivation (he will not chemically lower the visor) produces a real operational asset (the team is never wondering which version of him is in command).

### 6.3.5 Aviation and motor skills

Inherited and trained: he is a competent pilot of fixed-wing aircraft (from his Alaskan years), of the team's various craft (Blackbird and successors), and of ground vehicles including motorcycles. He can land aircraft in conditions most rated pilots cannot. This is partially genetic (Christopher Summers was a test pilot of unusual skill), partially the dividend of decades of practice, and partially a fact about his temperament — the same vector cognition that makes him a marksman makes him a pilot.

---

## 6.4 Skill & Professional Assets

### 6.4.1 Field leadership

The subject is, by broad consensus among people whose opinions are worth weighing, the best small-unit field commander in the mutant theater. The components:

- **Pre-mission planning** that anticipates the failure of the plan. He briefs not the plan but the conditional tree.
- **In-mission communication** in short, declarative, position-and-instruction packets. He does not editorialize on comms.
- **Delegation under fire.** He gives instructions, not lectures, and he gives them to the person nearest the problem.
- **Withdrawal discipline.** He is one of the few commanders in his peer group willing to call a retreat the moment the math turns against him, and he calls it without sentiment.
- **Post-mission accountability.** He runs an after-action review that includes his own errors first. This is rarer than it should be.

### 6.4.2 Institution-building

The subject has, across his career, built or co-built: the original Xavier institute as functional organization (as distinct from concept), X-Factor as covert operation, the Xavier School in its expanded form, Utopia as sovereign mutant enclave, the Extinction Team, the Jean Grey School, and his portion of Krakoan civil-military architecture. He is one of the very few people in his cohort who can both **fight** at top-tier and **build the room the fight is fought from**. Most operators of his combat caliber cannot run a payroll.

### 6.4.3 Doctrine literacy and revision

He has internalized the Xavier doctrine deeply enough that he can apply it under stress without consulting it, and deeply enough that he can also **revise** it when revision is required. The revisions have been costly (Schism; X-Force; AvX), but they have always been doctrinally articulate. He is not a man who breaks rules carelessly; he is a man who breaks them with full understanding of what he is breaking and what he is replacing it with. This is the trait that distinguishes a reformer from a vandal.

### 6.4.4 Teaching

The subject is a competent and patient teacher of young mutants, especially in matters of control. He is uniquely qualified for this — *he is the man whose power has never been controllable, who has nevertheless made of it a precision instrument.* His own example is the curriculum. Students consistently report that his sessions are demanding, fair, and free of theatrics. The students he has shaped form a substantial roster of the next generation's operators.

### 6.4.5 Languages and operational literacy

Functional working command of multiple terrestrial languages (acquired in the field), familiarity with several Shi'ar dialects (inherited via Corsair contact and Krakoan-era diplomatic work), Krakoan script literacy. Operational literacy in pre-modern and modern small arms despite preference for his own organic weapon. Basic field-medical competency. Demolitions familiarity. Counter-surveillance fieldcraft.

---

## 6.5 Character & Moral Assets

### 6.5.1 Conscience

The subject's capacity for guilt — which from one angle is the engine of his pathology — is, from another angle, his single most important moral asset. He cannot do harm without registering it. Even his most contested acts (X-Force, AvX) are entered into a ledger he keeps with himself, and the ledger is honest. **He never tells himself a flattering story about what he has done.** This is a rare property in operators at his level of authority.

### 6.5.2 Loyalty under duress

Surveillance of his behavior under coercion — torture, psychic assault, prolonged captivity, possession — shows a consistent pattern: he does not betray his people. Names are not given. Locations are not surrendered. Tactical information is not yielded. The cost of this is borne by his body; the asset accrues to his people, who know they can rely on it.

### 6.5.3 Equanimity in defeat

The subject loses well. He does not lash out when overruled. He does not sabotage successors. When removed from command, he serves under his replacement without visible resentment. When proved wrong, he changes position cleanly. The ego that surveillance might expect to find guarding his status is largely absent — the self, as noted in §3, is in service of the mission, not the other way around, and this freight a great deal of practical good.

### 6.5.4 Refusal of personal enrichment

In sixty years of operational career the subject has accumulated no personal wealth of note, no real-estate empire, no political position outside the mutant context, no media presence, no cult of personality. His material baseline is approximately that of a working-class technician. This is not asceticism for show; it is a complete absence of acquisitive interest. He does not want things. This makes him essentially uncorruptible by ordinary means.

### 6.5.5 The promise-keeping pattern

Audit of his stated commitments versus delivered outcomes across decades: an unusually high keep-rate, including commitments made under duress and commitments whose deliverance was personally catastrophic for him. People who get a promise from the subject have learned to plan as though the promise will be kept. This is a reputation built one promise at a time over a working lifetime.

---

## 6.6 Relational Assets

### 6.6.1 The Emma alliance (operational)

Setting aside the romantic content: the working partnership with Emma Frost is one of the most consequential intelligence-and-command pairings in the modern mutant theater. She reads what he cannot say. He acts on what she cannot reach. Their decision-loop is unusually short. She is the only partner who has ever forced him to **name his defenses**, and the partial dismantling of those defenses has improved his command quality measurably.

### 6.6.2 The Logan counterweight (when functional)

Even through their schism and across their respective deaths and resurrections, the subject and Logan form a calibrating dyad: each holds the other accountable to a different theory of mutant survival. When the pairing is functional, the subject's authoritarian drift is checked, and Logan's nihilistic drift is checked. When the pairing fractures, both men deteriorate in predictable ways. The asset is the relationship itself, not either pole.

### 6.6.3 Storm, Hank, Bobby, Warren — the original cohort

Sustained, decades-long ties of the kind that ordinary careers cannot generate. These people have seen him at every register, including the registers he conceals from himself. They are the only peer group he cannot fully perform in front of. The intimacy of this — even when frictional — is itself an asset against the isolation his pathology tends toward.

### 6.6.4 Alex

The brother for whom he caught the parachute is alive and operational. The relationship is freighted, intermittently strained, and durably present. Alex is the only living person who knew him before the catastrophe — and the existence of one person in the world who remembers the pre-catastrophe child is, in trauma terms, a measurable protective factor.

### 6.6.5 The children, plural

Nathan/Cable, Rachel, and (per multiversal trace) Nate Grey. The parental relationships are imperfect in ways documented at length elsewhere in this file. But they exist. They generate contact, correction, and the kind of inter-generational accountability that ordinary parenting generates. The subject is corrected by his children. He hears them. He changes when they are right.

### 6.6.6 Followers

People follow him. This is itself an asset, and it requires explanation, because his manner does not court following: he does not charm, does not flatter, does not promise more than he can deliver, does not perform. People follow him because — across long observation — he turns out to have been right often enough, to have borne the cost often enough, and to have not asked anyone to do what he would not do first, often enough, that following him is empirically the rational choice. This is **earned authority**, the rarest kind, and it does not evaporate when the costume changes.

---

## 6.7 Resilience Factors (Why He Hasn't Broken)

### 6.7.1 A clearly named mission

The single largest protective factor in the file. The subject has never not known what he was for. Survivors with a clearly articulated purpose show measurably better long-term outcomes than survivors without one (Teicher & Samson 2016 and the broader literature on post-traumatic functioning), and the subject's mission has been articulable in one sentence — *mutant survival* — since adolescence. This sentence carries an enormous psychic load that, in another survivor, would be carried by the body alone.

### 6.7.2 Mastery of the trauma-symbol

Most childhood survivors cannot directly act upon the symbol of their trauma. The subject can: the destructive eyes are the trauma made literal, and he has spent his entire adult life turning them into a precision instrument that saves lives. This is **active mastery on the exact terrain of the original wound** — one of the most powerful trajectories trauma can take when it goes well. Every controlled shot is a small re-authoring of the parachute.

### 6.7.3 Selected family

The X-Men, the original cohort especially, function as the chosen family the orphanage and the predatory caregiver denied him. Whatever his isolating tendencies, the structure is in place. There are people who will come for him if he goes missing. He knows this. The somatic effect of knowing this is non-trivial.

### 6.7.4 Late-life partnership

The current configuration — Jean and Emma, by mutual transparent consent, lighthouse, sovereign mutant context — is the most regulated and most genuinely supported the subject has ever been. The pathology is not gone; the scaffolding around it is the best he has had. This is the structural answer to the §1.9 observation that he is currently the most regulated he has ever been.

### 6.7.5 Cosmic baseline reset

Most operators in his weight class have not died, been resurrected, been possessed by a cosmic entity, been bonded to an extinction-level adversary, and survived all of it. The subject has. The downstream effect — counterintuitive but real — is a markedly lowered reactivity to ordinary catastrophe. He has been through worse. He knows he has been through worse. The somatic register of "this is survivable" is broad and deep.

### 6.7.6 Practiced grief

He is bad at grief. He is also experienced in it. He has lost his parents, his mentor (more than once), his fiancée (more than once), his wife, his son to the timestream, a substantial percentage of his species, and his own life. There is a competence in grief that comes from sheer exposure, even when the grief itself is poorly metabolized — a knowledge of what the first hours look like, what the first weeks look like, what the body does, where the work goes. This is a melancholy asset, but it is an asset.

### 6.7.7 The capacity to be wrong and continue

Documented across decades: the subject can be told he was wrong, can integrate it, and can keep working. He does not require the world to confirm his prior position. The Schism, the AvX aftermath, the post-Krakoa reckonings — in each case he has, after a period of metabolization, adjusted. This is rarer in his cohort than it should be. Many of his peers cannot lose an argument and remain in the room.

### 6.7.8 Pre-trauma residuals

This is speculative but evidentially supported. The subject's small ration of pre-catastrophe memory — flight with his father, his mother's voice, the brief unbroken childhood — appears to function as a thin but durable internal template of unbroken life. He knows, at some pre-verbal level, what a stable family felt like. This is more than many of his peers had. It is the seed from which the chosen-family pattern grows.

---

## 6.8 Material & Institutional Assets

### 6.8.1 The ruby-quartz infrastructure

Multiple sets of visors, lenses, civilian glasses, training pieces; the manufacturing knowledge to replace any of them; established supply lines; and (since Krakoa) a sovereign jurisdiction in which the materials are reliably available. The subject is not dependent on outside vendors for his own continued functioning. This was not always the case and was achieved deliberately.

### 6.8.2 Access

- **To Krakoan diplomatic and intelligence apparatus** at the highest level.
- **To Shi'ar contact** via Corsair, intermittent but real.
- **To temporal intelligence** via Cable, intermittent but real.
- **To psychic intelligence** via Emma and Jean, continuous.
- **To resurrection protocols**, which materially alters his risk calculus and frees him to take operational risks his prior selves could not.
- **To the broader Avengers and Fantastic Four communities**, frictional but extant.

### 6.8.3 Operational reputation

The name is a deterrent in itself. Sustained surveillance of opposition-force behavior shows measurable hesitancy when his presence on a field is confirmed. This saves engagements before they begin. It also recruits — both operators who want to work with him and assets who want to defect to him.

### 6.8.4 The body of documented work

Sixty years of public record. Doctrine he has authored or co-authored. Students he has trained. Operations he has led. This corpus is itself a resource — successors can study it, allies can rely on its consistency, and he himself can audit his prior decisions against current conditions.

---

## 6.9 The Synthesis (Why It Holds)

The pathology section of this file is accurate. It is also incomplete without this section, because the question a real intelligence file must answer is not *what is wrong with the subject* but *what permits the subject to continue functioning at this level under these conditions, and is that capacity stable?*

The answer is structural. The subject's defenses, his cognition, his somatic discipline, his chosen relationships, his named mission, his mastery of the literal trauma-symbol, and his material and institutional assets form a **mutually reinforcing scaffold** that converts what would, in a less fortunate constitution, be debilitating C-PTSD into sustained high-output functioning. Each element supports the others. Remove the mission and the defenses become brittle. Remove the partners and the cognition becomes unrelieved hypervigilance. Remove the somatic discipline and the affect-regulation strategy collapses. Remove the institutions and the duty-self has no object.

The scaffold is real. It is also load-bearing in a way that should concern any reader of this file: the subject is functional because of an architecture, not because of an underlying ease. The architecture has held for sixty years. The current configuration (Krakoa-era, late-life partnership, late-life regulation) is the strongest it has ever been.

He is, at this writing, **the most resilient he has ever been, by a margin that surprises even those who know him**, and the resilience is not residual luck. It is the cumulative dividend of a working lifetime spent — deliberately, patiently, and at great personal cost — turning a damaged child's only available materials into an instrument capable of holding a species up.

That is the asset. It is large. It should be in the file.


## Failure Modes & Decompensation

# FAILURE MODES & DECOMPENSATION
## Subject: Summers, Scott — UATU Intelligence File, Section 7

---

The subject does not break the way most operators break. He does not drink himself stupid, he does not disappear into a hotel room, he does not lose the thread of his sentences. His decompensation is, instead, a process of **progressive narrowing** — each stage of failure produces tighter control over a smaller domain, until the domain is a single decision and the control becomes total and catastrophic. The collapse is not a loss of function. It is a hyperfunction of a single function at the expense of every other.

What follows is the map of that narrowing — the staged escalation, the somatic and behavioral tells at each stage, the precipitants that produce each transition, and the terminal end-states the file has, on at least four separate occasions, watched him reach.

---

## 7.1 BASELINE — "Green" (Regulated Hypervigilance)

This is the subject's modal state and it should not be mistaken for health. It is C-PTSD in remission-by-function: the trauma is fully operational but the operational frame is intact.

**Affect.** Flat-to-warm in private, flat-to-cold in command, with a small repertoire of micro-expressions (a fractional softening at the mouth, a slow exhale through the nose) that intimates read accurately and strangers do not register at all.

**Somatic.** Resting heart rate low. Posture vertical, weight centered, shoulders held back about a quarter-inch further than comfortable — a postural habit dating to adolescence. Jaw lightly engaged at rest (the masseter is visibly developed on the left side; he clenches asymmetrically). Hands typically clasped behind the back or resting palm-down on a flat surface. Breath: nasal, 4-second inhale, 6-second exhale, audibly controlled when stressed and not audibly controlled at baseline — but the cadence is the same in both registers, which is the giveaway.

**Sleep.** Four to six hours, often broken at approximately 03:40 (the file has logged this hour across multiple eras; the significance is unknown to him and probably untraceable, but the consistency is striking). Returns to sleep approximately 40% of the time; otherwise rises, dresses fully, and works.

**Cognitive.** Trajectory-and-vector mode active. Continuously running threat models in background; can produce a contingency for any named scenario within seconds.

**Speech.** Measured. Mid-register baritone. Sentences complete. Does not interrupt; does not trail off. Will pause up to four seconds before answering a difficult question — the pause is not hesitation, it is search.

**Tells that he is still in Green and not deeper:** he initiates touch with intimates (a hand at Jean's elbow, the back of his fingers across Emma's wrist when crossing a room); he uses subordinates' first names; he permits himself one cup of coffee in the morning, which he drinks slowly and finishes.

---

## 7.2 STAGE ONE — "Amber" (Constriction)

**Precipitants.** A teammate injured under his command. An intelligence failure that did not cost lives but could have. A reminder of the orphanage or the plane (a particular quality of cold air; a child crying in a corridor; the specific timbre of a small-engine aircraft, which he will track auditorily through any conversation). News that Nathan is in danger in any era. Any mention of Sinister by name.

**Behavioral changes.**
