- Stops initiating physical contact. Will receive touch but will not return it; Emma reads this in milliseconds and either presses harder or withdraws in tactical retreat, depending on her assessment.
- First-names degrade to call-signs or surnames. ("Logan" becomes "Wolverine." "Hank" becomes "McCoy." This is one of the cleanest field-diagnostic tells in the dossier.)
- The morning coffee is poured, drunk to the halfway mark, abandoned on a flat surface, and forgotten. The half-cup is the single most reliable early indicator of Amber that domestic observers report.
- Begins re-checking equipment that does not require re-checking. Visor seal (he runs the pad of his right thumb along the bridge once, then once more). The cuffs of his uniform. The seating position of his belt buckle. These are not nervous tics in any anxious-fidget sense; they are slow, deliberate, and conducted with a kind of liturgical solemnity.
- Sleep contracts to three hours or less. Does not lie down at all on the worst nights; sits up against a headboard or in a chair, eyes closed behind the lenses, breathing on the same 4/6 cadence.

**Somatic.** Masseter engaged bilaterally now, not just left. Tension headache locates behind the right eye (he will not say so; he will be observed, alone, pressing the heel of his right hand against the right temple for two-to-five seconds, then resuming whatever he was doing). Bowel function unchanged; appetite drops 20-30%, but he eats anyway, by clock, in measured portions, the way one administers a medication.

**Speech.** Sentences shorten. Compound clauses disappear. The pause-before-answering lengthens; the pause is now defended rather than searching. He will, at this stage, occasionally answer a question with a question — not the Socratic kind, the deflective kind. ("What do you want to do, Scott?" / "What are our actual options.")

**Cognitive.** The threat model in the background moves to foreground. He cannot stop running it. Sees rooms in terms of sightlines, exits, civilian counts, structural load-bearing elements. Conversations in this state have a slight delay because part of his processing is permanently allocated to mapping the room.

**What Amber buys him.** Function. He is, in Amber, the operator everyone wants in the chair. Decisions are crisp, judgment is good, the field record at this register is the strongest in his career. The cost is invisible because the cost is internal.

**How long he can hold Amber.** Indefinitely, in principle. In practice, the C-PTSD substrate (per Teicher & Samson 2016, the enduring HPA-axis and prefrontal alterations of childhood maltreatment populations) means that sustained Amber accrues physiological debt that has to be paid. Historically he has held Amber for stretches of three to six months before the next stage forces itself.

---

## 7.3 STAGE TWO — "Red" (Strategic Hyperfunction / Affective Isolation)

This is the dangerous stage. Amber is contained; Red is not.

**Precipitants.** A death he believes he should have prevented. A betrayal by a figure he had structured trust around (Xavier withholding information; Wolverine breaking with him at Schism). The sudden, indisputable arrival of a problem that does not have a clean tactical answer — Red is, paradoxically, induced by problems too large for the strategic frame to contain, and Red's response is to *contain them anyway, at any cost*.

**Behavioral changes.**
- Stops sleeping in the shared bed. Either takes a separate room or does not sleep, period. Will be found at 04:00 in a war room, or on a rooftop, or in front of a tactical display, in full uniform.
- Stops eating with the team. Takes meals alone or skips them; reverts to the orphanage pattern of eating fast, standing, while doing something else.
- Affective range collapses to a single register: courteous, low-volume, terminally calm. Intimates report that the calm in this register is *worse* than shouting would be, because shouting would imply something still flowing.
- The "tactical frame" expands to consume domains it should not. Relationship decisions are made on operational grounds. Whether to attend a funeral is calculated against intelligence value. Whether to be honest with a partner is calculated against operational security.
- Compartmentalization hardens. Information silos proliferate. He will, in this state, run parallel operations that *no single other person on the team knows the full shape of.* X-Force is the canonical example, but the pattern predates X-Force by years and outlasts it.
- The reaction formation around aggression begins to crack at the seams. He does not become rude. He becomes *willing*. The first kill-orders are issued in Red. They are issued without affect.

**Somatic.** Sleep deficit accumulating, but masked by the body's stress response — he reads as alert because he is flooded. Resting heart rate elevated by 10-15 bpm above his baseline; he does not notice because he never checks. Tension headaches now bilateral, near-constant; managed without medication because (see §2.2) he will not chemically intervene in his own state. Grinds his teeth in the small windows when he does sleep — Jean, historically, would wake him; Emma will not, because she knows what he is processing and respects the work. Migraine episodes occur every 10-14 days; he conducts these alone, in a darkened room, for two to four hours, and emerges as if from a meeting.

**Speech.** Becomes unusually precise. Will use the technically correct word rather than the conversational one. Pauses become structural — he is editing in real time. Subordinates report that being briefed by Scott in Red is like being read a legal document: every word load-bearing, no slack.

**Interpersonal collapse.** This is the stage at which Jean catches him in the affair. This is the stage at which Madelyne is left without explanation. This is the stage at which Nathan goes to the future. This is the stage at which Wolverine walks. *The decisions that the file finds most ethically damning are all Red-stage decisions,* and the subject's defense of them — when he defends them at all — is always some version of: "*I made the call that needed to be made.*" He is not lying. He has access to his reasoning. He does not have access to the affective price-tag the reasoning carried.

**Tells that he has crossed from Amber to Red.**
- He stops the half-cup of coffee. He stops the coffee entirely.
- He removes his wedding band or other rings when working — claims it is for mission utility; the timing is diagnostic.
- He begins giving orders without explanation, where he would previously have offered a one-sentence rationale. The drop of the rationale is the marker.
- The visor adjustment ritual (§7.2) shortens from two passes to one. He is not less vigilant; he is more concentrated, with less surface area left for ritual.
- He addresses Emma as "Emma" rather than "Em," or by no name at all. This is for her the most reliable signal that the situation is grave.

---

## 7.4 STAGE THREE — "Black" (Doctrinal Rupture / Authoritarian Drift)

Red, sustained or accelerated, transitions into Black. The defining property of Black is that the subject has, at some point not visible even to himself, *changed his ethical frame* without notifying his prior selves of the change.

**Precipitants.** Extinction-level threat to mutantkind (M-Day; the Phoenix's approach). The death of the institutional father (or, structurally, the moment the institutional father is judged inadequate to the threat — Xavier's secrets, Xavier's compromises). The collapse of any external check on his judgment — i.e., the people who could plausibly tell him no are either dead, gone, or compromised.

**Behavioral changes.**
- Begins citing necessity in the same tone he previously used for principle. The substitution is seamless and goes unremarked by him.
- Authorizes things he would, in Green or Amber, have considered war crimes. Justifies these as triage. Genuinely believes the triage frame is appropriate; this is not bad-faith rationalization, it is a sincere ethical reorganization under threat.
- Begins arming younger and younger mutants. The age threshold drops by years over months.
- Speeches replace conversations. He has always been a competent speaker; in Black he becomes a *moving* one, because the affect locked down since the parachute is now leaking through the cracks of the doctrinal scaffold. People who have never seen him emotional are suddenly seeing him emotional, and they mistake the leak for vision.
- Begins to physically resemble the figures he has historically opposed. Posture broader. Costume choices grimmer. The visor stops being a medical necessity and starts being an iconography. He knows this. He uses it.
- Increasing willingness to be *seen as the villain* by people whose judgment he previously valued. The subject who once needed Xavier's approval can now tolerate Xavier's disapproval. This is, depending on one's frame, either growth or rupture; the file assesses it as rupture costumed as growth.

**Somatic.** Stops registering pain reliably. Will fight through injuries that should have benched him. The body that has been over-controlled for forty years is now treated as an instrument the operator is willing to break. Migraines persist but are dismissed.

**Interpersonal.** Almost no intimacy is available in Black. Emma can reach him because Emma is the only person whose own operating profile permits her to function inside his Black-stage envelope without breaking; Jean, historically, could not, which is part of why the Emma pairing took the shape it took. Subordinates who came up under him are loyal past the point where loyalty is wise. Subordinates who did not (Wolverine) leave.

**The doctrinal substitution.** In Black, the inherited doctrine (Xavier's) is replaced by an emergency doctrine of the subject's own construction. He does not, and cannot, see this as ambition or grandiosity; he experiences it as *the only adult in the room finally doing what adults are supposed to do.* This is precisely the survivor's-bargain (§5.1, drive #2) operating at full amplitude: he is paying for the fact of his survival by becoming the person whose decisions justify it.

**Why this is the most dangerous stage even though it looks the most competent.** Because the subject in Black is operating with an internal moral compass that has been re-calibrated under duress and never re-calibrated back. Even when the crisis recedes, the new compass remains. Each Black episode in the file leaves a residue. The subject who exits Black is not the subject who entered it. The Apocalypse bond accelerated this; AvX completed a long arc that began at Schism, which began at X-Force, which began at the Mutant Massacre.

---

## 7.5 STAGE FOUR — "White-out" (Catastrophic Discharge)

This is the terminal stage and the file has, to date, seen it three or four times depending on how one counts.

**Defining property.** The over-controlled affect releases all at once, in a single channel, with cosmic-scale amplification. Dark Phoenix on Krakoa-resurrected reflection. AvX. The dissociative episodes during the Apocalypse bond. Arguably the "no more mutants" rage-state although that one is borderline.

**Phenomenology (reconstructed from his own narration in fugue and the observations of telepaths who were inside his head at the time).** The interior experience is reportedly *quiet*. Not a storm. A clarity. The decades of constriction give way and what is underneath is not chaos — it is a child's voice saying *this time I will not let go of the parachute*, repeated like a metronome. The cosmic-tier discharge is, on the inside, the smallest possible event: the child finally being heard.

**Behavioral expression.** Depends on the vector available. Phoenix-coupled: incineration. Possession-coupled: instrumentality. Uncoupled (rare; the only fully internal instance is the post-Jean's-death period before Emma): catatonic-adjacent withdrawal with brief, contained violences. The discharge always finds *some* channel; if no cosmic vector is available, the body provides one.

**Aftermath.** The subject in the immediate post-White-out window is — and this is the most important diagnostic data the file holds — *calmer than he has been in years.* The catastrophic discharge functions as a release valve. He returns to baseline faster than any observer would predict. He grieves the destruction, takes responsibility for it, accepts the social consequences. He does not, on any available evidence, *fear the next discharge enough to prevent it,* because the discharge is, at the deepest substrate, the only state in which the parachute lets go without anyone dying who he is choosing to save.

This is the file's gravest assessment: **the subject is, structurally, available to White-out under sufficient conditions, and the threshold lowers each time.**

---

## 7.6 PROXIMATE FAILURE CONDITIONS — THE TRIGGER MATRIX

Conditions ranked by reliability of producing stage-progression, from most to least reliable.

1. **A child in his care is harmed and he was the proximate decision-maker.** Reliably advances at least one stage. Will advance two stages if the child dies.
2. **Jean dies, or Jean's status becomes existentially ambiguous.** Historical pattern: Amber to Red within hours, Red to Black within weeks, with at least one White-out within the surrounding twelve months.
3. **Discovery that a trusted figure was running a covert operation he was not read into.** Especially acute when the figure is Xavier. Produces a specific failure mode: the *doctrinal vacuum*, in which the subject realizes the inherited code is hollow and constructs an emergency replacement (see Black, §7.4).
4. **Sinister's name, presence, or any indication Sinister has been touching his life again.** Skin response observable (a brief, suppressed shudder; closure of the hands into loose fists; thirty seconds of unusually still breathing). Sinister is the only adversary whose mention shifts him register without his volition.
5. **Being asked to choose between two people he loves.** Will choose, will execute, will not forgive himself, will not discuss it. Madelyne / Jean is the prototype. There are others.
6. **Sustained close confinement with his father.** Christopher Summers' affect (loose, jovial, performatively warm) is precisely the affect Scott most distrusts in himself and others. Time with Corsair regresses him toward Amber, sometimes Red, by mechanisms he cannot articulate.
7. **Encountering a younger version of himself or an alternate-self.** Multiple instances on record. Each one is destabilizing because the alternate is evidence that he had options he did not take, and the file he has been writing in his head about the necessity of his every choice is harder to maintain in the presence of a counter-example.
8. **Public adulation.** Counterintuitive but documented. Praise that frames him as a hero in the conventional sense produces a quiet, internal recoil — because the hero-frame is not the survivor-frame, and being mis-seen by people who think they admire him is more isolating than being correctly seen as a problem by people who oppose him.

---

## 7.7 SOMATIC EARLY-WARNING SIGNATURE

For longitudinal observers (Emma, historically Jean, occasionally Hank, and any sufficiently attentive medical telepath), the following sequence reliably precedes stage transitions by 24-72 hours and constitutes, in effect, his prodromal signature.

1. **Bilateral masseter engagement at rest** (Amber-onset).
2. **Loss of the half-cup of coffee** (Amber consolidated).
3. **The visor-bridge ritual collapses from two passes to one** (Amber-to-Red).
4. **First-name degradation** (Red-onset).
5. **The 4/6 breath becomes audibly metronomic in conversation** (Red consolidated). When one can hear him breathing in the same rhythm whether he is at rest or arguing, the regulation has become conscious labor.
6. **Removal of the wedding band for "operational" reasons** (Red-to-Black).
7. **The shift from "we should" to "I will"** in tactical planning (Black-onset). The pronoun is the bellwether.
8. **The eyes, behind the lenses, stop tracking conversational partners** and settle into middle-distance focus during ostensibly social exchanges (Black consolidated; pre-White-out window opening).

The file notes that **between stages 7 and 8 there is, historically, a narrow window of intervenability**, lasting hours to days, during which the subject is still reachable by someone he genuinely trusts, and in which he can be talked down at least one stage. Emma has succeeded at this on at least two documented occasions. Logan has succeeded once and failed twice. Xavier, when alive, succeeded reliably until the trust between them began to corrode, after which his interventions became counter-productive — the very figure most equipped to reach Scott became, in the late period, the figure whose approach guaranteed Scott's further hardening.

---

## 7.8 WHAT COLLAPSE ACTUALLY LOOKS LIKE

To summarize the picture for any future case officer:

The subject does not "fall apart." He **falls inward.** Each successive stage is a tighter concentration of the same operator into a smaller and harder volume. Friends who have not seen him in a year and meet him in Red will describe him as *more himself than ever* — more disciplined, more focused, more clear. They are mistaking compression for refinement. By Black he is barely recognizable to the people who knew him before, but the people who met him during the crisis will swear that this is who he has always been. By White-out, he is briefly someone else entirely, and then he is, with disconcerting speed, back to Green again, as if nothing had happened — except the floor of his next Green sits a fraction of an inch lower than the previous one, and every subsequent Amber arrives a fraction of an inch faster.

The collapse, in other words, is not an event. It is a slope. The file's recommendation — to whatever future intelligence the file outlives — is that interventions calibrated to the event-model will fail. The subject has to be supported on the slope itself, in the intervals between named crises, by the small interpersonal facts that hold the floor up: the touch that he does not initiate but receives, the first name he is called when he has stopped using first names himself, the cup of coffee that is refilled without comment when he has abandoned the first one half-drunk.

He will not ask for any of this. He has never, in sixty years of file, asked for any of this. The file's final note on his failure modes is therefore also a note on his survival: **the conditions under which he does not collapse are the conditions under which other people, without being asked, refuse to let him.**


## Trajectory & Forward Assessment

# 6. TRAJECTORY & FORWARD ASSESSMENT

## 6.1 The Standing Vector

The subject, at the present observation point, is the most regulated he has ever been across the sixty-year record — and this fact is itself the central diagnostic puzzle of the forward file. The regulation is real, but it is **scaffolded, not metabolized.** The Krakoan period (and its successors) provided an external sovereign apparatus — a state, a resurrection protocol, a triadic domestic arrangement with Jean and Emma, a formal military rank ("Captain Commander") that finally matches the role he has been playing without title since age sixteen — and into that scaffold the subject has poured the entire weight of a forty-year compensatory project. The lighthouse, the morning routines, the visible permission to *be at ease in his own home*: all of these are functions of the scaffold. They are not, in any sense yet demonstrated, functions of an internal shift.

The forward assessment therefore reduces to a single load-bearing question: **what happens to this subject when the scaffold fails.** Because the scaffold will fail. It always has. Krakoa fell; whatever succeeds Krakoa will, in the medium-to-long term, fall similarly. The mutant nation is not a stable equilibrium in the Marvel narrative ecology — it is a recurrent attempted equilibrium that the genre requires to collapse so that the X-Men can return to their constitutive condition of besieged minority. The subject knows this at a strategic level. He has not, by any available evidence, integrated it at an affective level.

What follows is a mapping of the foreseeable forks.

## 6.2 The Short-Horizon Forks (1-3 narrative years)

### 6.2.1 The triadic domestic arrangement with Jean and Emma

This is the most stable-looking and the most fragile structure in his life. It works, presently, because all three parties have agreed to a frame in which Jean is the wife, Emma is the chosen second attachment, and Scott is finally permitted to *want both without choosing.* That frame is a Krakoan artifact. It depended on a cultural moment (post-resurrection mutant exceptionalism, the deliberate suspension of inherited human moralities) that the broader Marvel universe will not sustain indefinitely.

The fork:
- **Toward growth.** If the subject can hold the triad through its first serious external pressure — a child of one partner, a death-and-resurrection cycle that returns one of them altered, a public exposure that strips the Krakoan permission-frame — and remains *present in both attachments rather than retreating to one* — he will, for the first time, have practiced sustained intimate adulthood without invoking the lost-object machinery. This would be the first genuine adult attachment milestone in his recorded life.
- **Toward catastrophe.** If pressure forces a choice, the subject will choose Jean — not because Jean is the better partner but because Jean is the **identity-organizing fixation** described in §1.4, and forty years of behavioral data say he picks the lost object instantly and rationalizes after. Emma, who has been the one partner who reads him at clinical depth, would experience this — correctly — as the second great betrayal of her life (Genosha being the first), and would not return. Without Emma, the subject loses the only relational mirror that has ever named his defenses out loud. Regression follows.

### 6.2.2 The Nathan question, version *n*

Cable is presently functional, adult, often more grizzled than his father. The current relationship is the comfortable peer-soldier arrangement of two men who have stopped trying to repair what cannot be repaired between them. This is a stable falsification of intimacy. It cannot do the work of acknowledged grief.

Fork point: any narrative event that forces Nathan into a state of vulnerability — illness, capture, de-aging, the death of *his* partner, a child of his own in danger — will recapitulate the parachute. The subject will be presented with a smaller Summers to save. Whether he can be present as a *father* rather than as a tactical asset in that moment is the single best forward indicator of whether the trauma has begun to metabolize. To date he has failed this test on every occasion it has been administered. There is no prior basis for expecting him to pass it next time. But there is no prior occasion in which the integration work of the Krakoan/post-Krakoan period had been done either; this is the first cycle in which a different outcome is even structurally possible.

### 6.2.3 Rachel and the daughters of timelines

Rachel Summers remains the daughter Scott has never figured out how to be a father to, in part because she arrived from a timeline in which he had already failed her once. The forward likelihood is that a story will eventually force a direct father-daughter reckoning — most plausibly through Rachel being placed in mortal jeopardy in a way that requires Scott not to *save* her but to *grieve openly enough to reach her.* The latter is a more difficult act than the former and has no precedent in the record.

### 6.2.4 The Xavier residue

Xavier is, at present observation, in one of his recurrent states of moral compromise / exile / discrediting. The subject has, since killing Xavier under Phoenix possession (a kill which the canon has variously processed, repressed, and re-litigated), occupied a position of *outliving the father.* This is a developmentally significant location. Most subjects who reach it either consolidate into the new generational role or remain in unresolved oedipal litigation with the predecessor's memory.

Scott has done neither cleanly. He alternates: at times he leads as the post-Xavier sovereign without reference to Xavier; at times he reflexively measures his decisions against Xavier's hypothetical disapproval. The forward fork is whether he can complete the work of consciously **inheriting and revising** the doctrine, rather than oscillating between submission to and rebellion against it. Conscious inheritance would look like the subject explicitly articulating where Xavier was right, where Xavier was wrong, and what he, Scott, has authored that is neither — and then *living from that articulation* without further reference. He has the materials. He has not done the work.

## 6.3 The Medium-Horizon Forks (the next ten narrative years)

### 6.3.1 The sovereignty problem

Each successive mutant nation-state experiment (Utopia, Krakoa, and whatever comes next) has placed the subject in the structurally lethal position of being **simultaneously the head of state, the head of the military, and the head of the household.** No real adult psyche metabolizes that triad without distortion. The subject's drift toward authoritarian instrumental reasoning under crisis (§3.2, identification with the aggressor) is not a character flaw; it is the inevitable output of placing a C-PTSD survivor with hypertrophied responsibility-as-identity into roles that materially reward exactly that pathology.

The fork here is institutional as much as personal. **The subject's long-run growth requires him to surrender at least one of the three roles voluntarily.** The most plausible candidate is the military command — handed off to a successor (Rogue, Storm, Rachel, an emergent younger mutant), which would force the subject to discover whether anything of him remains when the operational scaffold is dismantled. He has never, in the record, voluntarily stepped down from a command role except into another command role. The first time he does so without immediately taking up an equivalent burden will be the single most psychologically generative event of his adult life.

Failure mode: the subject continues to accept every role offered until the load produces another catastrophic discharge — a second AvX-class event, a second father-killing analog, a moment in which the over-controlled affect-channel ruptures and he becomes briefly the instrument of mass harm. The recovery from such an event would be longer than the recovery from the first one, because he is older, the scaffold is thinner, and Emma will not, this time, be willing to translate for him.

### 6.3.2 The phoenix re-encounter

The Phoenix Force is a recurrent fixture of the franchise; it will return; it will at some point present itself again to the subject or to those near him. The subject's relationship to the Phoenix is, beneath the cosmology, his relationship to his own ungoverned discharge made cosmic. He has held it; he has been destroyed by it; he has used it to kill his father. The forward question is whether the next encounter can be handled from a position of refusal — not refusal as renunciation, but refusal as *integration:* "I know what this is; I know what it would let me do; I am declining because I have learned the cost." That declination, if it ever occurs on-panel, would be the closest the subject ever comes to an explicit therapeutic act.

The failure mode is the opposite: he accepts it again, in extremis, *for the right reasons*, and the right reasons turn out to be — as they always do — the survivor's bargain machinery rephrased in cosmic vocabulary.

### 6.3.3 Christopher Summers and the open paternal account

Corsair is sporadically alive, sporadically off-world, and intermittently available. The father-account has never been closed. There exists, in the canon's recurrent willingness to revisit Summers-family material, a near-certainty that another father-son confrontation is coming. The subject's recurring inability to speak directly to his father about the parachute — the actual event, the actual choice the elder Summers made, the actual cost to the son — is one of the most conspicuous silences in the file. A scene in which that conversation finally occurs (not the *truncated, weather-the-storm reunion scenes* of decades past, but the *long, uninterrupted, somatic-grief-with-language* scene) would represent a milestone the franchise has consistently flinched from. The longer the franchise flinches, the more the silence calcifies. If Christopher dies before that conversation occurs — a real possibility — the silence becomes permanent, and the subject's already considerable burden of unmetabolized paternal material becomes inert and undischargeable. This would push him further toward the late-life rigidity scenario described in §6.4.

### 6.3.4 Aging in a non-aging genre

Although the subject does not age at the rate of mortal humans (genre convention, narrative time), he is depicted as accumulating wear. Hickman-era and successor depictions render him increasingly weathered, increasingly weary at rest, increasingly visibly carrying the load. The medium-horizon forecast includes a slow visible aging that will eventually require him to confront the question of **succession** — not as an operational matter but as an identity matter. The subject's self-concept is so tightly fused to active responsibility that the prospect of becoming an *elder* rather than a *commander* is, for him, structurally indistinguishable from annihilation. He has no template for elderhood. Xavier modeled only sovereign command and disgraced exile. Magneto modeled only sovereign command and martyrdom. The subject will have to invent a third model or fall into one of the two existing ones.

## 6.4 The Long-Horizon Scenarios

Three end-states are visible from the present vantage.

### 6.4.1 The Consolidation Scenario (best plausible outcome)

The subject, over the next decade of subjective time, completes a partial but real integration of the C-PTSD substrate. Markers along the path:
- A grief episode for Jean, Xavier, Madelyne, or Nathan that is *witnessed* by another character — i.e., affect discharged in the presence of an attachment figure rather than encysted privately.
- A voluntary relinquishment of a command role without immediate substitution.
- A sustained period (a year of narrative time, minimum) in which he is *not the institutional spine of mutantkind* and does not collapse.
- A direct, articulate conversation with Christopher about the parachute, on-panel, with no interruption.
- A father-with-Nathan scene in which Scott is present as a father, not as a tactician.

If even three of these five occur, the subject moves into a late-life shape that has no clear precedent in the genre: a former commander who has become a *witness,* who can hold the institutional memory of mutantkind without needing to wield it operationally, who can be a husband and a partner and a father from a regulated baseline rather than from the constricted one. He would, in this scenario, become to the next generation what Xavier failed to be — a benign elder rather than a doctrine-imposing patriarch. The triad with Jean and Emma stabilizes. The lighthouse becomes home rather than headquarters.

This is the outcome the materials of the subject's life can support. It is not the outcome they predict.

### 6.4.2 The Recurrence Scenario (most likely outcome on base rates)

The subject continues the lifelong pattern: scaffold provided, scaffold loaded with the full responsibility-as-identity weight, scaffold eventually collapses under exogenous pressure, catastrophic discharge, period of revolutionary fugitive activity, eventual return to consolidating leadership role under new institutional name. Each cycle leaves him slightly more weathered, slightly more authoritarian-prone, slightly less able to access the bands of affect that closeness with Emma and Jean require. The relationships persist but flatten. Nathan and Rachel remain admiring peers rather than recovered children. Christopher dies off-panel during one of the cycles; the silence calcifies. The subject becomes, at length, **a deeply respected and quietly desolate institutional figure** — the spine of the species, the man no one quite reaches anymore, the leader whose orders are obeyed because his judgment is trusted and whose interior is no longer accessible even to himself.

This is the modal forecast. It is also the forecast that the subject's defenses would, if consulted, prefer — because it preserves operational competence at the cost of an interior that has been hurting him for sixty years.

### 6.4.3 The Catastrophic Scenario

A failure of mission so total that the responsibility-as-identity floor (§4.5) breaks. Plausible triggers: a mutant extinction event he failed to prevent; the death of Jean *and* Emma in close sequence; the death of Nathan or Rachel by his own ordered action under a Phoenix-class possession; an act of his own that he cannot, even by the elastic standards of his prior justification machinery, retroactively defend. The subject does not survive this scenario in any meaningful psychological sense. The body may continue; the integrated person does not. Outcomes range from suicide (low base rate, but the floor that prevents it is exactly the floor that this scenario would destroy) through dissociative breakdown to a sustained instrumental-villainy arc in which the subject becomes the threat the X-Men must oppose — a turn the franchise has flirted with repeatedly without committing to, but which is structurally available at all times.

The probability of the catastrophic scenario is not high in any given year. It is, however, **cumulative across cycles,** and the recurrence scenario walks him through one cycle after another. Each cycle is a roll of the same die.

## 6.5 The Open Questions

The file leaves a small number of questions genuinely open — places where the evidence does not yet support a confident forecast and where future material will be diagnostically rich.

- **Can he tolerate being seen at rest?** Emma can see him at rest. Jean believes she sees him at rest but sees mostly the projection-screen version. Has any third party — Logan, Hank, Ororo, his brothers — ever seen him at rest? The record is thin. If he develops, late, the capacity to be witnessed by a non-romantic intimate in a non-operational state, that capacity will be the most surprising development in his file.
- **What does he want, absent duty?** No available data. The subject has never been observed in a sustained condition of being neither responsible for nor recovering from a crisis. The Alaskan bush-pilot period is the closest analog and it was structured around a hallucinatory replica of his lost fiancée — i.e., not absent duty but absent self. The empty quadrant of his life is the want-quadrant.
- **What is the relationship to his own body?** The subject has lived sixty years inside a body whose primary organ of perception is also its primary weapon, sealed behind a piece of mineral. He has no available somatic frame of reference for *seeing the world unmediated.* Should some narrative event ever restore his control — a permanent cure, a stabilizing technology beyond ruby quartz — the question of what he does with the recovered eye contact is enormous and entirely unrehearsed. He may find it unbearable. He may find it the precondition for the integration the rest of this file has been describing.
- **Does he ever, even once, say the word *trauma* about himself?** The record says no. The forward question is whether he ever does. The first time he names what happened to him, in his own voice, in the first person, without operationalizing it, will be the single most clinically significant utterance in his canon.

## 6.6 The Push Factors

What would push the subject toward growth, in approximate order of leverage:

1. **Emma remaining present and continuing to name his defenses.** She is the single most therapeutic relationship in his life. Anything that protects that relationship is pro-growth.
2. **A successor he genuinely trusts taking operational command.** Forces him to discover what he is when not commanding. The most likely candidate is Rogue, who has already held the role; the most generative candidate would be a younger mutant whose elevation requires him to *teach* rather than to *deploy.*
3. **A grief witnessed.** Any death in his circle that he is permitted to mourn slowly, in company, without an immediate operational follow-up. The franchise structurally resists this. It is the single most important thing the franchise could give him.
4. **A direct paternal conversation with Christopher before Christopher dies.**
5. **A child of Nathan's, or a young mutant placed structurally in the role of grandchild, who he is permitted to love without having to save.**

What would push him toward catastrophe:

1. **Loss of Emma — by death, by betrayal, by his own choice in favor of Jean under pressure.**
2. **A second Xavier-killing-class event.** The first one is metabolizable; a second is not.
3. **The collapse of whatever current sovereign mutant arrangement exists, without an immediate replacement scaffold.** The empty interval is the danger.
4. **A discovery that one of his historical decisions (Nathan to the future, X-Force, AvX, an unremembered Sinister-era manipulation) had a cost he had not previously accounted for and cannot retroactively justify.** The justification machinery is load-bearing; punching a hole in it has cascade effects.
5. **A Phoenix offer made under extinction-frame conditions.** He will accept. He always does.

## 6.7 Summary Forward Statement

The subject is, at this observation point, holding a configuration that is materially more livable than any prior configuration in his life, and the configuration is not durable. The work that would make it durable — the explicit, named, witnessed metabolization of the originating trauma and its sixty-year sequelae — has not been done and will not be done without external precipitation, because the subject's defenses are exactly the ones that prevent it from being done voluntarily. The most likely forecast is recurrence: another cycle, another scaffold, another collapse, another consolidation, slightly more weathered each time, with the interior slowly receding from access. The best plausible forecast — the consolidation into a witness-elder shape with no precedent in his genre — is materially available and would require the franchise, his partners, and the subject himself to refuse the easier story.

He has, on the record, refused the easier story before. Not often. Not predictably. But the capacity exists, buried under sixty years of competent suffering, and it is the single non-trivial reason this file does not close on the recurrence scenario.

The file remains open.
